As a food  lover I was highly  disappointed with the service at Buddakan. The food was good but didn't match it price tag what so ever. The appetizers served so fast that my GF and I didn't even had the time to enjoy the wine. There was a 15 min gap between the first and the second entree, when I asked the waiter why does it takes so long he came out with a lame excuse..."the restaurant is too big"... why should I care...?At the end of the dinner (45 min after we came in- world record) we spoke with the manager and told him about the service and the waiter and he decided to solve it by saying: "I will talk to him, so sorry". I was shocked, but based on their reaction its seems like they used to such a criticism from client but they just don't give a shit. Never coming back, there are way too many good restaurant in NY that I would prefer to spend my money at...

It's Buddakan........chill vibe as soon as you walk in the door(if you don't walk right by it the first time) as you're greeted by a desk that resembles hotel check in.  The host/ess will probably ask you to go have a drink at the bar while "you're table is prepared".........don't fight it, just go grab your $18 cocktail and enjoy the decour.Once seated, enjoy as even though it has lost a little something since it first opened it is still an enjoyable night with an attentive staff.  Order a variety of dishes to share and get a main dish for yourself.  Pay your $500 bill(give or take) for 4 and enjoy strolling out into Meatpacking with a nice meal to soak up the alcohol you'll undoubtedly consume throughout the rest of the night.If you have visitors from out of town, take em here just for a drink.  You'll def get that WOW factor if they've never been.***Wheelchairs - Make sure you have a strong friend to help you up the 4 or so steps upon entry.  Buy him a drink and he'll be the one thanking you***
Buddakan is Asian fusion done well; there is none of that P.F. Chang's nonsense to be found here.Start with the edamame dumplings; the white truffle oil in there gives it a nice taste. For for short ribs, black pepper beef, lamb chops, pork belly, sausage fried rice and the lobster fried rice. The food comes for family style dining, and each one delicious and keeps you wondering what the next one will be. The presentation of the food is also quite beautiful.The cocktail menu is not bad, and I've always enjoyed the Solid (a bourbon concoction). You might not get full if you have a larger appetite, but it's a good place to sit and chat with old and new friends.
Attention fellow Celiacs: I know this place doesn't have a designated Gluten-free menu, but they are extremely accommodating. I booked a reservation on OpenTable, and gave them a heads up about my condition, and the waiter was extraordinarily helpful with regards to pointing me toward dishes that they could make gluten free. Oh, and the food was absolutely delicious, and the place is beautiful. Things got a bit slow, but that was because so many diners were there and the restaurant is so big. The place was packed. Also, if you don't want to take your time enjoying company and food, don't go out to eat. I would love to come back.

You go to Buddakan more for ambiance than for consistent cuisine. The food is good, albeit pricey for what it is. What are you getting? Asian "fusion" in it's prime. But consistency is where this restaurant sorely lacks. I've been over ten times (this resto is big with the out of towners) and can say I've always returned one item or been disappointed by a couple of plates. The way it works is you order several plates, family style and share. Avoid the duck at all costs, better duck can be eaten in Chinatown. "Fancy" Buddakan duck is sorely lacking (in flavor and flare). The dumplings are delicious (but again see Chinatown for delicious, cheap dumplings). The service is usually stellar and they were more than willing to accommodate when I've returned items for being over-seasoned or salty or even just bad. The people are beautiful, the cocktails are delicious. You go to see and be seen (and maybe a bit in between). #unintentionalrhymeskills
Great if you are a tourist or fresh out of college. Not great if you are a local, have standards for service, and recognize there are better places in New York.The food and ambiance were good, but I can't say the same about our server, Erik (I think that's his name). I came here for a birthday party on 12/5 with a party of 10. First, the staff was very accommodating even though a few people in our party were late (they won't seat you until your entire party is there). Second, the food was very good- I highly recommend the edamame dumplings, the chili rock shrimp, the mongolian lamb chops, and the tea smoked beef. The meat was really tender, and each dish was unique from the other, as opposed to some asian places where everything tastes like a variation of the same thing. The cocktails were forgettable, however.To start, we ordered 6 appetizers, 4 entrees, and two noodle/rice dishes and asked to keep a menu so we could order more. Erik had so MUCH attitude about this. He said, just so you know, that is only 4 entrees, and you have 10 people. Yes, thank you, I have a postgraduate degree and can do basic math. I really hate it when you order to share at a FAMILY STYLE restaurant and servers get annoyed that you are not ordering an appetizer/ entree per person. So, whatever, we continued to enjoy our meal. I had told Erik that it was my sister's birthday, thinking that, you know like any other place, they would bring out a dessert with a candle in it or something. At the end of the meal, he asked us if we wanted dessert, and no one was into it. And then...he brought us our check. He either completely forgot about the birthday, or was just pissed because we did not order the 1:1:1 ratio. At that point I just wanted to get out there. When our bill came, gratuity was added automatically. Apparently Buddhakan has not gotten the memo that it is now illegal to add gratuity to a bill automatically in New York. Disgusted, I paid (minus the "additional gratuity" they ask for on top of the automatically added 18%). It was surprisingly cheap- $50 a person total, including paying for the birthday girl, but still not worth it to me.
Buddakan is a really fun place to come. A big, loud restaurant, Buddakan screams style and success. We came here with a group of 8, and everyone had a blast. They have a huge staircase that takes you downstairs where they have additional seating. But the huge staircase means that the ceilings are really high, at least in part of the space, which I love. We all ordered cocktails (tasty!) and lots of dishes to share. The Dim Sum is great! We had the edamame dumplings, jade shrimp dumplings, boneless spare ribs and steamed bass roll. We also shared the tea smoked pepper beef, lobster fried rice, glazed alaskan black cod and sweet and crispy jumbo shrimp. All excellent! A pricey evening, so make it count for special occasions!
I was skeptical.  Very skeptical of the trendy curse.  You know, the curse where it's uuber hot on the inside...but the food makes you say "meh."Well, Buddakan somehow has missed the dreaded curse.  All the rumours about the ambience and decor are true, one star for you Buddakahn.  The drinks are amazing, another star.  The service and friendliness of the staff are impeccable, another star.  Food....oh, how can I describe the food without droning??  Well, I've eaten all over the world in many, many fine dining establishments...and Buddakan is hands down one of the best.  Boy, you're really racking up the stars from me.  Finally, the price.  Ahhh yes, the price.  I feel like for everything we experienced, it was a runaway bargain.  For two people with 4 drinks, an appetizer sampler, fried rice, and two entrees=$150.  We left stuffed, happy, and entertained.  Next time we're in your hood Buddakan, we WILL meet again for a rematch.

I came here on a Saturday night with a handful of girlfriends and I was immediately blown away at the hip ambiance and decor. The space is over-the-top huge and is decked out with exaggerated touches like larger than life chandeliers and electric-colored grates, all while sexy house music plays in the background as the score.The service was amazing and our waiter, Paul, was super knowledgeable and passionate about the must-haves on the menu, candidly sharing his opinions about what his favorite dishes were.  All in all, Paul was not only friendly and witty, but he was oh-so-attentive and made sure that my party was well taken care of.  As for the food, the edamame dumplings and the tuna tartare spring rolls were to die for!!  Everything came out very timely and was plated meticulously.  What's more, the cocktails were oh-so-tasty -- and boy did they pack a punch!!  Dessert served to polish off the meal perfectly, though in retrospect, I could've gone without having those few extra calorie-ladden bites of heaven.
Great ambiance, decor and terrific service. With the trance exotic music blasting in the background, this is a great place for friends and after work hang out. Definitely not for family occasions. If you come here with the expectation of dining in an expensive authentic Chinese restaurant, this is not the right place to spend your big bucks at because what you are getting are fusion Chinese dishes.I left Buddakan with a curious and lingering afterthought, the food does not possess great Chinese flavor, some no flavor at all, but the execution of the food is good. Should I rate this based on Chinese foods that I've grown accustomed to or separate ratings with the Asian fusions, overall execution of food or flavor?We ordered based on our favorite Chinese dishes and the recommended meal per Yelp-ers reviews:(Appetizer) Chili Rock Shrimp 4/5Its a spicier version (probably Sriracha Sauce) of Honey Walnut Shrimp minus the sweetness. Its an inspired combo of crunch and creaminess which pops in the mouth like malt. Were it a tad sweeter it would have been perfect for my taste bud. (Appetizer) Steamed Sea Bass 4/5 Closer to its authentic Cantonese Steamed Fish. Probably my favorite meal of the night. Topped with generous helpings of sliced scallions and ginger. The ginger was amazing as it was deprived of its strong ginger flavor and was sweet. The fish was soft as butter and the flavor was top notch and well balanced. Short Ribs 2/5Soft and tender. Served on a bed of flat rice noodle (Shahe Fen or Kway Teow depending in which part of the world you're at). Flavorless. Ma Po Tofu 3/5Unlike your Szechuan-ese  Ma Po Tofu with different layer of spicy flavor coming at you at waves, this was sweet and acidic. Which was not bad. The tofu was cut perfectly into bite size pieces and have great texture. Leaves me wondering if this would make a great topping for a noodle dish. Stir Fry Green Veggies 3/5 Legumes in stir fry are good for texture. Crunchy and savory. I liked it.Lobster Fried Rice 3/5 I'm usually a sucker for good fried rice, but this is way overrated by Yelp-ers. I'm giving it a generous 3 cause I'm too kind for these sort of comfort food. Just standard fried rice with expensive ingredient. Would I come back for its expensive meals? Not by my choice; if I did, its not for the food but for the great hang out atmosphere. But what an expensive hang out place.
It was my first time dining at Buddakan, and I was quite impressed with the whole experience. First of all, I'm allergic to gluten.  (We're not talking fad "allergic;" we're talking sick-for-days allergic to wheat and its grainy cousins.)  Our server, Corey, did an awesome job of guiding me through what was/wasn't safe for me to eat on the family-style tasting menu (Tasting Menu 2).  In cases where the tasting menu items weren't going to work, he offered up great gluten free alternatives that were absolutely delicious, like the Spicy Yellowtail Yu Sheng: paper thin slices of some of the best yellowfin I've ever tasted with just a hint of pineapple and sweet chili.Other big winners of the evening were the lobster fried rice, which had big, buttery chunks of lobster, and the Sweet  Crunchy Jumbo Shrimp, which completely lived up to their name.The atmosphere is chic and trendy, but not stuffy.  The decor is oddly elegant in a gothic castle-meets-ancient Buddhist temple kind of way; massive chandeliers and wax-covered candelabras commingle with abstract wood-cut dividers and Asian accents.All in all, the tasty food, unique atmosphere, and great, attentive service made it a memorable evening.  I plan to be back for seconds.

It's alright.I'm a sucker for the environment.  It was a very dark and mysterious place that widened my pupils, gave me a happy tingle in my stomach, and made me feel like the smoothest s.o.b. who was about to throw down some serious cash in genghis khan's new york loft.  The art, lighting, furniture, structure, everything in the joint was incredible and beautiful.  I was really hoping that the food was as magic as the space between the restaurant's walls.I raised my first eyebrow after I had requested a plate of spring rolls with chicken only.  (The only spring rolls on the menu have a chicken/seafood mixture).  He said he couldn't do that, because the chicken and seafood was pre-mixed.  Naturally, we asked for only vegetable spring rolls instead.  He said he couldn't do that either because everything was already pre-frozen.  I thought to myself why a place that seemed so classy wasn't using fresh ingredients.  I raised my second eyebrow.After my eyebrows got tired, I put them down and chose something else out of complete forgiveness and faith.We ordered some stir fry vegetables, beef, chicken and rice.  Everything was prepared beautifully, but everything tasted so bland and mediocre.  The beef was in need of some serious flavor.  The chicken was flavorful, but not anything out of the ordinary.  The vegetables were vegetables, and the rice never came to our table.We spent about $100 for two, and I'm happy we gave it a try.  Despite the food, I enjoyed a romantic evening with my wife.If I ever came back, I would prefer to hang out in the bar lounge and have drinks there instead of dinner.  Sorry Sex and the City movie fans if I ruined your girls night out.

It's a good Asian fusion restaurant, but there are better Buddakan's elsewhere. I went with a group of (3 others.. 4 total). Here's what I think:I must say that out of the Buddakan's in the Tri-State area, this is my least favorite. Because we're talking about New York City, the portions are small and the food costs much more. Expect to pay around $40 to $50 per person for a complete meal. Some things we ended up getting:Appetizer:- Crispy Calamari Salad - Staple at ANY Buddakan Restaurant. The crispy squid is complemented with a vinaigrette dressing and some crunchy salad leaves. Topped with a few nuts, the dish is an absolute MUST-TRY.- Tuna Tartare Spring Roll - I love Tartares! You have to try this. You will get 3 tartares (However, because there were 4 in our party, the restaurant made 4 for us).Entree:- Sizzling Short Rib - Short rib was a little fatty. Cooked well, but a little tough in some spots. It lacked depth in flavor compared to other menu items. It tasted more like an attempt at Asian fusion. The meat, when cooked, had the consistency of something you'd find at "Old Country Buffet" instead of something from a classy restaurant. I'd probably not get it again.- Glazed Alaskan Black Cod - HOLY SMOKES.. This is one of the best Cod fish I have ever tasted! ABSOLUTELY BUTTERY, MELT IN YOUR MOUTH! I wish the dish didn't end!- Dungeness Crab Sticky Rice - Served to you in a hulled out crab shell, the rice tasted average. The service size is reasonable. If you ordered a few entrees, the rice is a nice side (if you don't want to order brown rice). Flavors were average. They throw in some nice crab meat for you to enjoy. However, nothing too special.Dessert:- Clementine Cloud - A silken vanilla could! It's very smooth. Almost reminds me of a meringue! The clementine and coconut which accompany it are a nice touch.- Sorbet - Asian pear, concord grape and coconut. The sorbets at all Buddakans are top notch. They are made in-house. However, for $10, you get a few small balls of sorbet. If you want to get full off sorbet, I suggest you go elsewhere.The service at the restaurant was exceptional. We originally had reserved for a party of 2, but they were very accommodating in getting our party a table for 4.I'd go again, but not if I was paying. Although some of the food tasted good, the price point made me feel it wasn't worth it. For the same price at either the Atlantic City or Philadelphia Buddakan, you get much more and a larger variety!If you're in the area, and you want to go to a hip and happening restaurant in Chelsea, this is a great place. Has a bar, lively atmosphere and a friendly staff. Give it a shot.
Superior service, inventive food, great ambiance. Overall, excellent experience. Great date spot.

We went here for our company Christmas party. We called a week prior to make a reservation and they said they were booked but could squeeze us in at 6:45. They stressed the fact that if we were a minute late our table would not be held. So right after work we rushed to get there and the restaurant was half empty. We were confused as to why we had to rush so much considering how empty it was. Aside from that, the decor was amazing. I really loved the community table downstairs, however, we were seated upstairs in a back (very dark) corner. It wasn't quite as lively as it seemed downstairs, but it was still nice. As for food, we started with the edamame dumplings, they were melt in your mouth good and so unique. Then we had the rock shrimp, which had a spicy almost buffalo sauce, these were one of the table favorites. We also had the tuna tartare spring rolls, these were spectacular! For entrees we had the garlic lobster (my choice, loved it), my coworker got the black cod which was also really delicious. Then the guys both got the steak, which I thought was a strange choice for a place like this... but it was SO SO good. It was sliced with an amazing dipping sauce. I was very surprised this dish was so good. I should also note that we got two orders of the lobster fried rice and we all loved it! As for drinks, I sent mine back because it was so weak (I wasn't offered a stronger one, they just offered to take it off of the bill). I tried a coworkers drink and that was terrible too. Side Note: I'm not picky with drinks, I'll drink anything with liquor but these tasted like straight up virgin drinks! If I went back I'd stick to champagne or wine. I was surprised such a fun/clubby restaurant wouldn't have better cocktails. So overall Food was good and liked the decor, but service (reservation girl plus waiter) and drinks were seriously lacking.
I'm definitely not the first to review this restaurant, but here are some important points you should know before making a visit here:1.  As far as aesthetics goes, this restaurant has to be, by far, the most appealing I've been to (not this week, this year, but my lifetime).  I mean, how often do you walk down a long staircase, overshadowed by a glamorous chandelier and high ceiling?  You are then seating in dimly lit room, with slender white candles dripping it's wax on to a winged eagle.    2.  If you're Asian, when you look at the menu, you'll probably think this is overpriced Chinese food.  You're thinking to yourself, "hm .. I can go to Chinatown and order double the food at half the price." (I know I did!), but keep in mind if you're here at Buddhakan, chances are you're trying to impress someone, and you don't want to look like a pig (lol).  (More importantly, each dish has a western flare to it, and presentation is phenomenal.)3.  The workers here are very professional, If you're seated at the long dining table, and want a table of your own, just ask!  Don't get offended if it doesn't go your way, keep in mind they serve hundred of people a day, and they try to accommodate everyone.  Remember to make reservations and request the dining room that you want.

The first stop on my foodie trip to NYC is Buddakan for dinner. I'm always reluctant to try "fancy" Asian food, especially when I travel. However, my friend chose it because this place was featured the Sex and the City movie. It's the spot where Carrie and Big have their wedding rehearsal dinner and I must admit, it was pretty gorgeous on screen. Buddakan isn't traditional Asian by any means but Asian inspired. It was gorgeous and the food was yummy too! My two friends and I shared: Edamame Dumplings - Okay, let's get the bad out first. I did not like this at all even though so many reviews recommended it. It tasted like baby food wrapped in sticky dumpling skin. Save yourself some green and skip this. Tuna Tartar Spring Roll - This isn't too far fetched from how tuna tartar is normally served with chips or some kind of crisp. This one is so much better though because the crunch comes from the roll that neatly ensures that every bite is filled with delicious fresh tuna!Chili Rock Shrimp - OMG. This is my favorite of the night. The rock shrimp is perfectly fried and then drenched in a yummy orange cream sauce. The chili seasoning gives it a nice kick. I could have eaten two plates of this stuff.Boneless Spare Ribs - Succulent ribs! I wished I had some white rice to go with it. Chinese Sausage Fried Rice - Eh. It would have been fine IF the rice was cooked properly. Unfortunately it was hard and chewy. Not good news for a daily rice eater. Ginger Glazed Veal Cheeks with Lo Mein Noodles and Pickled Apple Salad - I loved the tender veal. The thick noodles were a great complement. Didn't care too much for the apple salad. It is definitely a little pricey but you come for the atmosphere as well as the food. Both in general don't disappoint. I also didn't think we would get full after this meal. I was pleasantly proven wrong.
Not a fan of anything we ordered, which was the chili rock shrimp (tiny shrimp), hoison glazed pork belly, and fried rice. However, the atmosphere is awesome. I'd go here only for drinks.
I want to live in NYC just to eat at this restaurant on a regular basis. Duck salad I could eat for breakfast, lunch, and dinner! You want a trendy place with beautiful decor that actually tastes good? This is the place for you.If you say to yourself "I want to go somewhere trendy for dinner where I can see celebrities!" don't sacrifice quality for decor!  There are so many places in the city that have a sterling reputation for some weird reason (Tao, Spice Market) that just don't deliver on serving great food along with a trendy ambiance.Buddakan is not in the same vein as Tao or Spice Market.  This is first and foremost a place that consistently delivers great food, and really is the total package if you are looking for ambiance, decor and a delicious meal.  This place is huge, so this is highly recommended for big groups.  Each room has a distinctly different atmosphere to it, which really adds to your experience.  You can dine at Buddakan 3 different times and feel like you've been at a different restaurant each time.Highly Recommended.

I came to Buddakan to celebrate my birthday. We were immediately directed to the lounge area for drinks until our table was ready. Despite arriving on time for our 7:30 reservation, it was half hour until we were seated. The ambiance here is very chic, dim lighting and lots of candles. There's a trendy crowd here, and lots of large groups. We were seated in the downstairs area which looked like a labyrinth of dimly lit rooms with long tables. Club music was pumping, adding to the vibe. Our waiter was warm and attentive.I started with a refreshing drink called Smash, which had strawberries. For appetizer, I had lobster egg rolls and my husband had spareribs. Both were good, but average. The entres didn't go as smoothly as expected. The waiter brought out my husband's dinner first, then our rice. I waited a least 10 minutes before my meal was served, which made it awkward for my husband who would not start his meal until mine was served. Shame on Buddakan. The charred filet was also average. The cod was soft and tasty, but the chef slightly burned the glaze on top. The tiny eggplant accompaniment also had a burnt taste, which virtually ruined the dish. Since the food was mediocre and the prices outrageous for the quality, we skipped dessert. The waitstaff brought out vanilla ice cream with Happy Birthday scrolled in chocolate, which was a nice touch.This is a place to try at least once, but IMHO the high prices are for the scene and good service, not the food. It's also better for large groups. The loud music isn't conducive to conversation, and I left with a sore throat.

JulieBuddakan for V day...  what can I say???  yep I'm a wonderful date...   Reserved this over 3 weeks ago and the best I could do was a 10pm reservation so this spot is popular....   I honestly try to avoid these themed asian fusion spots as I am of the Asian persuasion and feel that the food will disappoint...  I go to these spots with a cynical mind thinking that food should always trump over the bougey atmosphere that's built into high ceilings, grand chandeliers, super sized Buddha's, enormous ice sculptures, long ass tables and super model hostesses.....So going in I'm thinking, where the heck is the doorman that's usually there trying to make the spot look like a fancy lounge/nightclub...  As i approached the over crowded check in area exactly on time for my resv... I'm thinking there is no way I'm getting to my table for another 30 - 40 mins...  I'm ready to head to the packed bar/lounge and start sucking down $15 fruity cocktails....  But OMG..  As my gorgeous date and I head to the bar after checking our coats, we're stopped by a hostess with menu in hand ready to seat us...  "STEAK SAUCE..."  And yes the restaurant is wait for it...  'Legendary"  We were seated on ground floor which is like having mezzanine level seats at a broadway show.  The real action is downstairs in the orchestra seats with the incredibly long table, high ceilings and side rooms that look ohhh so cozy and romantic...Our waiter came promptly and was excellent at describing the menu and letting us know how many dishes would be appropriate.  Thus far I am having a wonderful 5 STAR time.   Got my Tsing Tao and I'm ready to go....Now to the real test... THE FOOD.   Started with the edamame dumplings cause everyone raves about them on yelp.  There were 5 pieces and very unique in flavor.  Almost like edamame mash potato as a filling in a dumpling.  I say unique because I thought they were ok and don't regret ordering it but my date thought it was fantastic.  Also went with the tuna tartare on top of chopped deviled eggs.  I thought that was better and a great combination.  The tuna though were small cubed sushi pieces.  I might have preferred tuna tartare to be softly mixed with the usual mustard, oil, lemon juice and then put on top of the chopped deviled eggs.  But still an excellent choice.  I considered the tuna tartare spring rolls but just couldn't fathom what that would taste like???Entrees were the crusted ribeye and the hot and sour scallops.  The ribeye was good and done medium (which they cooked it more than they should have).  But it does pale in comparison to the sizzling t-bone that i can get in chinatown.  It was a nice sized meat and we didn't even finish it.  The scallops were also just ok.  You get 4 pieces and the sauce wasn't really sour or spicy???  It said made with mushrooms and tofu but neither accompaniment really stood out either.  I think both dishes are victims of a restaurant that wants to look shi shi and present well, but when faced with an asian dude that eats too much will fail in the taste dept....  We ordered a Chinese sausage fried rice cause I think it will be something incredibly tasty and unique.  It wasn't :(  Just typical fried rice...  shuda just saved the $10 bucks and had white rice....Finished the night with the dessert special which was a chocolate cake filled with ??(forgot), some mousse with fruits in a triangular chocolate sandwich like setup, and sorbet covered with vanilla ice cream.  This was fantastico !!!!  A nice finish to a nice meal for a nice evening....   Again, the service was impeccable, they changed dishes and utensils for as after each course and didn't give us cheap takeout chopsticks like Megu did....  Expect to pop $150 - $200 for this meal....So to summarize:Staff:             5 STARSAmbiance:   4 STARSApps:            4 STARSEntrees:       3 STARSDessert:       5 STARSOverall:         4 STARS

Everything at the restaurant was perfect.  The service, ambience, and food were all great.  My friend said their drinks were also great but because my other friend is pregnant so we just had water.  The dim sum menu looked great.  I almost wanted to order one of each.  We end up ordering the Lobster and Crab Shu Mai, Sea bass Roll, and Scallion pancake with spare ribs.  I love all three and especially the scallion pancake because the texture was just spectacular.  The pancake with the beef topped with green apples makes it sweet, salty, and crispy in one bite.  For entree, we had the steak and pekking duck fried rice.  The steak was very tender but the fried rice was way too salty.  I'm guessing the chef is probably non-asian because when you stir fry rice with soy sauce you don't need to add salt anymore.  For dessert, we had the banana bread pudding and green tea donuts.  If you ever order these two, eat the green tea donut first because the sweetness of the banana bread pudding will cover the taste of the donut and make it bland.  Of course, that's what I did and I end up not being able to taste the donut at all.  I will definitely go back and try all the other dim sum items.  This is definitely a great place for food and hangout.

Entering through a nondescript door on 9th Avenue you are greeted by a busy concierge desk and then escorted to a dark, sexy lounge to await your table. This place exudes class. A bouncer guards the kitchen door just to keep things tidy and safe. After a host gathers you to your table (how did they find us?), you will be wowed as you descend the grand staircase. Soak it all in. It is huge.We didn't realize at first but the menu setup of Buddakan favors sharing so this is not a she and him meal but rather order a number of items and share. The edamame dumplings are indeed inventive and a must-try. The rock shrimp were perfectly done and just the right spice. The filet strips melt in your mouth. The monkfish is crispy, just the right heat. The crying chocolate dessert will leave you weaping for more.Most NY restaurant reviews tell the tale of tight spaces and small tables. While Buddakan is huge you can taste your neighbors food. But the ambience keeps you focused. It seemed like it was setup to favor different groups, as we found a large table singing Happy Birthday had plenty of lighting but our two-top was intimate and cozy. So many little enclaves and rooms - loved the 'library' room. The crowd is mixed, a lot of couples and singles dressed for a night out, a father with his two teenaged girls celebrating something, a birthday party of 20-somethings. Hip enough to keep out Mah and Pah Denim-Shorts but not too hip to need a socialite under your arm.

All the glamor of sex and the city but with the good food of a hole in the wall.Food: we got the tasting menu, which was ravishing.  There were a ton of different dishes served family style, but here are what I liked best:Appetizers:-chili rock shrimp - I don't eat much fried food, nor do I like gelatinous sauces, but this tangy spicy sauce on my favorite protein made for an irresistible combo.-edamame dumpling - strangely intense flavor for a dish made out of one of nature's most subtle beans.  -peking duck salad - pulled Peking duck glazed with hoisin sauce and then topped with rocket, shredded wonton and a perfectly poached egg.  It was divine.  And beautifully presented.  I don't even like Peking duck and I loved this.-the tasting menu came with many more delicious treats, but these were the stand out options.Entrees: (again, commenting on standouts only, as the list of amazing dishes could fill this page)-some sort of butterfly shrimp with candied walnuts that I've only ever seen before in an authentic Cantonese restaurant in Flushing...and that place was so authentic the menu was in Cantonese, so nice to put delicacy to name.-hoisin glazed cod - hoisin is usually fool proof but this cod was also cooked to moist fluffy perfection.-beef and pepper sauce - served in a rice flour crisp basket.  You'll definitely have a second helping of this, if the shrimp runs out.Dessert: of the 4 options, I loved-bread pudding a la mode with a crisped sweet wonton wrapper.-molten chocolate cake - and it was as good as my 2 favorite chocolate cakes in NYC (Jojo and Pastis).  Service: took of a star here.  People were nice, water glasses usually stayed filled, but sometimes they were just clueless.  And given how expensive and fancy this place looks, I didn't appreciate that gy often forgot serving spoons.  Still - amazing experience for my stomach!Ambience:  stunning downstairs area.  It's the type of place to which I would take an out-of-town guest.  It has all that ritzy lavishness that NYC is associated with, yet at its core, the food is truly great.  Very rare that I love a big fancy restaurant but I would come back here!

Let's face it, you come here for the "wow" factor. And you definitely get it. I came here for my birthday and was not disappointed. I had no trouble making reservations and was even asked when they called to confirm if it was for a special event. Those small details make a huge difference and are the reason you pay more. The entrance is very discreet which is cool. There were about five hosts checking people in, so you know the place was busy. I let them know we had a reservation and they told us to wait in the "lounge." I was a little worried that they would seat us in there. It was cramped and everyone seemed to be on top of one another. They didn't though. We waited about five minutes until a very nice woman came and escorted us down the grand staircase to our table in the main hall. Wow, that was impressive! We all ordered drinks and a few appetizer plates as well as dessert. Everything was great, but since I didn't have an entree plate I can't really judge the food. Overall though it was a great experience. I loved that the music in the restaurant wasn't too loud and overbearing like some places. The big hall had an echo with all the people but I could still hear the conversation. Our table was at the base of the staircase, pretty big and private which was nice considering how cramped NY can be. And the crying chocolate cake was amazing! They even wrote "happy birthday" to me in chocolate syrup on the plate. When we were all taking pictures a manager came over without asking to let us all get in for one shot. We weren't rushed out even though it was a busy night. I'd come back, but probably only for a special event. This is a great place to take someone if you want to impress them!

I've been here a couple of times on business dinners and really like it so I recommended it for dinner with another couple. I was not let down again. The dishes here are fresh, tasty and blend different spices and tastes for a great sensation. For appetizers we had wok fried oyster with foie gras, (great blend of tastes with the oyster, some soy and the fried texture), tuna spring rolls (how do they keep the tuna cold with the spring roll fried!!! was awesome), boneless spareribs (very tender, glazed tasted like plum), general tso dumplings (similar to a soup dumpling but with kick) char sui pork "buns" (actually pork belly with a hoison glaze!).  All were top notch and I would have them again.For side dishes we split the lobster fried rice (very delicate with pieces of lobster throughout) and the dungeness sticky rice (a heavier rice wi pieces of crab served in the car shell) were both excellent and contrasted with each other nicely.For entrees we had Mongolian lamb chops (I'm not a lamb fan but by the sound of the people who had them were oohing over them), charred filet of beef (tender like butter served medium rare with a wasabi mayo), sweet and crisply shrimp (a sweet but spicy glaze was perfect), black pepper beef (a little kick!).A great dinner with friends is the perfect night out. I recommend this to small or large groups but the larger the group you can share more!!!
If I could give this restaurant a "zero" rating I would. I was visiting NYC with my friends and we had made reservations a month in advance. Despite that, they seated us 55 minutes late. The service was sub par at best. We waited a long time for our drinks. We had specifically asked for steamed rice to be brought out with our entrees, but our entrees came, got cold, but the rice didn't come. The food was absolutely terrible; there was not a single dish that I would recommend. I will say that their appetizers are very good and unless you want to make a meal out of appetizers, stay away from this restaurant. We asked to speak with the manager on three different occasions, but nobody showed up. We finally got the manager to come after our entrees had gone cold as the rice didn't come. His explanation for the late seating and the poor service was "well..we are very busy". When I am spending my hard earned money, that is just not a good excuse. I will never visit this restaurant again and certainly do not recommend that anyone go there. There are far too many good restaurants in NYC to be wasting your precious time here.
I went here with a fairly large group for dinner.  The food and service was good.  I also liked the interior of this place.  Worth checking out.
So after years of wanting to go to Buddakan, I finally did ! I took my boyfriend there for his birthday and we both loved it! Upon arrival, you are greeted by the friendliest staff [looks like you are checking in at a hotel]; they kindly told us to have a drink in the lounge area, our table will be a few minutes. By the time I opened the drink menu, she had come to scoop us away to our table! That was a plus.I was a little disappointed when she kept walking us past the stairs [The downstairs is so beautiful, I was hoping to sit down there]. But we still sat in an OK area. [The ambiance wasn't as nice as downstairs though!]For drinks, I had a glass of Prosecco and my boyfriend had a Fever, which consisted of Tquila  jalapenos -- a bit of an acquired taste for some, but we loved it! [I say we because of course I drank some of his :) ]After reading so many reviews, of course I had to take others advice and try the edamame dumplings -- OUT OF THIS WORLD! THESE WERE BY FAR THE BEST THINGS I'VE EVER EATEN!We also shared the hoisin glazed pork belly which was a gorgeous presentation with spicy shallots, cabbage, and steamed buns -- also, AMAZING!! The appetizers look small at first, but are filling for two to share!Unfortunately, I wasn't as impressed with the entree as I was with the appetizers, but still tasted good -- I had Alaskan Black Cod; he had broken Chili Chicken [-- beer battered with yummy chili sauce].And lastly, for dessert, we shared a Chocolate Peanut Butter Bombe -- he loved the chocolate, I loved the peanut butter -- it worked out for both :)So I only gave it 4 stars for the fact that we didn't get to sit downstairs and because the entrees weren't as great as I expected. But I will be back to Buddakan and definitely try something else for my entree!
Went on Saturday night for my friend's bachelorette party. Impeccable food and service. A must-visit in NYC. Try the specialty cocktails!
5 stars on architecture and decor alone...both indoor and outdoor decor is amazing...feels like you are in Barcelona or some European country. Amazingly high ceilings. Bar and sitting / waiting area is so upbeat and NY meets Europe meets LAish. Definitely not good for walk ins, very crowded, can be a long wait even with reservations. A little loud for convo at dinner if upstairs...room for larger groups downstairs. Dressy casual attire, i.e. ladies, cute shirt, jeans and some hot heels and a jacket depending on weather will suffice...men, ask your ladies what to wear LOL. Edamame and chicken dumplings were yummy, boneless ribs, lobster fried rice, mixed greens, also very tasty...kinda like a tappas feel though, so if super hungry, order  lot but don't be mad when you get the pricey bill!
Wow. Stunning decor, beautiful people and delicious food are rare combination but plentifully exist in New York. Especially if you expect that fancy Chinese fusion will turn out to be such a disaster, Buddakan presents a chic way to enjoy everything Asian that actually taste unbelievably yummy.The place is also featured in Sex and The City The Movie when Carrie had her rehearsal dinner before the wedding. I'm such a fan of the medieval Asian meets modern romantic interior. Between the ancient giant door and dangling chandelier at the big dinning room, this place swept me off my feet.-hoisin glazed pork belly. spicy shallots, cabbage, steam buns. succulent pork belly with sweet glazed flavor.-edamame dumpling, shallot-sauternes broth. let's start with my least favorite dish on the table. Taste like mochi gone wrong, despite the great reviews. -sizzling short ribs. mushroom chow fun, Asian pear. this one is amazingly cooked to tenderness and flavorful.-glazed Alaskan black cod. chili egg plant, black bean relish. very soft and moist. -pepper steak chow fun. Chinese broccoli and garlic chives. surprisingly delicious and reminds me of Thai's pad see ew.-chili rock shrimp, toasted ginger. perfectly fried to crispiness, spicy sauce adds a kick to it. yumm...-chinese sausage fried rice. sunny side up egg. another favorite of mine, unexpectedly it taste so similar with Indonesian fried rice. two thumbs up!pics - yummycrave.com/2010/04/b…
Swanky and trendy, Buddakan is one of those celebrity-infused restaurants where you take your favorite out-of-town guests to make them jealous that you live in New York.  The food is amazing, particularly the Edamame Dumpling appetizer ($11) and the Whole Peking Duck ($44).  Arrive about a half hour before you reservation so you and see-and-be-seen in the front lounge area.  There are a number of specialty drinks around the $12 range that are very fun.  If you are seated upstairs, be sure to take a peek into the massive and cavernous downstairs dining room, with ceilings more than 2-stories high and filled with a long banquet-like table.  The service is excellent, the food is fantastic; just be sure that your wallet is prepared to take a hit.

Food is not fantastic, pushy waiter that kept saying that we haven't ordered enough food (we actually left food on our plates....).Drinks are good.Good to impress not so demanding tourists...

The black cod was super delicious and I really love the flavor and the combination. The service was fantastic. It was very dark and a little loud but not as loud as Tao. It was a saturday night and the only reservation we could get was for 10:30.And it was all worth it. All the meals are family style and delicious. The drinks were strong. The service spectacular. I really can't find anything bad to say about this place. I made reservations for me and 3 friends, as soon as we came in we were told to go to the lounge and somebody would take us to our seats shortly. After we got drinks and about ten minutes passed, we were taken to our seats. The whole place looks really nice and well decorated. We had the friendliest waiter and he really knew a lot about the menu which is important since I want to know about what I am eating and what's best to order. The food tasted great, we got a bunch of appetizers since it was too late at night for whole entres. We were served quickly and everything was delicious, especially crying chocolate for dessert!
Their gold star is for consistency. Check:My out of town guests consistently enjoy this place. The ambiance is consistently stellar, somehow it escapes being outdated and it feels like a different experience each time depending on which room you sit in.Check: The menu doesn't irritatingly change every month. My favorites are consistently there(  black cod, whole crispy fish, rock shrimp. I really can't vouch for anything else..).Check: There is consistently good service. For example, a fork and spoon set placed before me for dessert was less than sparkling clean and authentic or not our server seemed appalled as did the manager. I made zero stink, just smiled understandingly and they still comped two desserts for us and apologized profusely. That kind of response should be the norm but it isn't and it's one of those things that makes buddakan special.
I came here for one of my birthday dinners and basically chose it because it was the most attractive restaurant I had ever seen (via online pictures).  The large room with the stairs and long table is what got to me - this is what my fantasy dining room is like by the way.However my party was seated in a room beyond this one.  We ordered a ton of food to share.  I thought the dishes were decent but for me the decor was the most memorable part of the experience.
This is probably one of the best restaurants I have been to in NYC and by far the best culinary NYC experience! I highly highly recommend it. Such a beautiful restaurant. And we were very lucky to have this really nice, cute and patient guy serving us, I think his name is Fred!  Make sure to ask for a table in his section. Don't forget to  try the edamame dumplings, the short ribs pancakes, the tuna tartar egg-rolls and the vegetable rice!
The decor makes you feel rich. Don't really understand the fusion part though. I got the rib eye and shared the lobster fried rice with my gf. She got some duck wanton soup which did not look appetizing. The steak's flavor was nothing new and what they seem to call fusion there is just you order either an american main dish (steak, chicken, etc.) with an asian side or vise-versa. Back to the steak; it was the most tender steak I have ever had, Literally melted in my mouth. Lobster fried rice was ok.   For dessert we had the crying chocolate dessert. So good it deserves its own paragraph. I mean it was an orgasm in my mouth good. Only problem  was it was SO SMALL! Now that I look back I regret not ordering another one. Recommend this place, but be prepared to spend $$$.
We took a high school graduate for her graduation because we knew it was a sceney place. I don't have much to add to the other reviews. I will only say the decor and atmosphere is spectacular, service was over the top. Our server was a professional server not an actor.The food is very good. I think this is a special occasion place and you pay for the over all experience. There was nothing wrong with the food. The presentation was great, the food was good but the menu was pretty standard. You can view the menu at their site or at menu pages.I had a cocktail which was called Charm. It was a passion fruit sparkling wine cocktail. It was very good. All menu items were very good. The Peking Duck everyone at the table agreed was the best they had ever had. The beef tar tar appetizer was great. It was all good.The desserts were all kind of similar and if they could improve anything about the food it would be the desserts.I would highly recommend it for anyone.

Does Buddakan need another review? No. But five days after eating there, I still cannot stop thinking about the edamame dumplings and shredded beef scallion pancakes. This was by far one of the best meals I have had in my three years living in New York. We were greeted by the friendliest bartender in New York when we waited at the bar. She happily advised on cocktails and made a deliciously strong drink for the bf and I -a rich man's John Daly. We were seated within ten minutes of our reservation, and again, greeted by a most friendly waitress who was so attentive it was shocking. The food came out quickly, but upon biting in, it was evident how fresh and calculated the ingredients in each dish were. My bf told them it was my birthday and they came out with a beautiful bread pudding with Happy Birthday in chocolate and a lit candle. Come here, come here, come here!
For those of you who are not aware, Buddakan is the restaurant where they filmed the rehearsal dinner of "Carrie and Big" from Sex and the City Movie.  It is located in the Meatpacking district.We had made reservations for 8:45pm.  Upon arrival, we were escorted to the bar.  The "bar" area is quite nice.  There is long bar on one side of the room with bar stools and in the middle of the room there are large square tables with benches that are meant to be shared with other customers as you enjoy your cocktail.  The bartender was extremely nice, she made a very good cosmopolitan Martini for us (Didn't taste strong, but once finished, you felt the effects).  The restaurant is beautiful and very large.  It is a 2 story building where you can see the first floor from the second floor.  The decorations and the candle light lighting were perfect.   After a few drinks, we were escorted to our table on the first floor.  The service was exceptional.  The waitress was extremely knowledgeable about the restaurant as well as other restaurants from the same Chef.  Appetizers- Lobster egg rolls were fantastic!  Pork pot stickers were also very good, but nothing out of the ordinary.  Main- Lobster fried rice and Sizzling Short Ribs were delicious.  We also ordered the Shacha Chicken-I don't love BBQ so I may be partial, but it was OK.  Nothing grand about it.  Dessert- Peanut Butter Bar!  Delicious!!!
Fellow NFL football player Dustin Keller recommended this place to me, and let me start off by saying this isn't really my kind of food, im more of a steakhouse kind of guy, but this place is truly amazing. If you're looking for a visually stunning place to eat, a place with culinary vision and a obviously inspired chef, go here.The food was simply amazing, everything about it, taste, freshness, presentation, it was delicious.If Adrian Peterson loves it, you better.
When I first came here a few years ago I thought it was pretty damn excellent. We went crazy with the cocktails and tried a million small dishes and whiled away the hours without feeling rushed. The waiters let you flirt with them.Lately I've been feeling less than impressed. First it was the clientele. When did all the people from New Jersey and Long Island start flooding into this place like it was the ark that would save them from the flood? Then they must have fired their mixologist, because the cocktails still have fancy names but they taste wrong! A good cocktail is one that goes down easy, but I could barely get down half a glass of the new swill they are passing off as designer drinks. As for the food, well, each time I visit i lower my expectations for the next occasion accordingly. The menu is consistent, but the taste isn't, and that is bewildering. Some dishes are overspiced, some are undersalted. It's like they decided to hire the busboys to do the cooking. This place is no longer fun, and if someone suggested returning, I would most likely pass. There are so many amazing places in Buddakan's league that would be better bang for my buck.

Went to Buddakan for dinner last thursday... myself and 2 friends...the place was filled with a lot of "business" looking types, and even though I don't appear that way, it wasn't an issue with our service etc... basically, being 3 rocknroll looking people didn't effect the way we were treated.We had a variety of dishes and everything was very, very good.Some could/would say the food is pricey, but it IS a restaurant in NYC, so you have to accept the business has bills to pay, and with that in mind, you need to pull a profit to stay afloat, so the prices didn't bother me.All in all, I'd highly recommend Buddakan.It is goooooood.Oh, and the waiter gave us free dessert! Went with a few friends that were visiting from out of town. So it was one of those once-in-a-while nice restaurant nights. The wait wasnt long at all, but then again, we arrived around 11pm. I was suprised they were still serving, but there were still people being seated and tables still being served. Service: A bit slow. Our waitress was nice but she didn't make her rounds very often. Once we asked her to take a picture for us but she said she'd be back as her hands were full, but never did come back. We ended up having a bus-boy take it instead. She was however quite polite and apologized after when she remembered. Food:Typical of a higher end dining restaurant. The portions were small, expensive, but delicious and well prepared. Everything on the menu is meant to be shared family style. Think of it as a Tapas restaurant with an asian twist. Most of the dishes had some asian/chinese origin to them. A few of the dishes we had:Edamame Dumplings - served in a light broth - basically edamame bean paste wrapped inside a chinese dimsum shrimp dumpling skin (sans the shrimp) - you can really taste the edamame flavour, slightly on the salty sideLamb Chops - medium rare - spot on, very tender. Deep fried jumbo shrimp - quite good, reminds me of a japanese izakaya dish Ive had before Ambiance: Romantic. The dining room downstairs was very nice - think medevil time long table with chandeliers hanging down from a very high ceiling. Too bad we didn't get seated there.
Crazy cool interior - it's worth checking out the main dining room. I'd like to know just how much cash the owners droppped on that rennovation....The food is delicious but certainly pricy - the edamame dumplings are quite a unique experience and the Black Cod was mouth watering. If you're with a group of discerning foodies with deep pockets, this is a great spot. It's a bit of a ridiculous scene though - when I was there, a racuous group of pre-teens had gathered for a friends birthday. All of the prepubuscent girls were decked out in designer duds. The youth of Manhattan grow up way too fast!

I'm originally from las vegas, so it's extremely reminiscent of Tao. Especially in size. The lounge exudes sexy low red lighting, pefect vibe for a rendezvous- until you realize the cocktail servers could really care less about you. Actually this would be the perfect place for a couple who only has eyes for eachother and who won't be distracted by the vast amount this Restaurant/ Bar is lacking. The drinks were sub par and mildly unique. They offer bottle service, but I couldn't imagine anyone ordering anything other than a bottle of champagne. This isn't a nightclub, and if you want to pick someone up, you might have a chance at the bar. Lots of out of towners- I'm sure the food isn't bad, but I think I got my fill. I wouldn't return unless someone else insisted- even then I would probably suggest somewhere else...
If basing my time at Buddakan on how my body physically felt while I was there, I would have to give it a 1. I was still hungover from the night before, had walked 6 miles all day, was stuffed on chillie cheese fries at snack time (yes, snack time), and felt like I was going to be sick to my stomach. HOWEVER, despite this, the food was excellent, the service spot on, and the atmosphere unbelievable. I'll break it down. 1. Service- Minus having to wait in the bar area for our table (what's the point of reservations, i ask?) the area was lively. Due to feeling ill I didn't drink but my friends cocktails seemed beautiful and creative. Our server was wonderful, attentive and explained the menu well. 2. Menu- Flipping unbelievably delicious. we ordered the springrolls which were steaming hot and amazing, and the rock shrimp. I am obsessed with rock shrimp and this was very good. For our mains we had the Short Rib, chillie chicken, lobster fried rice, blackened cod, caulliflower, and a few other things I can't remember now. All of it was steaming hot and delicious. Special shoutout to the short rib. I polished it off it was so good. My only negative is that the waitress suggested we order 2 aps, 3 mains, and two misc. from the rice and sides. This was way too much food for 3 girls and we ended up only eating half of it. 3. The Vibe- It was on SATC for crying out loud so of course it's cool but it was REALLY nicely done. New York has nailed the "concept" restaurant, and this one did not dissapoint. Large, loud, and lively and not so dark that you couldn't see your food or friends. Amazing place, yummy food. **1 thing to note. The bathrooms on the upstairs floor are GROSS. at least the ones I used. Communal, and the floor was wet. For a restaurant so commited to looking chic, cool and at over 30$ a plate, I'd appreciate a cleaner restroom that a male didn't just use. There could be other bathrooms I was missing though.**

I took my wife here for her birthday on Monday. From what I had heard about Steven Starrs' first venture into NYC, I had to check it out. We weren't disappointed. Visually, the restaurant is stunning. We were seated at a table overlooking the BIG room. It reminds me of scenes from movies like "The King and I" with its ridiculously high ceiling, elaborately carved relief's and 3 massive chandeliers hanging over a 40 seat long table.My wife had one of the special cocktails, the "Charm" ($11.00), made with prosecco,  passion fruit liqueur, apples and berries. To perfumy for me, but my wife loved it. For appetizers, we shared the chili rock shrimp ($13.00) and lobster egg rolls ($14.00). The shrimp were tempura fried to perfection, and the sauce was sweet and tart.  The egg rolls were, I think, frozen and fried, but they were still delicious with a sauce that I can't recall now.The wine list is categorized by adjectives. Rich, Refreshing, Silky Smooth and Muscular are a few of the categories. We opted for Silky Smooth with the Rex Hill Pinot Noir ($65.00). It was, well, silky smooth with a nice black peppery finish.For main courses, we shared the Filet Steak ($29.00) with a wonton filled with crispy potatoes and  Dijon mustard sauce, and the Lobster and Shrimp Chow Fun ($35.00) The steak was melt-in-your-mouth tender, and they got medium-rare perfectly. The portion was kinda small, I think it was about 8 oz. The mustard sauce was almost custard-like, and was great for dipping the steak with. The wonton was just a shell filled with potato chips. The lobster and shrimp chow fun came in an x.o. brandy sauce and the classic chow fun noodles (wide, slippery rice noodles) This dish was great, served in a deep bowl, and the lobster was cooked right...it wasn't too chewy as often is the case.Dessert was presented very nicely, the pastry chef wrote "Happy Birthday Susan" on the Crying Chocolate Cake with Coffee Ice Cream ($10.00) and we also enjoyed the Kaffir Lime Tarte ($10.00). What can  say about chocolate and lime? Just that the desserts alone would be a reason for us to go back.We splurged a bit on two Inniskillin Icewines ($25.00 each), but it's a birthday, right? The server was awesome in that she brought out tastes of three different dessert wines for us to taste, and when we tasted the Inniskillin, the price didn't matter. Rich and intensely sweet from the concentrated sugar in the grapes, it was the perfect end to a great dining experience.The server (Yonella) was very friendly and informative, very important to me, being in the biz. The service was prompt when we first arrived when there were a lot of empty tables. It got a bit slower when the restaurant filled up. I took about twenty minutes to get the check, which sucked cause we have a new puppy that was missing us. I know the server just got maybe 4 new tables, but that's when a manager should check on all the tables to see if anyone needs anything. The total check was $261.00 before tip, so if you are going to splurge here, bring a fat wallet or purse. (Well, we did spent like $140.00 on booze) Overall, I have to say that it was a good value, based upon the total experience. We are thinking of having my next birthday party there, but this time with 20 people, at the BIG table in the BIG room...and I want to sit at the head of the table!
Could Buddakan be the best Asian fusion restaurant in NYC? I, for one, would not be scandalized if somebody suggested that was the case - it's that good. After having some excellent drinks at the bar while waiting for our table (mezcal jalapeno), we were ready to enjoy some serious food at 10:30pm. One of our team members was vegetarian, so we ordered edamame dumplings, carrot dumplings, and the 2 vegetarian tofu dishes. Add on top of that the lobster spring rolls, the glazed pork belly, the filet, the soft shell tempura crab and a noodle soup. The result is bliss. Everything was excellent, but the edamame dumplings (mashed with truffle undertones), the soft shell tempura crab (crispy delish), the glazed pork belly (mouth-wateringly fatty scrumptious), and the filet (usa that mustard-mayo sauce) were just over the top amazing. Excellent wine list too, though on the expensive side. Service could not be faulted. And the ambiance has just the right amount of pre-party vibe leading up to a crazy night in the MePa. Bring adventurous out-of-towners to impress.
This is place is enormous and elaborate and might take your breath away, yet somehow manages to stay intimate. It's an extravaganza of sights and sounds (with all the requisite Pan Asian twists) but it works. 

To be fair, my party only went here on the later side, for drinks and small plates (mostly dumplings, which were great), but the atmosphere - especially since Buddakan is so new - was that you were at the right place at the right moment in the right city.

The decor here is stunning and it is such a scene.  Definitely worth the overpriced asian fusion food.Highlights include the Tuna Tartar spring rolls Jade Shrimp Dumplings (every bite is brimming with meaty bites of real shrimp, not shrimp paste or fillers)Sweet  Crispy Jumbo Shrimp - covered in that mayonaissey sauce (yes, it's a bit like the traditional chinese restaurants, but the shrimps are massive and the flavor is spot on)Dungeoness Crab Sticky Rice - served in the shell of a real dungeoness crab.  Great presentation.  Note- the rice is going to be sticky tho and you'll have to work to dig out all the glutinous rice out of that crab shell.Twice Cooked Long Beans - this was AWESOME and quite different that just stir fried long beansSpiced Tofu  Cashews - a friend threw this dish into the mix, and at first I was like, who's going to waste space on this?  Boy was I wrong?  It was absolutely delicious!In general, I think all the fish entrees are great!To save on $$$ and calories, I would pass on: Edamme Dumplings (now I know that others think this is a real favorite, but it is too mushy for my taste)Taro Lollipops - I love taro puffs, but to have minced pork inside which is a bit heavy on the ginger turms me off.  If it was pork and shrimp minus the ginger, it would be a home run.Beef Bao Buns - the skin is too dense, should be much lighter.  Filling to thick and sweet.  A hole in the wall in Chinatown would have much better meat buns or pork buns.Beef Lettuce Cups - not enough dressing or wetness, just blah.  PF Chang's chicken lettuce cups are even better than theseI think all the noodle/fried rice dishes are pretty good as well.  A great place to go for a nice dinner/client dinner where everyone can dine family style. Here is a TIP:  SAVE ROOM FOR DESSERT.The dessert here is awesome.  That crying chocolate?  I think it really did make me cry.  And there is some other dessert that they had going on Winter of 2009 that was a non-chocolate dessert...it was like pear or cardommom or something...anyway, it was absolutely awesome.  Kudos to the pastry chef.  Also, if you are going to use the mens or ladies room, take note of the paintings of the man and woman of the wall leading to the entrance of the bathrooms.  The side the man is on leads to the mens room, and the side with the curvy naked woman leads to the ladies room.  There are no signs or doors, so beware!

Said to be the biggest space in all of Manhattan. Take a fantastic space. Add 4- (rather than 5-) star food.Then turn down the lights, turn up the music, and dial the pretence all the way up to 11 (let's all pretend we're at Tao in Vegas!). And drop in a few reminiscent-of-Vegas prices.... you'll get pretty close to Buddakan! If that's your thing, you'll absolutely love it. But you're going to pay for the privilege of - in this yelper's opinion - all the superfluous stuff.I know this sounds ridiculous, but if this food had been served to me in a back alley somewhere in Chinatown with neon lights and ducks hanging in the window (and a price tag to match that imagined decor) I'd be giving this place 5 stars. Instead, for me at least, it's a meh. Won't be going back, but I can understand why some people dig it.
I'm typically not a fan of high-end restaurants.  Their minuscule portions are generally no match for my vast appetite, and their hefty prices too much for my student budget.  And of course, there would usually be a palpable air of pretension that sometimes turns eating into an artistic endeavor.But Buddakan is unlike the others.  While their portions won't exactly remind anyone of Chinese takeouts, they are still sizable compared to restaurants of similar pedigree.  The decor is nice and intimate, but not so much as to overshadow the dining experience.  And the food is good.  I'm usually skeptical of these kinds of Americanized Asian places, but this place is the real deal.  Frog legs, Peking Duck...savory and authentic.

I suggested this place to my friends who were in town, mainly for the fact it was in Sex and the City! We called on a Saturday afternoon and were told the only reservation available was at midnight. We decided to show up at 8pm anyway and were able to find a table in their full service lounge. We each ordered a $12 cocktail, which were all delicious and had unique ingredients. I love this place. A friend first introduced me to Buddakan when we were looking for a chill yet not too overcrowded place to go to on a Saturday night in the Meatpacking district. The decor has a polished Asian flair and tends to be very dark and cavernous. Even though the place is large, it emits a feeling of being underground or somewhere removed from the chaos of the city. The menu is great. I love the seafood shumai and the spring rolls. The music is typical Euro modern background music and the crowd is fairly trendy but definitely chill. There is usually always a place to sit in the bar area or you can dine in the main area. My favorite drink hands-down is the specialty drink Fate; a less sweet but really tasty rendition of a hybrid martini. Overall, I can't say one bad thing about this place as it is a true departure from the over-crowded vibe of most Meatpacking locations.

This may have been my first real "fusion" experience.  Most fusion places offer Asian dishes with a European price tag.  Buddakan actually delivers an interesting twist to their dishes.We started with the Tuna Spring Roll which was tuna tartare in an eggroll crust.  It was my favorite appetizer.  Also had the Scallion Pancakes and Edamame Dumplings which were both good/ok.  I would recommend getting the Charred Filet of Beef and the lobster noodles.  The beef was a little dry, but very tender and flavorful.
I came here for dinner on Saturday expecting a fully mediocre meal in a glitzy and ridiculous restaurant.  I was pleasantly surprised at how good the food is.  The staff was a little annoying, but on the whole pleasant.  And once our server stopped talking down to me as if I had never eaten in public before (literally taking the menu from me and pointing out where the apetizers can be located), we warmed up to her.We got a bunch of small plates to share which worked out nicely for my friend and I:edamame dumplings (the texture is so soft and pillowy, outrageous), mixed mushroom chow fun (earthy, chewy, noodle goodness), hoisin glazed pork belly (a little tough, but good flavor), frog's legs (a little overcooked), chilled udon noodles (very good, mellow flavors, nice spice, but I didn't really understand the addition of the scoop of sorbet on top, it didn't really track with me), the chocolate ganache dessert (was a molten cake, not ganache at all and burned, but the jasmine ice cream was divine), and the donuts (average, they weren't as tender and soft as I wanted, but the dipping sauces were very good). On the whole, this place is beautiful, very sleek, totally over the top, but you do feel like an A lister walking down those stairs into the main dining room.  Perfect when you're in the mood for some unrestrained glitz and glamour.  Which, to be honest, I frequently am...
I wanted so much not to like this place. It's trendy, on the edge of the meatpacking, and as everyone has commented, in the rehearsal dinner scene of Sex and the City movie. I knew the atmosphere would be wonderful, but I wanted to be able to sit here and type this review saying "Sure the atmosphere is great, but the rest is overrated." Unfortunately when I break it down into atmosphere, service, food, and drinks, everything was a complete knockout and I can't help but give it 5 stars.This is swanky. It's NYC chic at its finest. If you want to dress up in your hot little outfit, and stare at people who are in equally hot little outfits, this is your place. The only thing that could've been better is if a couple of men in perfectly tailored suits came over and talked to us. And by talked to us, I mean if they bought us drinks. The drink menu was clearly tailored to my tastes. A cocktail with gin, elderflower, and prosecco? YES PLEASE! It's like they were prepared for my arrival. People have commented that the drinks are pricey, but honestly, $12 for a specialty cocktail is not absurd - it's the same price if not more anywhere in SF, and in NYC you should be prepared to spend $10 on a cocktail. Okay, I was so ready to knock the food, but honestly it was surprisingly delicious. The flavor of the edamame dumplings was subtle, light, and simply amazing. I was highly impressed. And the hoisin-glazed pork belly was...well everything pork belly should be...like ambrosia.Finally, the service was just great...we were joking with the waitress as soon as she came over, and she never left us waiting too long for our drinks. What more could I ask for?Don't let all the hype psych you out. This place has all the elements for a fabulous NYC dining experience.
In a nutshell, Buddakan is a restaurant that has good food and a better vibe. It's really more of an audiovisual than culinary experience, The food does not disappoint;  It just doesnt quite match the "oomph" of the architecture and interior design. Located conveniently next to Chelsea Market, Buddakan is a visual experience that is hard to describe. At first, it seems like you enter a hotel lobby, but once you make it past the bar, that's when you realize how large and stunning the place really is. Gorgeous chandeliers adorn the dining room that blends a medieval setting with industrial and oriental undertones. The rest of the space is really nice and functional too. The food was above good, but not great. I've personally had better Asian Fusion at Vong. However, there were some standouts. The Mongolian lamb chops and charred filet of beef were tender  perfectly cooked. The noodles were a bit greasy for my taste, but not bad. The Taro Puffs lollipops were just okay. Drinks, however, were very tasty. A lot of people complain about the service of Buddakan, but our waiter was really quick and efficient. The place does get ridiculously busy on the weekends, so I suggest going on a weekday to avoid the tourists and excessive BT crowd. Otherwise, it's the perfect place to take a date or hang out with friends before going out in the area. Buddakan reminds me a lot of Tao, both food and space wise. But, Buddakan gets the higher mark for the flash and overall experience. I just really hope it doesn't get too touristy, but it's inevitable as word of mouth continues to spread. Still worth checking out for sure.

Came here for my birthday last month. I've only been to Buddakan in AC, so didn't really know what to expect since the menu is different. I was fiending for the edamame dumplings (though it is edamame ravioli in AC) and the crispy calamari salad. We ordered those two items for appetizers, Alaskan cod and rock shrimp for entrees. Needless to say the portions were tiny. Portions in AC are huge btw. We were very happy with the appetizers. They were close to AC, but AC does it better. I've been here 3 or 4 times, but not recently (I think I was there about a year ago for a birthday). The food is always consistent, which is great because you don't have to worry about recommending something that turns out to be bad. The edamame dumplings are my absolute favorite thing on the menu. I also recommend the scallion pancakes, the chili rock shrimp, the roast duck, and the sweet and sour chicken. Their desserts change seasonally, but I remember during the summer they had some sort of dessert plate that included corn ice cream - sounds weird, but it was absolutely delicious!The only reason that this isn't getting a higher rating is because I think the food is way overpriced. It's tasty and all, but the portions aren't large, and you can easily blow $150 on dinner for 2. Another con is the clientele. Sure, it's a good restaurant and all, but I've always noticed a lot of BT in there - you can tell because they're WAY overdressed, way too loud, and tend to use the word "classy" too often. Just an observation.That being said, it's a solid restaurant with consistently good food, served in a gorgeous space.

I have been to Buddakan a number of times over the past few years, regularly when I lived in the area, and I have never been disappointed with it.  Like many locals, I usually take people from out of town or head over when I am looking for a bit of a splurge.  The wow-factor of this place really is the combined theatrical quality of it all.  I completely agree with some other reviewers in that the menu reads like overpriced Chinese, but please stay, order, loosen that grip on your purse strings, and enjoy the delicious food, fun atmosphere, beautiful surroundings, and inventive cocktails.  Enjoy the experience as a whole!  Everything I have ordered at this restaurant has been delicious, from the edamame dumplings, glazed pork belly, tuna, to the salads, the wild mushroom chow fun (Sooooo beautifully earthy and flavorful), vegetable rice with coconut curry foam, kung pao monkfish... I could go on and on.  Nearly all of the cocktails are unique and special, stars in themselves.  This is not a weekly spot, and it probably would disappoint self-proclaimed hard-core NYC foodies (what doesn't?), but I urge you to make a reservation, choose the library or the Buddah room for you and your honey to have a special, intimate but exciting night out and enjoy the opulence of it all from your first cocktail to the last bite of dessert.

I'm no Sex and the City fan but I have heard for years how fun, delicious and scene-y Buddakan is. It's all true! Especially the scene-y part! (You'll also find tourists and groups who want to be a part of the scene!)Though the food was quite good it was not spectacular. The high points for me were definitely the chilled udon noodles with lime sorbet and the yellowtail appetizer as well as the peanut butter bomb dessert. However, where they definitely shined far beyond any other restaurant I've ever been to is the service. From the hostesses to the waiter to the busboys I have never experienced such attentive, professional and genuinely amazing service. Our waiter attended to our party of 7 with professionalism and he was a warm and funny guy as well. In addition, one of us is severely allergic to nuts (but not peanuts) and he went above and beyond necessity by checking every single dish with the kitchen to make sure which ones she could eat or not. When another table's noodles topped with cashews was placed before her (which she could not eat) the waiter apologized and assured her it was meant for someone else. Hers arrived momentarily. He even automatically checked all the desserts before she even asked as well. So, food: pretty good. Atmosphere: great. Service: outstanding. I'd go back. Make sure you're dressed to impress.

I had no idea what to expect when my colleagues made reservations at Buddakan for a dinner with clients, but I think I had the best experience possible. First of all, I recommend going here with a good-sized group (5-10 people) so you can take advantage of the family-sized portions and experience a variety of dishes. I think I would have been disappointed if I went with only one or two other people. As for the food, the edamame dumplings are great and my dining companions raved about the short ribs, lobster spring rolls, and deviled tuna tartare. We sampled the whole Peking duck, chilled udon noodles, vegetable rice, spiced tofu with cashews and eggplant, and several beef dishes. Everything was really good, cooked perfectly, and plated beautifully. Leave room for dessert and if the spice cake is still on the menu, try it. It came with ice cream, a small piece of cake, and a delicately fried apple, I believe. Good wine and saki selection, too. Oh, and it's just as beautiful inside as everyone described. Be careful though - the dishes add up!!!
