I didn't specifically made a dinner reservation because this was THE rehearsal dinner spot for Carrie and Big @ the Sex and The City movie.But as soon as I stepped out of the lounge and into the dining area, I was stunned.The sight was oh so familiar - the staircase leading into the basement dining room, the long table with four chandeliers and the high vaulted ceiling. Still I had doubts - not until another friend made the guess did I do what I do best: google and wiki the hell out of everything, and there, I found my answer.Even without the pizzazz, additional credential and instant recognition brought upon this place by the SATC movie, I still loved the experience. The restaurant represents everything about Manhattan: the tres-chic sophistication, good food (lobster fried rice, mildly spicy szechuan-crusted rib eye and glazed alaskan black cod, and then crying chocolate as finale) and drinks, beautiful people - everything that makes you feel a million dollar for a few hours. Something I would gladly pay for.
Admitted, I'm not a New Yorker--spoiled by all of the plenty that surrounds the city. But I was a bright-eyed graduate intern in the city for just three months, and I made it my business to try every restaurant I possible could (and 7 pounds later, you can see I meant business).Buddakan is one of my favorite restaurants in the city.  Yes, it's a little big and touristy, but the food is amazing! And the drinks are fantastic! We started off with a couple of fizzy fruity cocktails, with blueberries playfully floating on top. Next we went into appetizers--tuna tartar and sweet pea gyoza. The tuna was smooth and buttery, and the avocado had been picked at the peak of ripeness. And the gyoza--never had I imagined that putting peas inside of a potsticker would be delicious, but whoa! Next was entree--after those two hard-hitters I decided to go light with a tofu-veggie stir-fry. The tofu was lightly browned, smooth and yummy paired with the crisp flavorful vegetables. My boyfriend ordered the hot pot which was a savory blend of broth, seafood and vegetables.Then the big show--we innocently ordered the donuts, thinking we would get a small nibble to end the meal. No. Instead they bring us 5 piping hot sugary donuts, paired with homemade ice cream and delicious citrusy sauce. These donuts were one of the best desserts I have ever had--order them!
I went here with my girlfriend for her birthday dinner expecting a really top notch dinner at an expensive restaurant. The decor inside is incredibly nice and expansive. Waitstaff was quick and friendly.However...I was looking through the dishes and just saw what I've known as regular ass chinese food. We ordered frog legs, the full peking duck, and crab fried rice and they were just regular ass chinese food that I've eaten at places substantially cheaper AND better in Flushing and Chinatown. I'm not sure if I walked into this restaurant with the wrong mindset, or if I'm just a biased Chinese boy but I figured a restaurant expensive as this would have mindblowing renditions of what I saw as Chinese restaurant staples. However, I am not trying to discount this restaurant as bad, as the dishes themselves were in fact tasty but for the amount I payed, I could've gotten better food at a Flushing location for half the price and double the portion.

Easily the best Chinese food I've ever eaten!  Hands down!Although this place is quite expensive, our party decided to bite the bullet and go for it.  The restaurant itself it quite chic and tastefully ornate, complete with ambient lighting and grand murals.  The service is impeccable, and our sharp, sociable waiter never missed a beat.As food is concerned, I'd call this place a "P. Maybe I just had really high expectations. As an avid Top Chef watcher, I've been wanting to try this restaurant for ages (I was a big fan of Dale!). I was super excited when my friend scored a reservation for 7 people on a Sunday night. The restaurant itself is beautiful. We walked down the grand stairs, and were seated at the large communal table. Felt like kings and queens!The food, unfortunately, definitely disappointed:- Edamame Dumplings: Didn't expect the filling to be a mushy puree, but still pretty darn good- Deviled Tuna Tartare: Nice play on deviled eggs. I was pretty surprised when I bit into the tartare, expecting to taste avocado. Except it was egg whites covered in a green sauce. My friend found a tiny eggshell in his though...- Pork Belly Buns: Unfortunately I'm a pescetarian, but my friends all enjoyed this dish. Most agreed that Ippudo's are better- Miso Cod: Tender, melt in your mouth. Probably my favorite of the night- Monkfish: Recommended by the waiter. A definite NO. It was drenched in the oily kung pao sauce that you get with your Panda Express chicken. The sauce was so overpowering that I couldn't even taste the fish. - Lamb Chops: Didn't try this either, but some said this was the best lamb chops they've ever had!- Lobster Fried Rice: $19... for fried rice... with not much lobster... not worth it- Mushroom Chow Fun: Drenched in soy sauce... and the noodles were all stuck together! Definitely go to Chinatown for some real chow funsCocktails were okay. I got the Tranquility... couldn't taste any alcohol in it though.Maybe people come here more for the ambiance rather than the food. But if you're going to make me spend over $50 on very little food, the food better be good.

We chose Buddakan with high expectations to impress some very special friends of ours that were in the city for a long weekend. Upon arriving, we were seated in a brightly lit room with no ambiance whatsoever.  We were moved quickly to an area with a bit more "atmosphere."  I will give credit where it is due - the staff was lovely and accomodating.Once we were seated at our new and improved table, I couldn't help but notice we were crammed in like sardines.  Once the table next to us sat, it truly felt as though we were dining with them.  At that point, the trouble of relocating was not worth it.  We just guzzled our cocktails and got on with enjoying ourselves.The food definitely redeemed Buddakan's reputation.  Can't miss appetizers:  Edemame dumplings in shallot-sauternes broth; Duck Spring Rolls with foie gras  passion fruit dip; Chili Rock Shrimp with toasted ginger and my favorite:  the amazing Scallion Pancakes with braised beef short rib and green apple.  Dinner:  Charred Filet of Beef with wonton crisps and mustard sauce;   Sweet  Sour Chicken with bell peppers, snow peas and tempura; Wild Mushroom Chow Fun with garlic chives and my favorite:  the Dungeness Crab Stick Rice, served in the crab shell with x.o. sauce and Chinese broccoli.Dessert:  You cannot miss the Crying Chocolate with malted white chocolate ganache (which "cried" out of the chocolate cake once you put your fork into it) and coffee ice cream.    The food was very good, it just didn't knock our socks off.  We left feeling as though we had gone to an overdone and trendy Chinese restaurant.  It was a decent dining experience, but I wouldn't rush back there.  Definitely good for a cocktail in an ecelctic and unique atmosphere.
Buddakan is one of my go to restaurants, especially when I'm with friends from out of town.  The place is enormous, cool layout  design, has a great bar scene, beautiful crowd, and great food.  Everything is served "family style", but the portions are relatively small.  This isn't like Carmine's, where an order of calamari could feed an army.  My advice is to try at least 4-5 apps, and 2 entrees for dinner.  Yes, it's a scene, and no longer the new hot spot it was a few years ago, but who cares?   Went last week with a group of six, and ordered the following:  Edamame DumplingsTuna Tartare Spring RollsBeef CupsSpare RibsScallion Pancake w/ Short RibsMiso CodSweet  Sour ShrimpBeef TenderloinThe sauce that comes with the beef is ridiculous.  I could pour it over pretty much anything, and it would immediately make it taste better. I'm not crazy about the deserts, but I happen to like the sorbet, which is unusual because I'm typically not a sorbet guy.
This place is wonderful!  when i have friends coming to nyc from another country on holiday or visiting, i usually take them here if their looking for a good looking place with good atmosphere because of the decor and ambiance of this place.  the food is surprisingly not pricey at all and quite good for asian fusion cuisine.  and if you order alcohol (other than beer), the drinks are surprisingly strong, a BIG +!  every meal i've had here was very good, i haven't had an unpleasant meal yet!the best section to be if you just want to lounge around with a couple of friends is either the gold room or the entrance lounge.  the best section to be if you have a large number of people or you want to eat the meals on the menu is the great room or the Buddha room.
We had a terrific meal at Buddakan tonight.  We took the recommendation from other yelpers and started off with the chili rock shrimp and edamame dumplings - the two paired well together - the shrimp were slightly spicy and so fresh.  Eating the edamame dumplings afterwards helped ease the heat.  I usually eat edamame out of the pods so this was a nice alternative - the edamame in the steamed dumplings were creamy yet so fresh...I haven't had anything quite like them before. For our meal, we had the pepper beef and broken chili chicken - both were tasty - the chicken was a whole breast sliced delicately with a Thai basil/pepper rub - another unique dish.  We also enjoyed the vegetable rice with  coconut curry foam - the foam is separated from the rice when presented - the curry is not overwhelming - this is an excellent accompaniment to the main dish.  The snap peas were also delicious.  I wasn't that crazy about my cocktail - reflection which included pineapple and rum - I thought it would be slightly sweeter than it was - it wasn't sweet.  My friend got the charm cocktail which includes passion fruit liqueur, berries, apples, and prosecco - that tasted better - the berries were the dominant flavor in that drink.  Service was great.  Atmosphere reminded me of Tao but a little less noisy and without the giant Buddha.

This was quite possibly the best meal I have ever had in my entire life.  My friend and I went here on Valentine's Day and the ONLY disappointing thing was that even though we had made reservations, we ended up having to wait 30 minutes...BUT it was totally worth it!  I had the drink called "Charm" which was GREAT but tasted a little like cough medicine.  For appetizers we had the General Tso's Dumplings which were SOOOO good and then we also had the Chili Rock Shrimp which was delicious (kinda like Bang Bang Shrimp from Bonefish Grill).  For dinner my friend ordered the Lamb Chops and I ordered the Kung Pao Monkfish.  I have never had a better entree in my entire life out of ALL the restaurants I have been to!  The fish was cooked perfectly, the amount of sauce was perfect, the amount of spice was perfect, there is just no other word besides perfect!!  We also ordered a side of the Twice Cooked Long Beans which we both polished off.  For dessert they had a special of a flourless chocolate cake with a scoop of vanilla ice cream with an orange glaze.  I will be coming back to this restaurant every time I visit NYC!  And the fact that Carrie's rehearsal dinner from the Sex  the City movie was filmed here is just icing on top of the cake :)

Walking up the stairs to the huge lounge area is just a taste of what is inside. We ate in the lounge cause like momos we did not make reservations well in advance but regardless we enjoyed it. So here goes....ServiceOur waitress Laurel was awesome. Very attentive, great smile, excellent attitude, and no pushy when taking our order (i.e. she gave us enough time to look over the menu). The bus boys are great as well... very non-intrusive when clearing your plates. Look and FeelThe place is massive and so eye catching. DrinksThe drink selection was great... the wines, mixed... all of it was greatPriceAnd it all comes down to this. For 5 apps, 3 entrees, one side, 3 desserts, 8+ drinks = $299 (tax, no tip). An average of $75 per person. Not bad considering the food, service, and place. OverallLike I said, we are going back in 2 weeks. Its some of the best food we ave had in a while and worth the price. I admit that I am harsh towards asian restaurants. Budakkan offers typical asian fusion food. There are some bright spots, and great food, but the food is by no means good enough to justify the prices. Yes, I think it is overpriced. I'm not one to complain about the price, but I think that Buddakan charges the way it does because we allow it to. Sure the place is pretty, but the service is mediocre at best. We made reservations for 11:45 on a Friday, and we were sent to wait by the bar for 30 minutes before we were seated. We had the edemame dumplings, and I simply do not understand the love it gets here. Maybe my palate is not accustomed enough, but the texture and taste was weird. Salty with some sweetness and mushy covered by mushy served over sauce. We had the short ribs and fried rice, and they were both good enough. Would I go back, no. There are far better restaurants in NYC.

It's expensive Chinese food, but I like it. The place is gorgeous, especially the chandelier filled room that was in the Sex  the City movie. I have to eat in that room next time. And unlike typical Chinese food places, the service was excellent.We started off with the Edamame Dumplings, which we were told was the most popular appetizer. It was alright. It's creative and I like the use of truffle oil in it, but I thought it was a little dry. Next came the deconstructed pork belly buns. 5 pieces of pork to put into 5 piping hot buns. Garnish with spicy cabbage that's similar to what my grandmother makes at home. The meat was okay.  The hoisin glaze made them better. For my main entree, I had the King Crab Hot Pot. I was a bit worried that eating crab in front of my date would not be pretty, but the chefs were ahead of me on this one.  The crab legs were cut into smaller pieces and split in half so the meat could be easily pulled out. Phew. It's not really a hot pot of broth and stuff floating around. It's thicker like a stew. Nevertheless, it was very flavorful and had a nice kick to it.For dessert, we had the coconut custard cake. Skip this one. It didn't have enough coconut flavors to warrant it's name. There was a small custard cake, a fritter thing, and creamsicle ice cream. I didn't like the combination. It was too tart for a coconut dessert. I think our waiter noticed my distaste and explained that it was a new item. He also took it off our bill. Next time, I have to try the Peking Duck and the taro lollipops.

Concerning the service, our waiter was friendly to a point, where his smile was - just a little - creepy... but he was very attentive and we were never left wanting for anything.First of all, the cocktails. We had to wait for our table, and ordered some drinks at the bar in the front, but as soon as they stood in front of us, and we wanted to take the first sip, somebody came to show us to our table. We then found out,  that you have to pay for everything you consume at the bar separately, before you move to your table, which made for kind of a rush, since the waitress was already standing next to us looking rather impatient. But the cocktails were excellent! Especially the 'Lush', made with sake, lychee, gin and rosemary...On to the food - I know that some really seem to like the edamame dumplings, but I can not relate... I'm usually not a big fan of Asian fusion because most places have an identity crisis and are not capable of making dishes as good as their authentic counterparts, BUT I am a big fan of Buddakan.Let's start from the very beginning. I usually HATE waiting to get seated, but considering we got there early, the drinks were delicious, and the other patrons were all good looking, I didn't mind too much. Once I walked in, I was amazed at how large this restaurant was. It could pass as a club. We walked down the stairs to a very open area with a communal table. I guess that's cool if you're into that thing. We were seated in the back room, which I preferred much more.So onto the food. We got the most creative dishes on the menu since one of my friends told us that the more traditional dishes were not up to par with authentic restaurants (as per my original dislike for Asian fusion). Edamame dumplings - was not a fan. I like texture in my food, and this had NONE. I had my hopes up because people called it gyoza. FALSE. Gyoza has a crispy exterior. This did not. The dumpling was steamed and had a thick skin (also another reason why I did not like it). Tuna spring roll - The BEST dish by far. But be warned because they're tiny. It's basically a tube of crispy spring roll skin filled with spicy tuna tartare. I loved the crunch of the spring roll with the fresh tuna and a hint of spice.Chili rock shrimp - Good, but nothing special here. Just fried rock shrimp with a chili sauce. Lobster fried rice - Quite delicious! I even tasted a hint of kewpie mayonnaise, which I like to do at home. It sounds weird, but quite awesome when done right.Dungeness crab sticky rice - I liked this better than the lobster fried rice. It's like the traditional dim sum sticky rice that come in bamboo leaves, but with a spin. Lots of crab and the sticky rice is a bit harder. Great presentation too. The fried rice came in the shell of the crab. Short ribs - mediocre. The short ribs were very tender, but they were over-sauced/too salty. Small cubes of fresh pear provided a good balance to the heaviness of the dish and also gave it texture.Crying chocolate - nothing to write home about. I have a hard time remembering exactly what it even was...Chocolate peanut butter bombe - also had a lot more excitement for this dish than it ended up being. The ice cream was just meh. Overall two thumbs up from me! AND it didn't break the bank. Nice.

The atmosphere is amazing, the food is "good"... but way way way overpriced.  I had to give the rating a 2 stars b/c you can get comparable food for 1/4 the price.Here's a list of what we had:=Appetizers=* Edamame dumplings - GREAT. the best thing we had.  very delicate, soft and creamy.  It had a very mild subtle flavor.  the broth they served it with was a perfect compliment.* Chili rock shrimp - OK. it was good but nothing special.  it was very well fried, not greasy.... and lathered with the mayo and sriracha sauce, the same sauce used in spicy tuna rolls, etc.=Entree=* Peking duck - GOOD. it was the whole duck, so i was expecting to eat just a bit of it and take most of it home... but the serving size was much smaller than I thought.  it is served with all of the bones and fat removed.  It had great flavor but the meat was a bit on the dry side and the skin was not crispy.  I prefer my duck fatty.* Lobster fried rice - GOOD. not greasy and tasty. the rice was a bit on the dry side which i like in fried rice.=Dessert=* Apple cider doughnuts - HORRIBLE.  the doughnuts were cold and dry and didn't taste that good.  But the creme fraiche ice cream it was served with was great.

Overhyped.This is a good place to take someone visiting NYC who wants to go to a sceney, impressive place.  It's huge.  It's cool.  It's filled with beautiful people and is decorated in impressive and enormous scale.But it's expensive.  The entrees range from the mid-twenties to thirties for SMALL entrees without any sides.  I ordered the spicy shrimp for $25, and was told I may want to order a side to go with that because ALL that came with the 5 shrimp on the place was a few sliced radishes.  So I changed my order to the sliced duck with noodles in broth.  Also about $25, but at least you can call it a meal.  It was good... but not really much better than the nearly same dish at Republic for half the price.She got the tofu with mixed vegetables, which looked good but not significantly different from your local Chinese food place's dish.We got veggie dumplings, and they were good and fine... but nothing special.  They were cute in that they sort of resembled red peppers (red dough with bits of scallion sticking out the top).  I liked that the veggies were coarsely chopped enough to still be recognizable.It's not bad, it's just overrated and overpriced.  NYC has many, many better places.

I rang in my 23rd year of existence here with a big group of girlfriends. The restaurant was absolutely amazing when it came to dealing with my reservation situation. I originally started out with a group of 5. Then it turned to 4. Wait! Back up to 5! Then on the day of, it changed to 6. Wait scratch that, now 5. Hold on, now it's 7... Ahh I wanted to tear my hair out! I felt SO SO bad every time I called but the reservation girl was such an angel. Of course to make things worse a few people showed up late. No worries, Buddakan to the rescue! They still gave us a great table downstairs right past the main dining room (which is gorgeous by the way). I am kind of picky when it comes to Asian fusion but Buddakan is one of the better fusion places I've been to. For a group of 7 girls we ordered: edamame dumplings, tuna spring rolls, chili crab and crispy noodles, crap fried rice, sizzling short rib, and the glazed alaskan black cod. Not everyone was a fan of the edamame dumplings - the texture is a little weird. It's just one of those things you love or don't love. I happened to love it! The tuna spring rolls were NOT worth it. They are literally two 3 inch long spring rolls with spicy tuna in them. I loved the short rib (really flavorful) and the black cod. I feel like all that food we ordered was good for our group size. But  a few girls were left a tiny bit hungry. I think if we ordered one more main dish, then that would've been perfect.Of course a birthday is not a birthday unless someone from your dinner party whispers really loudly to the waiter "It's her birthday!!! Can you bring her a dessert?" The fried doughnuts we got were freakin tasty. Within about five minutes the plate was empty. I'm so glad I celebrated my birthday at Buddakan! Compared to all the other meat packing restaurants, I'd say Buddakan is the place to go hands down.

DELICIOUS! I'm always skeptical about Chinese fusion places (since I'm Taiwanese Chinese) that are overpriced with wanna be "Chinese" food, especially with a name like Buddakan. However, I was pleasantly surprised to find the dishes truly creative! The taro and minced pork lollipops were very cute and good. I enjoyed the butternut squash dumplings and the beef lettuce cups. The short rib scallion cakes were a bit too salty, as was the short rib entree. The lobster dish was pretty good, but I enjoyed the small plates the most. The decor is truly amazing. You walk in and see and bar and imagine the rest of the restaurant to look the same, sleek and modern. However, you hang a left and you see a dining room 30 feet below! It's huge downstairs! Minus the rude idiots seated next to us, Buddakan is a great special occasion dining spot!
First time at Buddakan. Very impressive decor...upon entering there is an enormous tapestry behind a reception desk to the right with 5 or 6 host/hostesses waiting to greet you. Why do they need so many people was the question running through my mind. We had a reservation and were seated quickly after being asked to wait at the bar. The place is dark and modern, with many nooks and crannies. The street level tables look down over a cavernous lower level with one of the largest tables I've ever seen surrounded by smaller dining tables. I image they must have communal seating at that large table but we sat on the upper level. Our waitress was very charming and accommodating. We had a diner with food allergies and she was eager to help us in any way she could. We ordered the edamame dumplings and general tso's dumplings for appetizers as we were told dishes come out as they are ready and are meant for sharing. The edamame dumplings were a standout with a creamy smooth filling. For entrees we had the charred filet of beef, Mongolian lamb chops, minced pork lo mein, shrimp and lobster chow fun and lobster fried rice. I thought the lo mein was ordinary but the other dishes were fabulous. The beef came with a side of garlic butter that everyone was fighting over!For dessert we tried the crying chocolate, almond bread pudding and sorbets. The bread pudding was the best of the three.

If you're from Queens or Jersey, GO HERE!If only to keep you from intruding on the rest of the city.I'm kidding (ok I'm not), but seriously, the biggest issue with Buddakan is the crowd and location. The food is decent, if unoriginal and lacking any real creative inspiration. The main dining room is of course spectacular, but unfortunately it's all spoiled by the nightclub vibe and mediocre service stemming from it. Because of it's prime douchebag-centric location in the Meatpacking district, here you can find a mix of investment bankers trying desperately to appear cool as well as wide-eyed tourists and bridge-and-tunnel freakshows seeking a 'New York' experience. It all combines to form something less than desirable in a culinary outing.It may be a decent choice for a quick after-work meal or drinks, but I'll be skipping it for anything more than that.

The food and service are always top notch.  This place is quintessential NYC - I love the hotel lobby style check-in.  This place is definitely worth a visit if you are in the mood for Chinese/Asian fusion and perfect for a light dinner before going out.  It is on the pricier side but worth every penny IMO!
Coming here was an exciting prospect. I had been invited to a tasting dinner by a chef. Not only would I get to sample a trendy Meatpacking hot spot, but in the company of the people who are so talented at bringing food to that extra degree of taste we normal cooks aspire to go to. The short story: mixed bag, most dishes disappointing apart from a few highlights. The good: edamame dumplings are ridiculously yummy. After a night of drinking, I could mow through a plateful of those and forget any social obligation to share. Equally yummy were a pork belly bun, bok choy-wrapped sea bass, and crab fried rice. (My fellow diners also liked a tuna tartare spring roll and soup dumpling.)The marginal: a glazed beef ribeye, and a crispy chili chicken. While the beef was finely prepared, the sauce seemed to have too much hoisin. And the chicken was good, but seemed like an ordinary dish for Buddakan to serve. The no--thanks: a fried croquet that wasn't potato, but turnip. Another dish of pork belly was dry. Dessert was ginger flan (?), a combination I hope to never eat again. Sorbets were not that awesome; while not poor, I was surprised this was what Buddakan was serving. Though there were loads of criticisms made around me, I'm inclined to look at my experience kindly regardless. There are some good eats to be found here at Buddakan, simple things that remind me of trips to Hong Kong and creativity that works well when it does (I still want edamame dumplings). And, the service is impeccable. But, I'm just as content going to a cart for the same pleasures, and don't feel I need to spend a lot of money. Were it not for the fact that I got to hang out with chefs, I would be bitter over the amount I paid for dinner. (But, I'm still mildly annoyed at getting stuck paying for other people's cocktails. Feh.)

Aesthetically pleasing would be the way to describe Buddakan. Upon entrance of the restaurant, you already see swanky large doors and a dark interior setting. Buddakan is spacious- it has a dining hall downstairs and everything in it screams New York panache. The bar has awkward minimalistic stools that can hurt your butt, but don't fear fellow yelpers! The fabulous bartenders will make you an out of this world great drink called Fate. It's a delicious drink with three components- elderflower, pineapple juice, and prosecco. This bubbly and sparkly drink oozes with yumminess. It actually might be my favorite drink ..for now that is!The food here is definitely worth trying. Lobster fried rice had big chunks of juicy lobster and the rice was lightly fried. Wok fried tofu with broccoli was another hit. Slivers of garlic tainted the broccoli and tofu in just the right amounts and touches of seared tofu had our taste buds tantalized. It is definitely East meets West.One weird thing I wanted to share is that when I went to the restrooms upstairs, I was a bit confused and creeped out. There is a portrait of a 17th century Frenchman.  Aren't we in an Asian fused restaurant? AND I'm trying to use the restroom, his creepy eyes were not cool.
Think this might be one of the few restaurants out there that is actually better than the original. To be clear, I actually love the Buddakan in Philadlphia (not so much the one in AC...), but the one in NYC inches out ahead. The space is the first thing that's noticeably different. While they both have similar decors, the NYC one is just a lot bigger and there are actually separate areas (versus having the entire experience be in one room). Even as a large party, we were able to secure a location that was relatively quiet without renting a private room - pretty sure you can't pull that off in the Philadelphia counterpart. The NYC menu also has a lot more choices than the one in Philly. Think we actually ordered all of the hot appetizers, and they were all strong to quite strong. The favorites of the table were the lollipops, edamame dumplings and the tuna tartar springroll. Consensus was that the appetizers were a better value than many of the entrees, so we would advise ordering more appetizers you would at a typical restaurant and maybe just splitting an entree or two. I can't comment on price since it was on the corporate card, but the prices seemed fair for the quality, location and service. I'd recommend this place for large group outings celebrating special occasions.
My boyfriend and I decided to check out Buddakan one night when we were seeing a show in the city. We are both HUGE fans of all varieties of Asian food and fusion, so this seemed right up our ally. We like trying new things, so we asked the waiter for his recommendations. Every suggestion that he made was perfect. The best bite of the night was the pork-belly dim-sum, which is served with steamed buns. It was INCREDIBLE. We ordered two appetizers, two entrees and rice to share. We completely over-ordered. The prices are up there, but if you are careful not to order too much (as we did) the bill is completely manageable for the experience you will have.The house cocktails are pretty delicious too ::wink::

I find a lot of Manhattan restaurants more interested in a trendy atmosphere than good food.  (I'm talking about you, Butter, Kitty Chai, Susha Samba.)  Buddakan combines both.  The atmosphere is very cool.  Very Hogwarts-y, and plus, for Sex and the City fanatics (ahem: me!), this was where Big and Carrie had their engagement party.  Needless to say, it's a great date place and also a great place to hang out with your girlfriends. Food-wise, I think the appetizeres really steal the show here.  Love the taro lollipops, the tartare eggrolls are prob. my faves.  The entrees are good too, but nothing too special.  I still order them because the appetizers and entres are roughly the same prize, and the entres (esp. the noodles/rice dishes) are much more filling.

We were "escorted out," but I love Buddakan.  Our show ran late so we rolled in an hour late for a 10p reservation.  Immediately and without judgment, they swooshed us through the crazed bar, down the multi-tiered steps to the gilded Grand Room with a single table running 50 feet flanked by rich art tableau on the ends.  White-linen topped banquettes filled with happy diners line the garish walls.  Within seconds, our party was satiated with wines, specialty cocktails and good ole Stoli.  The vixen twins (we had two servers decked in body defining black) quickly had appetizers and entrees ordered with skillful recommendations on crowd-favorites for flavor and the amount to order.  (The service is family style.)  Tuna sashimi eggrolls, popcorn shrimp with a kick and a couple of other starters quickly arrived.  Glasses remained topped.  The entrees began to flow - flank steak with the most delicious brown-butter soy sauce, moist snapper, well-prepared scallops, maybe some fried rice.  I think we may have had dessert but things begin to get blurry about now.  Looking around, we realize we are the only people left in the recently-filled laughter-echoing room.  We're deep in meaningless conversation and indulgently finishing our final round when a bouncer arrives and hovers next to our table.  Large, jovial guy who stayed on message: "Get out," so we can lock the doors.  This is my third time at Buddakan, which never fails to deliver on food or ambiance.  I've never understood why anyone would subjugate themselves to the cramped quarters of the bar though.  The steak is par excellence, and the tab is always surprisingly lower than expected.  I hope to get thrown out of more places like this.

Really, really good food, but make reservations.  We arrived on Saturday evening at 10 PM and were informed that without a reservation our best bet was to try and grab a sit in the bar area (first come, first serve).  It was packed and dimly lit, which made spotting an opening an added challenge and mildly stressful. The table we finally scored was not ideal for the intimate meal we had envisioned, but the food was certainly worth the wait.  The menu has an asian fusion flair and we found each dish to be this divine assemblage of flavors.  We enjoyed the Tuna Tartare and the Char Siu Roast Pork, among other dishes.  Luckily the room was really loud or else our neighbors would have been slightly distracted by the cacophony of "ohhs and ahhs" coming from our table.  I mean, the meal was dynamite.  I also concluded my meal with a lovely cup of tea (rooibos tea with hints of rose and almond flavors).So definitely a place worth checking out.  But call ahead for reservations and know going in that the place will be loud.  If you are looking for a low-lit, quiet place, this isn't the restaurant for that experience.

This is the best Asian Fusion I've tasted so far.The place is obviously overpriced and you can't come here regularly but the food has such good strong tastes and flavors you won't regret splurging the one night out.  I enjoyed the food overall as Asian dishes tend to be very oily, greasy and heavy on the stomach but this place does so well in making sure the food tastes fresh and clean. I didn't feel gross walking out of the place which is always a huge plus.The ambiance is so chic and trendy. They're famous for their huge main room with communal table (The scene at Carrie's Engagement Party in the Sex and the City movie was filmed here!). You wouldn't expect the place to be so spacious when walking in since the outside of the of building looks like a standard black warehouse building.  They did really well to work with their space and the main rooms are accessed by walking down steep stairs to a lower level straight into the communal room and other side rooms that have extra seating.The restaurant suggests ordering family style so our group ordered the following starters and entrees (with my thoughts on each!).:APPETIZERS:Cantonese Spring Rolls - Nothing too much to rave about. Tasted pretty good with the nice blend of shrimp and chicken.Hoisin Glazed Pork Belly - The flavors were very good but the Pork Belly is very fatty. It may not appeal to some squeamish eaters who don't like food with mushy/squishy consistencyCrispy Calamari Salad - Top notch. The apples gave it a slight sweet and sour flavor with an added crisp and the cashews balanced out all the tangy/salty/sweet tastes.Chili Rock Shrimp - Pretty good. Like the way they cook their shrimp. Not too overcooked.Edamame Dumplings - This was just average for me. Just mashed Edamame in a dumpling. Still tasted good but I wouldn't order again.Tuna Tartar Spring Roll - Really good. An interesting play on a classic dish.MAIN DISHES:Sizzling Short Rib - This was tender and juicy and loved the Mushroom Chow Fun sideWhole Crispy Fish - The presentation on this was beautiful! The fish tasted amazing, not too dry and not too undercooked. Sweet and Sour Chicken - Did not taste like the typical Sweet and Sour Chicken dish, which is a good thing. It was a toned down version with much better flavors.Glazed Alaskan Black Cod - Good!! Once again, fish was perfectly cooked.SIDES:Chinese Sausage Fried Rice - Pretty good but the Chinese sausage taste didn't come out as strong for me. Lapchurn has a very distinct flavor and it was missing a bit there.Vegetable Rice - Pretty standard. The Coconut Foam was interesting to look at but didn't contribute to the flavor of the dish.DESSERT:Crying Chocolate - My favorite of the threeGinger Spice Doughnuts - Very good. Not too sweet and not too greasy.Chocolate Peanut Butter Bombe  - This was just average for me since I'm not a huge peanut butter fan but everyone else LOVED it.

Buddakan is the Meatpacking District equivalent to Midtown's Tao - big, over-the-top, pricey and a well-heeled crowd.  You can easily miss it - across the street from the Maritime hotel in a large black warehouse-looking building with a small lacquered sign.  It's quite the experience, and I'd have been satisfied with a selection of appetizers alone - actually, I feel like appetizer-only sampler is the way to go.With a date, this would be a better pick than Tao, as the variety of seating and slightly more intimate atmosphere lend to a better conversation spot - while still impressing a new interest or group of friends with an upscale pick in a trendy neighborhood.  Get 2 orders of the Rock Shrimp - I could eat these every single day and never get sick of them - as well as the General Tso Dumplings.  These are absolute, can't miss dishes.Also highly recommended are the Edamame Dumplings and Lobster Spring Rolls - these choices all sound similar, but I swear, they're all unique enough to try.  Cocktail selection is as girly as it gets.

The service is exceptional and the decor and ambience are great.  See you next month.

Anyways, the drinks (particularly the named ones - Lush, Fever, Spice) were sufficiently delicious to distract me from our late seating; more than 30 minutes after our reservation. After being guided through the labyrinthine basement, we sat down and watched our waiter recite his "recommendations." One of my pet peeves is when you ask for a personal food recommendation, and get an (admittedly enthusiastic) reading of a prepared script. Definitely order the edamame dumplings, and stay far, far away from the disappointing and ridiculously salty vegetables with 1000-layer tofu and the whole peking duck.Finally, Crying Chocolate has to be the strangest name for a dessert I've ever seen. "What kind of food DON'T you like?" asks my friend. "Asian Fusion," comes my quick reply. It's true:  I'm extremely, extremely wary of Asian Fusion cuisine. More often than not, it screams gimmick and is more a sign of chef's whimsy than artistic rendition of a cultural dish. Buddakan is a love-hate, hit-or-miss, take-it-or-leave-it kind of place. The main dining hall with grand ceilings and dripping wax candles certainly has its wow factor, but I wouldn't want to share that long banquet table that could fit a small army of diners. I've never felt so modest to have a dress go all the way mid-thigh. The food. There are only two reasons why I go back to Buddakan repeatedly: 1) Edamame dumplings. They could be on my plate every day of the year and I would still crave more of them. The most boring sounding dish is brilliant upon first bite. Believe the hype. 2) Desserts. Peanut Butter Bombe is incredibly light and refined, and might be the most delicate version of these heavy flavors I've tasted to date. The signature Crying Chocolate is for true chocolate lovers, better shared between 2-4 friends if only to eat more of the other desserts. Granted, my friend used to be a pastry chef here and I first came to pay my respects, but I've gone back for the PB bombe and the Edamame dumplings.  Not quite a solid bet for everything, but as a pre- or post-dinner (note my next review for Morimoto) supplement, I could eat my words about Asian Fusion for some more of those dumplings.

I went to Buddakan for dinner with my girlfriend a few nights ago.  The restaurant is pretty interesting inside, with a lot of space and high ceilings, although I found it a bit too dark.  They serve dishes "tapas-style" (the waiter's description), although I think the dishes were larger than typical tapas.The food was good.  We ordered two entrees: Charred Filet of Beef (pretty good, but I think that was mostly due to the butter sauce they poured over the top) and Kung Pao Monkfish (good but not memorable); and three side dishes: Chinese Sausage Fried Rice (good), Sugar Snap Peas (ok), and Chili Rock Shrimp (awesome).  If you're being strategic about your dinner and want to maximize your food for the money, get the fried rice - that alone could have filled us up and it was only $10.  Also, don't feel like you have to order an entree for each person - they expect you to share those as well, and the entrees are generally much more expensive than the appetizers and side dishes without offering much more food.The service at Buddakan was fine, although they didn't come by to fill our glasses of water for the entire meal, until we flagged someone down at the end.  No big deal, but worth noting if you care about that sort of thing.I'd definitely go back to Buddakan again, and if I did I'd order less food and save room for dessert (which sounds great according to other Yelp reviews).

"Kinda like Tao, but with better food."                                                         - Wifey-"Reminds me of Spice Market, but with prettier people."                                                          -Me-Pan-Asian joints have become so chic lately.  When they're done well, you'll get a great meal, a sleek Eastern atmosphere, and a lotta jealous friends who wished they were Asian too.When these joints are done badly, I hide my head in shame and try to convince people that I'm not Chinese, but Eskimo.Fortunately, Buddakan is a place that lives up to the hype.  And you'd better believe there's a lotta hype surrounding this place.  For starters, it's one of many establishments owned by the Starr Restaurant group.  A group known for glitzy, trendy, and high-profile eateries across the US.Confirming Buddakan as an "it" place, waves of models, well-heeled financiers, and general glitteratti seem to flock to its nouveau, buddha-inspired "chinoiserie".Wifey and I walked in at 6pm on a Thursday night.The bar was packed.PACKED!Packed with all the model-quality beautiful people that New York had to offer - and a couple of homely ones thrown in just to make the pretty people seem all the more gorgeous.Typically, a demographic of this type is not a good omen for the food.Wifey and I confirmed our reservation with the requisite vacuous blonde at the desk and decided to forgo the monstrous line at the coat check area.  The ditzy blonde then told us to wait at the bar and that someone would be along to get us.  These seemingly simple instructions take on new meaning when you actually walk into the endless hoards of people at the bar and wonder how they'll actually find you.The seating ritual at Buddakan is absolutely the most inefficient and haphazard system I've ever witnessed at a restaurant.  While you're patiently waiting amongst the boisterous and tipsy crowd at the bar, these poor girls wander around aimlessly with nothing but a tiny piece of paper with your last name scribbled on it.  The girls feebly call out random names hoping for a hit, but their delicate blonde voices are drowned out by the din of hipsters juiced up on lychee-infused vodka.If these young waifs finally manage to find you amidst the din and chaos, you are led into an ornate, 2-story chandelier-swinging dining hall of immense proportion.  There is a huge communal dining table in the center of the room with more of the aforementioned glitteratti feasting on pan-Asian treats.The menu is varied, but familiar in its offerings.  You'll be offered fare like potstickers, fried rice, and spring rolls, but they'll be "kicked up a notch" as the banal Emeril Lagasse would say...Whatever the case, those overpriced potstickers and spring rolls will be some of the best you've ever eaten.The food's pretty good.I'll be damned.
I'm not about to argue that you can't find better food for the price.  It's pretty solid asian fusion, but not incredible.  What sets this place apart is the atmosphere.  Between the renaissance painting tapestries, candy colored wooden window fixtures, and taxidermy birds on the walls, you half expect a Quentin Tarentino fight scene to break out in the middle of your meal.  And the giant wooden chandeliers in the banquet room - AWESOME!!!With that said, I did eat a few things there that warrant mentioning.  The clay pot duck was quite delicious, as were the edamame dumplings and tuna tartare.  I also got this dessert that was like a high-brow cider doughnut with ice cream.  Delicious.

Did not disappoint...   Although we had to wait a bit longer for our table then we would have liked (we had a 9:15 reservation and we weren't say until about 9:40), the overall experience was great.While we were waiting, the manager offered to take us to the library bar... if the upstairs bar is as packed as it was last night, I would highly recommend this move.  The downstairs (library) bar was empty, and we had plenty of space to sit and enjoy our drinks.Another recommendation, unless you like very dim light... I'd strongly recommend to ask to be seated in the main room.  The music is not as loud in there, and the lighting is much better.Finally, for the food...  best part of the night.   What we ordered:Edamame dumplings -  As good as advertised.  Everyone really enjoyed them.Pork dumplings --- very good, but not anything amazingBoneless spare ribs -- Great.  Like some of the best fall off the bone ribs you've ever had... but no bone.  Easy to eat with fork and knife (actually no knife needed), with a great sauceRock Shrimp -- Another great dish.   The breading layer is so thin, and it's so lightly dressed in the spicy mayo, you almost forget it's bad for you.  If you like shrimp, this is a great dish (which we all do)Scallion pancakes with braised short ribs and apple -- very good, although not amazing.  The short rib was very good, and was definitely the star.  The scallion pancake was run of the mill... and not very crispy because the beef was piled on top of it.Cod (entree) -- very good.  fell apart with the lightest touch of the fork, and great flavorLobster fried rice -- very good fried rice... with a few chunks of lobster.  The lobster didn't change the flavor all that much, but the fried rice stood on its own.Broken Chili Chicken -- great sauce... definitely the best part.  I spooned it on to my fried rice at the end it was so good.   The chicken is all white meat, light tempura battered (with the skin on) so it's super crispy on the outside...  but the chicken in still incredibly moist (despite being sliced in the kitchen)Bread Pudding   -- everyone liked this, but I actually didn't eat any.... too full from everything else.

My first time here was on a less then perfect date where all three choices(salty crab fried rice, pork belly buns, and sweet and slimy rib tips) almost made me give up on the place for good. I wasn't too thrilled either that I could have literally ate off the plate from the person next to me( and I seriously wanted to, whatever they ordered looked way better then what I had). But I went back to give it another chance and learned that I should choose my own dinner. Both the Edmame and Shrimp dumplings were redemptive enough for my palette to forgive my prior experience. Skip the rice and the carbs and try the charred asparagus as a side instead. I ordered duck for the first time while I was there and now I'm hooked for life! The exquisite design of the dining area close to the stairway rivals the run of the mill dinner experience at Koi or TAO. Unfortunately the red head bartender upstairs is pretty snotty and his mojito's aren't worth drinking but I had one of their specialty cocktails the second time around with lime and rum that complimented my dinner nicely. It's a great place if you want to impress someone or treat yourself to a night out.

I've been here three times so far and every time I've been beyond satisfied with my experience.The place is stunning. Huge layout  with two floors and several rooms. I've eaten only downstairs all three times. The restaurant is absolutely beautiful. Super trendy and hip. You don't have to come swanked out but a lot of people do especially on Fridays and Saturdays.I'll focus more on my second visit for this review because I tried a wider variety of food with my family. Our waiter was great. Very courteous and helpful. He helped us pick a few appetizers which were all excellent. We started off with general tso dumplings, scallion pancakes, and the boneless spare ribs. The dumplings were fantastic. The hot and sour soup in them is a nice surprise to bite into. The ribs were tender and smothered in a delicious sauce, paired with their mustard which is sweet and zingy. The scallion pancakes were great as well! I ordered the Fever cocktail (spicy!) which is definitely one of the more unique cocktails I've ever had. It was a nice addition to my meal.Although the main entrees for this place are intended to be shared, we each ordered one. I ordered the charred filet of beef which was cooked medium, even a little closer to medium rare which is how I prefer my meat. The plating is impeccable here. It arrived with thin and very tasty wonton crisps, their signature mustard, and a savory but sweet sauce that had hints of caramel in it. Needless to say, it was excellent. My sister ordered the black pepper beef which comes in a beautiful, delicate "birds nest." The beef was cooked perfectly and there was a delightful crunchy texture in the vegetables accompanying it. My father, mother, and brother ordered sha cha chicken and broken chili chicken. I didn't try either of these but they were happy with their food. To top it off we ordered the summer peach upside down cake and the bittersweet chocolate mousse pave. The summer peach upside down cake is possibly the greatest dessert I've ever had. The cake was buttery, delicate, and moist. The egg custard ice cream is brulee'd on top and melts nicely with the cake. The bittersweet chocolate mousse pave is not really bittersweet but still amazing. The caramel popcorn sherbet is out of this world. My family still raves about it, months after their visit there. The bill was a little scary but its nice to splurge on a good meal every now and then. My father thought it was well worth it. Not just for the food, but for the overall dining experience that you can't get at any typical restaurant in the city.
[I'd be mortified if I tripped on those stairs leading down to the main dining room =p]Every aspect of this restaurant was appealing. The restaurant is beautiful, the employees were full of smiles, the corner banquet table had the best view, and the food was amazing. Allow me to break it down.For a party of 6, we had:APPSCrispy Calamari Salad - lightly-battered calamari with mix greens in a tangy miso vinaigrette, very basicEdamame Dumplings - unique, the filling was really smoothChili Rock Shrimp - tasty rock shrimp smothered in a sweet and spicy sauce, goodWok Hay Frog Legs - the best of the apps, the best frog legs I ever had. I'm at lost for words to describe it.Boneless Spare Ribs - tender and savory, a delightful classicChili Crab  Crispy Noodles -  sauteed blue crab in chili brown sauce over crispy noodles, the sauce was a little too powerful but I liked the dish nonethelessLobster Fried Rice - very light, no flavorTwice Cooked Long Beans - crisp cut long beans in a minced shrimp oyster-like sauce; so good we ordered a 2ndENTREESzechuan Crusted NY Ribeye - my fave cut done right, thick slices served with hong kong steak sauce and turnip fries (I'd substitute the bbq-like steak sauce)Charred Filet of Beef - tender and perfectly charred; this entree was raved about on yelp but I preferr the rib-eyeSizzling Short Rib - off the bone, similiar to braised brisket, yummy Whole Sea Bass - coated and deeped fried, unfortunately mushy, the veggies were more delectable  DESSERTCrying Chocolate - delicious rich molten cake with a scoop of coffee ice creamCoconut Creme Brulee - very good, a palate cleanser, especially the lemongrass ice creamChocolate Mille Feuille - a stacked dessert of bruleed bananas, ice cream and thin chocolate Jasmine Lemon VerbenaEveryone was satisifed, happy... in euphoria. Definitely a place to return to, especially with guest. Amaze them with the cavernous dining room, attractive design, and good food.

Came here with an eclectic group of friends, of which one was visiting from out of town and appreciates a trendy scene...Buddakan was a great call for this group. The interior is beautiful and we were seated upstairs in a semi-private area which was great. We ordered plenty of app's and entrees and shared them all which worked well. All of the app's were tiny but still tasty...some of the notables include the edamame dumplings, tuna tartare spring rolls, and my favorite the beef lettuce cups. My favorite entree was the charred filet of beef and king crab hot pot was a close second...apparently the vegetable tofu steamed buns were decent, but I didn't save room to try them. Also, I was feeling bold and ventured away from my standard drink (Hendricks and tonic) and opted to try something different from their fun cocktail menu, the Lush, which was ok but reminded me why I have a standard drink. Overall, come for the food and the scene (try to snag a spot downstairs under the gorgeous chandeliers), but not for the portions or the service which was blah, from the (seemingly slow :-/ ) girls at the front to lack luster waitstaff. A close 4 star, but by comparison to the other great places the city has to offer, it's a 3 for me.

Buddakan is fun, fabulous and my first choice where to bring friends from out of town for dinner. It always gives everyone a taste of people watching, creative Asian food and a splash of New York city glamour. The spacious restaurant provides for all settings, either a happening bar, communal dining table with chandeliers, or more private seating in surrounding areas. You've got to try their signature edamame dumplings, plus the cabbage wrapped seabass and peking style, spicy pork belly for the adventurous. Whether it's been for a date, friends in town, or late night scene spotting, I've always had a good time here.Culinary Explorer's Guide to Dining at a New York Mega Restaurant:1. Book reservations early in advance for large groups or take an early reservation at 6 or 7.2. Be sure to try their signature dishes.3. Order family style to get a taste of many dishes.4. Expect a busy scene and loud music, but that's all meant to be part of the experience.

I've never been a fan of fusion food; cuisines are developed over thousands of years and taste a certain way for a reason, if you're gonna smash it together with something else... fine but the odds are stacked against you. I've wanted to try Buddakan for a while, given good reviews on food and the fact the space is beautiful. However I found both to be a bit lacking. The food is pretty blah: a calamari salad, frogs leg app were forgettable, glazed cod is the same thing they serve in every fusion asian resto, the peking duck was dry and bland (I've literally had comparable stuff from take out places), deserts of the chocolate mille fuille and 5 spice donuts were probably the highlight. The decor was very nice but I feel like some of the details are going by the way side in the wake of their success. The place has the feel of a disney theme restaurant, but the central room is still a mind blower, chances are you'll just be walking by it on the way to your back room table so it won't do you much good. This would be a great bday place or if you're with a huge crowd, the kitchen is a machine pumping out food so you can be sure everyone will get fed in time. But besides that you should leave it alone.
Nice place with some very special dishes while others not so special or over-spiced. I always recommend getting 1.5 orders of charred beef for every person at the table. In addition get an order of regular fried dumplings and general tso dumplings for every 3 people. Everything else is just "ok or good" enough to try once but why get that when you can have "great and excellent" food that will make you want to come back. I will steer you far away from the fried rice dishes, which are consistently over-salted and actually inedible. Their cocktails are over-priced crap but you come here for the charred beef and dumplings, which you can't get anywhere else. Waiters/waitresses are always very experienced and on the ball trying to make you have a great evening. If there is a problem, they don't become panicky like every typical restaurant, they get confident to make sure you will be satisfied.

It's just overpriced Asian-fusion in the has-been Meatpacking. Why was I there? Oh, come on. You know it wasn't my idea and you certainly know I wasn't footing the bill. The four of us sat down in the lush and cavernous interior to be greeted by a huge ass bird candle centerpiece. It was so big I couldn't see my friend, or the waitress who came over to chat with us. Pushy and rather annoying, she used a pedantic voice when explaining the "family style" approach at Buddakan and suggested at least four entrees and four appetizers to share. Normally I would have rolled my eyes at so much food, but because I wasn't paying, I enthusiastically concurred. I also insisted on ordering drinks. I went for the "Fate", which I felt like a moron ordering. However, the elderberry-pineapple-prosecco combo proved to be a delicious one. Throw elderberry in anything and I am a happy camper. My friend's play on a gin and tonic also won me over, but it was not so memorable that I can remember what it was called, or even what the "play" was. On with the apps! The duck and foie spring rolls were an interesting way to serve up such fatty and succulent delicacies; which is to say I can't believe anyone outside of wd~50 would fry foie. Passable at best. The pork belly, served dimdum style, was a bit stringy for my liking, and just not as rich as I prefer. You know, that fat should be so moist, but it was on the gummy side and tough to chew. The chili beef tartar was delish, but it's hard to ruin a tartar if you've got quality goods. And finally, we all loved the frog legs, wok sauteed and covered in a ginger sauce.By the time the appetizer plates were cleared away, we were all starting to feel it. Now it was time for four entrees? Oh god. First thing's first: Get rid of that fucking bird candle centerpiece -- which a waiter did, patronizingly asking me, "Do you want to bird to fly away? Say the word, say the word, this bird will fly away." Yes. Get rid of that fucking bird, asshole. Okay. Entree times. We tried to mix and match, but definitely went meat heavy, starting off with the short rib we had heard good things about. Thumbs up, but nothing too special. Next out was another meaty delight, this time the veal cheeks, prepared over lo-mein noodles with pickled apples. This entire dish was fantastic, and for the record, I had never had veal before. Unfortunately, I'll now be ordering veal cheeks. Oh, don't hate on me, I'm sure I won't be able to afford it anytime soon. We followed the heavy meat dishes with rice with Chinese sausage, which was a pretty food fried rice, but at the end of the day, just fried rice. Hard to ruin. The pièce de résistance of dinner was the Three Crab Delight which blew our minds. The most delicate and sweet pieces of crab were served over more crab on top of crab. I can't explain to you how wonderful it was: I tried to hawk most of it but was soon overthrown by the other half of the table. So by this point we were ready for a trip to the vomitorium, but no, we went for dessert, which were all actually phenomenal. The highlights were  my blueberry tart served with mouthwatering corn (yes, corn) ice cream. Also a big winner were hot, fresh donuts with ginger ice cream. Clearly I am a sucker for kooky ice creams. The chocolate thing was also good, but I am over chocolate, and the other dessert was some thick white something covered in meringue. Eh, I can take or leave meringue. All in all, the food was pretty good. You know, give me a yummy cocktail and throw down some gourmet offerings like foie and crab and pork belly and I'll be smiling no matter what. But! I have had much, much better without all the pretense, without the attitude, and without the lame bridge and tunnel crowd. Sorry, Buddakan. Meatpacking is offish over.
Buddakan was GREAT. It can get pretty crowded, but not in a claustrophobic way, so definitely make a reservation. Despite everything, the reception staff and managers really went to great lengths to help my group with all our requests. Our server, Jordan, was also really attentive. Food-wise, there are some must-try dishes, and some other ones to skip over. The Scallion Pancakes were good, together with the Carrot Dumplings (interesting mushroom filling, better than the highly acclaimed Edamame Dumplings). The Peking Duck was a good choice, so was the Char Sui Roast Pork and the meat dishes. I would give the Alaskan Black Cod a miss though. It turned cold quickly and wasn't very flavorful. I would also skip the Rice dishes and Asian Green Stir Fry - definitely not Buddakan's strengths. Dessert-wise, try the Clementine Cloud and the Crying Chocolate. Clementine Cloud comes with a variety of light desserts that was a good end to the dinner, and the Chocolate was designed beautifully, tasted pretty good too. The Chocolate Sesame Fondant is pretty dense, so get that as a sharing plate. All in all, a wonderful experience. Go for the slightly pricier items, they really are worth the occasional splurge.

Order it!King Crab Hot Pot: Really fresh crab, tender and delicious. The avocado is just that: avocado mixed with a bit of butter and squeezed from a bottle into thin lines. Not great, and kind of kitschy to rely on that kind of novelty.DRINKS:Order the "Fate" cocktail! I hosted my 23rd birthday dinner at Buddakan NYC. I had originally made reservations at Butter but backed out after they started imposing absurd price restrictions for groups. I called them on the Thursday before my Saturday dinner and got lucky as they had an opening for 15 people! The special events coordinator was so accomodating and made the planning process very easy, I was able to pre-select everything from their prix fixe menus and they let me add in substitutions from their a la carte menu.  When we first arrived, the lounge looked very crowded, but it was pretty spacious downstairs in the main sitting area. They seated us at the large communal table located in the center of the restaurant -- a swanky and fun atmosphere. This is where Carrie Bradshaw and Mr. Big's engagement party was filmed in the first SATC movie!! The restaurant was fairly busy as it was a Saturday night, but our staff was extremely friendly and attentive. The decor was fabulous and darkly lit with high ceilings and gorgeous chandeliers. Dress code: Most girls were wearing dresses/skirts or jeans with heels and most guys were in slacks and a dress shirt. We started by having the specially created birthday cocktail! They began bringing out the food almost immediately after. Everything was served family style. For appetizers, we started with edamame dumplings, cantonese chicken and shrimp spring rolls, general tso's dumplings and a calamari salad. The edamame dumplings were fried but not too oily. The calamari salad had green apples, cashews and miso vinaigrette - perfect blend of flavors. The General tso dumplings were sweet and tangy, and dipped in a hot  sour broth. We were already pretty full from all the delicious appetizers when the main course started rolling out! For the entrees, we had:1. sizzling short ribs - they were cooked how I like them (well done), not too dry, not too moist -- just right. 2. sweet  crispy jumbo shrimp - my guests said they were delicious, I'm allergic so I can't comment on the shrimp. 3. shacha 5-spice barbeque chicken - the bbq chicken was tender, moist, mildly spicy and paired well with the lo mein and vegetable rice. 4. hot  sour scallops with sweet corn, tofu  black mushrooms - the scallops were yum!5. minced pork lo mein and vegetable (side) - great lo mein, wasn't greasy, and it served as the perfect side6. vegetable rice with coconut curry foam - rice with coconut curry, standard thai combination, it was deliciousMy favorites were the chicken, scallops and lo mein.They gave us 3 chef-selected desserts:1. golden carrot cake with black raisin plum sauce and caramelized cream cheese2. "crying chocolate" malted white chocolate ganache with a side of jasmine tea ice cream3. peanut butter bar with char siu peanuts, sweet and sour cherry sauce, and horlicksI can't decide on a favorite dessert because they were all to-die-for!Overall, the planning process was smooth and stress-free, the service was impeccable, and most importantly, the food was AMAZING. I can't think of a single con so I give Buddakan NYC 5 stars! The event was fantastic!

I only have two Gaysians.  That makes me Gaysian poor, by New York standards, especially since one of my Gaysians moved home to San Francisco (the ancestral homeland of the Gaysian).  Anyway, my San Francisco Gaysian is a close friend.  So when he came back to New York, we hung out quite a bit, including a dinner with a decent sized group at Buddakan.So normally if a restaurant is above average in every way except one, I will make sure to mention that one point last, because I know that my reviews are ridiculously long, and virtually nobody reads them in their entirety.  This flaw was so inexcusable, however, that I feel like it needs to be mentioned front and center.  The appetizers, entrees, desserts, wine, and our waitress were all four star quality.  I'm not going to knock off a star for this, but they say that dessert is the course that can ruin a restaurant, because it is the last thing that the customer remembers.  This was true for me at Buddakan, but not for the taste.  The bus boy took my plate, which had chocolate syrup on the edge, and swiped it across my shirt as he cleared it.  I don't know if he noticed it or not, but he certainly didn't apologize.  I couldn't give a crap about the shirt, but a restaurant that is supposed to be upscale...  Well let's just say that I would rather have a meal that was mediocre from start to finish than have a meal where attention was paid to almost every facet, and then one detail was just totally butchered.  Buddakan: Hire decent busboys!Anyway, I usually try to mention in my reviews the exact items that I tried, but our party had about six or seven entrees and about four or five appetizers.  Plus I think that every one of us had dessert.  I would say that the dessert was simultaneously the most disappointing and spectacular (not even counting the chocolate streak on my shirt).  This is because the presentation was borderline museum quality, while the taste of the dessert was fairly bland, with the exception of the ice cream that they included a little scoop of.I'm not an expert in Asian cuisine.  So I don't know what things were, but I had some sort of boneless spare rib that was out of this world (tender and tasty).  I had something that was like a small, chewy fajita shaped thing with maybe pork or something to fold inside of it.  That was excellent, too.  The fried rice was great.  The seafood dishes were very popular with my friends who eat seafood.  I don't remember a single appetizer or entree getting a single negative (or even mediocre) reaction from anyone.  The dessert being a little boring, flavor-wise, was the worst thing that I could say about the food.Our waitress was absolutely awesome, too.  She was very friendly, knowledgeable, and attentive; but still unobtrusive.  Actually, the waitress was probably five stars.  The food was a solid four stars.  The atmosphere, etc. was probably four to five stars.  It was really just the careless busboy that made part of me want to drop this rating to a three star rating.  There are plenty of unemployed people looking for jobs right now.  It shouldn't be that hard to find one with just a tiny amount of work ethic (or at least etiquette) to hire as a bus boy.

Sounded too cool to pass up.It arrives and it's one of those plates that ought to be hanging alongside Pollack. Too beautiful and delicated to dig into. But of course for $14 you do. Forks however do not break up the juxtaposition. You'll have to pick apart each individual sheet  manually. It doesn't melt or crumple or water ones mouth like it's supposed to. It's definitely fun to sit with a group and decipher and deconstruct.You see avocado, but taste banana...bummer...I was really excited to see how they were going to incorportate avocado. I can go on and on about the randomness of this dish, but I'll stop. It's a food to play with, not digest.The main courses were -fine-. Nobody was particularly overwhelmed with joy, but again the constructs blinds you from ever realizing.I love that you can get dressed up. My leg was broken at the time though and I hopped in, in sneakers and jeans (and crutches) and didn't feel snubbed on. The servers were all very friendly. Upscale, but not upturned noses. I would come back to impress people and try these edemame dumplings I keep reading about, but I'll always be a Highline girl.
Well now that I have actually set food in the ultra-trendy venue that serves delicious Asian food, I can say for myself that it is pretty hot.  All of the dishes we ordered were pretty much worth the money - and there is a large selection of things to choose from on the menu.  The only thing that tainted our personal experiences was the brusque attitude of our waiter.  He just seemed to hate us, though I don't know why since we weren't the least bit rude and we did order most of his suggestions (His highest recommendation was the Charred Beef entree which came cut in big medium rare chunks with a rich butter sauce to dribble all over it.  I think it was my favorite thing).  So yeah, the waiter's 'tude kind of put a damper on the evening, but the food is so good and the decor is so pretty that i still will tell you all to go there so you can feel special on your special occasion.  Unless you're rich and every weekend is a special occasion.  Then, go there immediately too. Like far too many things in life this place started out amazing and ended up disappointing. Like getting a shiny new penny and realizing that it can't buy you anything. Or a great first date and not another phone call... I digress. The space is beautiful and massive. The decor was a little confused as it blends Renaissance art with Thai statues and food. Somehow it worked. My mind and palate were set for what friends had been raving about. One of the reasons I made the massive drive up from DC...We're seated quickly, and I order a St. Germaine and sprite.  I'm feeling good about the initial service and decor....  Everyone was happy with their drinks (less a really light poor of wine).  Alas that was the end of the wonder of the shiny Buddhakan penny. The salad was dripping in dressing making it virtually inedible. I don't think that anyone was happy with their appetizer, though some people were less disappointed than others.  The "entrees" were no better.  The sizes were tiny, the food was not good... Oh and the bill.... Now, I'm not a big spender, and I know this.  But I don't mind shelling out a good chunk of hard-earned money when the food was either amazing, or at least satisfyingly filling.  This was neither.  For the amount of food and the quality of food, I shouldn't have paid half as much as I did.  Soooo disappointing.  If I were to come back it would only be for drinks, I wouldn't give them money for food again!
Actual conversation with a friend coming to NY to visit:Adam: I am going to take you guys to Buddakan tonight. It's a delicious Chinese restaurant. I guess it's like Asian fusion, whatever that means.Friend: Is it like P.F. Chang's?Adam: It's P.F. Chang's on steroids.That's pretty much the best way to describe. This is off the basis of visiting Buddakan twice.  Once it was a 5 star experience, the other time, a 0 star experience.Let me talk about the initial experience first.Me and a friend were stressing out over school, since it was midterm season at NYU, and we though to indulge ourselves and go to Il Mulino (thats how NYU kids cope with stress-turn to alcohol and fancy dinners), but, unfortunately even on a Tuesday we were unable to get reservations.  It was about 4:30pm,  so we decided to give Buddakan a call, and were able to get reservations for 8:45pm.  We got to their check in desk and were seated by 9pm.  The waiter came out promptly and we ordered drinks and appetizers.   I had a "Fever" and my friend ordered a Bay Breeze.  I would have opted for a manlier drink, but, I figure at a restaurant like this, the specialty cocktails would be fine.  At about 15 a piece, they arent cheap, and not especially strong.  I couldnt taste the Jalapeno at all, but it had a good pomegranate essence.  I pounded it, and had the "Lush" drink next.  It was significantly stronger, and arrived at the same time appetizers did.    We had...Edamame Dumplings-amazing.  I had never had anything so delicate, so evangelical in my mouth (giggity), and they seemed to be levitating on top of the broth.  Beautifully presented, albeit a little hard to eat, due to the fact that they are so soft.  Picking up with chopsticks almost assured that they would be stabbed, and try eating them in multiple bites without mutilating them.  haha.   Lobster Egg Rolls-came with 3 in our order.  Solid, fresh, warm, thick chunks of lobster, and delicious.Taro Lollipops--cool presentation, but overrated, IMHO.For the main course, my friend opted for the peking duck, while I had the Sweet and Sour chicken.  I am not a duck fan, but she seemed to really like it.  It was a large portion of duck (and for $50, it better be), and she only finished about a quarter of it, after all those amazing appetizers.  My SSC was awesome, albeit a smaller portion.  Really well cooked white chicken breast, on top  of fresh vegatables and SnS sauce.  The star, however, was the side of vegetable rice we ordered.   OMFG.  Best rice I had ever had.  Tasted amazing, and had this great sauce with it.For dessert, we had  crying chocolate, and a specialty dessert cocktail that the waiter recommended to us.  The cocktail wasn't great (and was $17 --he didnt mention the price when he talked about it), extremely sweet.  The actual dessert was decadent, and having ice cream and chocolate cake balanced out perfectly.The bill came out to about $250 after tax and tip.Now for the horrible experience.  I wont make it super drawn out, but here it goes.We made the reservations about 3 weeks in advance, for a Saturday night birthday dinner for a party of 10 at 830 pm.  We got it,which was awesome.  Birthday girl had friends coming in from colleges out of the state, and had to get back that same night on the train, so it was crucial that we leave by 11pm, so they can catch the train back to CT.   We stressed this to them, and upon arriving they said our table would be ready by 9pm.  ok.  not good, but fine.   WE WERE NOT SEATED UNTIL 9:45PM!!!!!!!!  We were in the waiting room like idiots, while waiters pushed and shoved us to get out of their way, whispering rude remarks under their breaths, and downright yelling at us twice to get out of the way.  WE DO NOT WANT TO BE IN THE WAY!  WE SHOULDNT BE IN THE WAY!  WE SHOULD BE SEATED!!!!  The manager kept coming up to us and telling us that we were their priority group, etc.  Bull.  After an hour of being treated like cattle, they led us out of the waiting room down to the main dining room table....only to make us stand THERE awkwardly for 10 mins, watching people eat.  wtf?  Were they trying to clear out that area?  whatever.  We thought we were being seated. silly us.  We were led around the restaurant about 3 times, before being stuck at possibly THE WORST TABLE AT THE RESTAURANT. Situated between the bathroom and the kitchen doors, we saw clamors of waiters running in and out, hear them cursing and talking about tables, and toilets flushing.  FML.  Only table with that location, so maybe malicious move on their part.  They ID'd everyone, and waitress never came to check up on anything.  Also, one of the waiters slipped and fell going into the kitchen,  sending glass shattering all over the floor, and under out table.  There was also food that had fallen, which was now surrounding the table.  I started to think we were in some kind of hidden camera show, a la boiling points.  Two of the girls had to leave to catch the train back to CT BEFORE their food arrived, and waitress disregarded that, and told us to split it between us.  she knew of the time sensitivity.  Food was meh (I had the filet).  It all arrived at different times, which is Not ok.  Some people were finishing before others meals arrived.None of us will EVER return.
