My dinner at Buddakan, or the day I realized I really am a food snob.So I went here with work as part of a big SATC night (silly yes, fun obv!) The place is gorgeous and you just feel like a celeb walking in. We ate at Carrie and Big's rehearsal dinner table, the big long one in the center of the room down the stairs. The chandeliers were amazing-the room reminded me of Temple of doom meets Ikea or Gymboree. Weird I know, but between the elegant details of the walls, the fresco-like painting on the walls and the colorful abstract window sculptures, it's what came to me. The service was spectacular and the waiters were knowledgeable and friendly.But on to the food... here is where i realized my snobbery. From the room, the hype and knowing the cost of things - I was expecting to be amazed by the food. I wasn't. It wasn't bad, but I wasn't blown away. It reminded me very much of a Chain restaurant, much like a Ruby Foo's.We had the Edamame dumplings, which I see raves for on Yelp, but am wondering if these people enjoy baby food as well. The dumplings were filled with green pureed mush and the "Sauternes broth" did not taste of Sauternes at all and was, imho, a waste of a good dessert wine. The lobster egg rolls were decent- did not taste of mint though they were touted as such, and were no better than local delivery. The lobster meat was a little tough too; one bite and the filling was all hanging from my mouth while i still held the shell! The crispy calamari salad was delicious and would be something I would return for (and is the only food related reason for the 4th star) and the General Tso's Chicken dumplings were messy and kind of boring.I only had a few items from the sides we ordered as I was pretty full (and ok, getting a little tipsy - which sometimes kills the appetite) but the crab fried rice was gross - a little too fishy, and overloaded on coconut or something sweet-ish. The Sugar snap peas we tasty but not very impressive/innovative. I had the sweet and crispy jumbo shrimp for my entree, and while it had interesting flavor, it also tasted like it was doused in the mayo sauce they use to make spicy tuna rolls, minus the spice, so it tasted like shrimp covered in sweet mayo. Nice flavor, strange texture - and once I think of seafood with mayo I get a little nauseous. I did get to meet Chef Dale (of top chef fame) which was cool, and while the food was well prepared (go Dale) it was really the structure of the dishes/menu that left me thinking Buddakan ought to stick to the less picky/more easily impressed metro areas, i.e. philly.A co-worker was a big fan of the beef dishes, and as I avoid those, I will defer to her, seems beef is their wheel house... but I still claim that Buddakan is overrated...Maybe I really am just a jaded foodie.

Went to Buddakan for the first time with two friends. Yes.  it is a upscale, trendy and super expensive for a Chinese restaurant; however, Its food is really NOT that impressive.  We had four appetizers with raving reviews on Yelp, but disappointed with all four. Edamame dumpling was mushy and tasteless, Scallion Pancake was extremely salty, Hoisin Glazed Pork Belly was kind of fatty, Chili Rock Shrimp was popcorn shrimp with a fancy name.Our three Entrees fared much better than appetizers. Glazed Black Cod was tender and delicious. Shrimp Lobster Chow Fun was my favorite. For its $35 high price tag, It had decent number of fresh and large shrimps. The chow fun was very well made. Broken Chili Chicken was OK. Two Desserts we had, Crying Chocolate and Almond Bread Pudding, were with great presentation, but average taste.Overall, we give Buddakan 3 stars.
Situated in the corner of the Chelsea Market building, the space and scale of things is physically impressive. At over 17,000 sq. ft. and with a capacity for over 400 guests, it was not a shy venture.Appropriately, it has been divided into a collection of connecting spaces. There is a bar area with communal tables where diners choose from either a smaller bar menu or the full restaurant menu - which isn't really much more extensive. Numerous other darkly lit rooms host tables, but the main dining area is a sight to behold. In the middle of the entire layout, a doorway opens up to a cavernous room, with tables one floor below and the roof a floor higher than the main level. It is an incredibly ambitious space - complete with giant 40ft table in the centre - but somehow has been worked to conjure up a French-Asian royalty look, with rich maroon and gold colors. Eating downstairs must make one feel like being invited to dine at a palace.The atmosphere inside hums with a casual yet trendy energy, and the crowd is full of good looking, successful types and 'foodies' trying out the latest venture. More importantly, the Asian-inspired menu pulls off some impressively flavorful dishes. We ate at a communal table in the bar area that comfortably sat twelve people, a more relaxed way to dine amongst such regal settings. Notable were the Tuna Tartare dumplings, Lobster Dumplings with truffle soy, and the Sea Bass rolls with ginger. According to our waitress, the pastry chef is "an inspired man" (though she couldn't name him!), but we did not leave space in the end to confirm this. I do sense I will be back though.Overall, Buddakan offers an opulent dining experience and pleasing menu that tries hard to impress as much as the restaurant's presence does. However, you'll probably remember the experience more than the food itself.

during my most recent jaunt to the big apple, i had the privilege of celebrating a dear girlfriend's bachelorette at buddakan, which was just another *nbd* moment seeing as her engagement soiree was at the point of view lounge atop the w hotel in dc, her bridal shower was in a private room at the carlyle hotel in nyc, and her wedding was in palm beach. (i know, i've stopped trying to figure out how much money i spent as i was present at every event.)let me start with the establishment itself. it's incredible that such an understated entrance leads into a (super cool) dungeon that has a bar and spiral staircase down into the bigger dining area. think the hogwarts dining hall for adults. yes, it's true, i got to eat at the very table where carrie bradshaw had her rehearsal dinner (youtube.com/watch?v=ZOGQ…), and yes, it was just that breathtaking.to start off (that's misleading as we spent the entire evening getting refills), we had the tranquility beverage:: citrus vodka paired with lemongrass-infused oolong tea. definitely tranquil..until about the fourth glass..then it's just all giggles. my affection towards the special beverage has since won me the nickname "quill" with the girls.get the edamame dumplings. the soft shells are penetrated with a shallot-sauternes broth that reminded me of shanghai's xiao long bao (soup dumplings) and warmed the cockles.we then shared the beef lettuce cups (with puffed rice and pickled tomato salad), steamed sea bass roll (with cabbage, ginger, and sizzling scallion oil), and minced pork lo mein (with pickled cucumbers and thai chilies). all very flavorful and held their own.of course, we couldn't leave without indulging in a couple desserts. the crying chocolate (with malted white ganache coffee ice cream) was beyond decadent and really demonstrated chocolate's aphrodisiac powers. berry cloud, on the other hand, was a strawberry-calamansi (but incorrectly spelled "kalamanzi" on their menu..boo!) sorbet with green tea and tickled the senses with its fresh and flirty tartness.all in all, an amazing experience, and the waitstaff is on point. i removed a star because it's awkward sitting at the large table with a first date going on (literally) beside you and a rollicking gaylebration (the studly men told me i could call it that) on the other side of your party. and i get it..we could've chosen *not* to sit at the large table..but that chair i sat in puts me at one degree of separation from charlotte! or stanford! or mr big! so i'm not complaining. yep, samantha's buttcheeks and mine could've indirectly touched. i'd be jealous, too. the removal of a star is also due the disappointing state of the restroom. toilet paper and paper towel strewn about..poor form.but still..if i can make a reservation FOR 1030pm and walk out on MY own terms at 3am..that's golden right there, folks. i'm positive buddakan has and will continue to provide for awesome memories to all who visit.
I'm not ashamed to say that Buddakan provided me with one of the best dinners of my life. In fact, I've been holding off giving any restaurant 5-stars until I wrote the review for this place.Oh, Buddakan. How I love you. Restaurant was gorgeous, plain and simple. Their great hall is really something to behold. We didn't sit there, but we marveled as we passed. Food was simple, elegant, and most of all, delicious. The edamame dumplings that everyone is raving about deserve all the praise. The filling was so smooth and light. It was light eating a cloud. We also had the lobster fried rice, the steak with mustard sauce, and the black cod. While the lobster fried rice and the steak were DELICIOUS, the black cod was to die for. I can't even explain. But every time I eat fish at another restaurant, I think longingly back to Buddakan's black cod. Yum. Just, so yum.The stars of the meal, though: DESSERT.Sweet Jesus, the dessert. We had the Crying Chocolate (melting chocolate ganache with jasmine tea ice cream), and the Almond Bread Pudding (with whiskey ice cream). Gorgeous too look at - but you won't be looking very long as you shovel them into your mouth. Try to continue to look classy as you do it, even though it'll be tough.Will definitely come back.Try it out yourself; thank me later.

Oh. My. Goodness. This meal was out of control. Boyfriend's dad and step-mom took us here last month for an absolutely fabulous dinner. We were joined by Boyfriend's sister, step-sister and her boyfriend, so the waitress offered us the option of getting one their three tasting menus. Overwhelmed by the thought of ordering the proper amount of food for the table ala carte, we opted to get the second tier tasting menu, which was $80 per person, plus an extra $15 for the additional peking duck course. This would have been plenty of food as it was, but we actually ended up getting two extra appetizers and a salad on the house. Boyfriend's dad has an epic sesame allergy, and there were three or four things on the standard menu that he couldn't eat. Instead of offering substitutions, or having a separate course for him, they the waitress actually brought enough of the extra dishes, (described as some of their "premium items"), for all of us! Talk about amazing service. She was also there every step of the way to make sure that he knew which dishes he could and could not eat. As for the food itself, I can't tell you the last time I was treated to such an endless parade of delicious and interesting dishes. Lists are boring, but everything on this one was really good: we got the taro lollipops, cantonese spring rolls, edamame dumplings, jade shrimp dumplings, tuna tartare spring rolls, beef lettuce cups, peking duck, peking duck salad, crispy calamari salad with green apple and cashew, chilled sesame udon noodles with lime sorbet, asian green stir fry, szechuan crusted rib eye steak, glazed Alaskan black cod, sweet and crispy jumbo shrimp, plus what was probably their entire dessert menu.I'll describe a few of the standouts in detail. The beef lettuce cups were great, just a little bite of beautifully charred medium rare steak with lettuce. The edamame dumplings just melted in your mouth and dissolved there, and were like a little bundle of delicious pea soup. I especially loved the cold sesame udon noodles with lime sorbet, which is definitely not the sort of dish I would have expected to like, but the lime and peanut flavors somehow worked really well together, and the thick udon noodles were deliciously chewy. This was definitely the most unexpected dish in my opinion. One really simple dish that packed in a lot of flavor was the asian green stir fry. I just love really fresh and simple veggies, so this was a favorite of mine. It would have been the star of the entree round were it not for the glazed black cod, which was soft and flakey and deliciously sweet. My other favorite fish dish came earlier in the tuna tartare spring rolls appetizer, which was another unexpected treat. I love raw tuna sushi, but who would have thought to pair the rich meaty fish with a crunchy spring roll shell? So good! The only dessert that I couldn't get enough of was the crying chocolate cake, with its delicious white ganache tears. Don't leave without getting it.The other dishes were all tasty, but were less memorable. For instance, the rib eye was great, but it was not as unusual as some of the other things we were served. And though we all enjoyed the peking duck course, it was a very traditional take on the dish, and you'd be just as well served ordering it at an old school Chinese restaurant for much less. On the other hand, the accompanying peking duck salad was more original yet its inspiration was still evident, so I'd recommend ordering that if you want some duck with your dinner. All in all, everything was pretty much great, and I felt like a giant pig from eating so many different things. It was fun, but I'd probably order less were I lucky enough to go back.I would highly recommend Buddakan for your next special occasion. Its such a dramatic setting, with wonderfully accommodating service and phenomenal food presented impeccably. Our bill may have been obscenely large, but if you order ala cart I actually think the individual prices are fairly reasonable. If you like Asian food and aren't afraid to mess with traditional flavors, Buddakan is sure to surprise and amaze you with its wonderfully unique dishes.

In the niche between "casual" and "fine" dining seems to lurk the happy medium of "upscale," which would seem to fit Buddakan very nicely. The restaurant has all the trappings of a trendy, downtown restaurant, with a nice Louis-meets-Asian theme. Although one certainly doesn't need to don a full suit and tie to feel comfortable, "dress to impress" would certainly be de rigueur. (One helpful hint: If possible, ask to sit downstairs.) Service was incredibly (perhaps too) prompt and friendly, and pleasantly not-snobby for a place that's so popular. I could easily tell one of Buddakan's reasons for being one of the five most profitable restaurants in the U.S.: high turnover. Our server flatly "suggested" we order all of our dishes at once, and once we had they began to arrive with lickety-split precision. In fact, even after ordering dessert and coffee, we were out of there in less than two hours.Regardless of the pacing, the food was, on the whole, quite good. Many dishes lean more towards the Asian end of the continuum... A $44 whole duck arrived as rather plainly mound of (granted, delicious) duck meat with the typical accoutrements you'd find for a fraction of the price over in Chinatown. However, other items like the edemame dumplings or the petrale sole showed real creativity, flair, and of course, delicious flavor.In all, a nice, albeit leaning-towards-pricey place to go for a special dinner out.

The black cod was good but a little overcooked. Come for the decor and the scene, but don't expect to get your socks knocked off by the food. It's good but not great Chinese food.

Sigh*It was our end of the year office party and we decided Buddakan would be an acceptable choice of venue. So...the decor - how pretty! The lounge area is so sleek. The paintings in the restaurant are just sexy. You know that if the restaurant can hang a wall painting behind the front desk - again its just sexy. It took my breathe away (all you yelpers might think I'm over-exaggerating - but I like the restaurant so let me say all the good things I want). The main dining hall is so sexy with its high ceilings. So nice. They have this section of the dining area where the walls are painted like book shelves. The bindings are all gold. People dub it as "The Library." So nice. LOL @ the people that work there. I guess my coworkers don't often fancy these type of restaurants. They were commenting on how the hosts (or maitre d's?) looked like security bodyguards. Hilarious. Nice people but sort of pushy in my opinion. Almost snobbish I guess. Jalapeño liquor? What? Why?! Cool. My first cocktail was charm. Very pretty and not strong. It is made with passion fruit liqueur, apple, fresh berries and prosecco. It's a good starter cocktail. My next cocktail is fever; made with mezcal, lime, jalapeno and pomegranate. Ever had a spicy cocktail? This is it. It has quite a kick to it. Very enjoyable though.  We also had a bottle of sake (sorry don't remember which). Lastly, the food. We ordered a whole bunch and if I commented on each one - well no one would ever read this yelp because then it would just take up the entire page. Highlights - lobster egg rolls, general tso's dumplings, deviled tuna tartare, and shrimp and lobster chow fun.  The not so greats - edamame dumplings. The reason for this is just because the texture bothered me a bit. I know a lot of people like these so its just a preference thing. For sure for sure order the general tso's dumplings. We ordered only 2 in the beginning and then ordered another 2 because it was so great. I do have to say though they are pricey for the portion that the restaurant gives you. I do believe this is a spot you should hit up at least once. Would I go there again? If I can afford it then for sure. Def. one of the few top restaurants on my list. happy eatings~

Hot DAMN this place is HUGE!  As soon as I saw the army of 10 hostesses at the front, I knew this was going to be a serious operation.  This restaurant must hold 1,500 people.  It took them a while to seat us, because the place was chaotic packed, and it was a Friday night.  So, we had a drink or two in the club-like bar area and anticipated our seating.  Finally, when they did seat us they were very apologetic and seated us at a great table in the main dining room, adorned with massive wooden chandeliers and 50ft high cielings.  They also sent out two appetizers on the house...nice touch.  One of them included these amazing edamame dumplings.  Mashed edamame with truffle oil, butter and cream all inside a steamed dumpling shell.  SO GOOD!  I am really glad they sent those out because we wouldnt have gotten to try them otherwise.The other dishes we ordered were good, and the dinner went well.  But, I have to say that the main reason you should come here is for the ambiance and the scene.  It is really an amazing space- it used to be a coca cola factory.  Plus, its hopping on a weekend night.  Come here for pre-dinner drinks in the lounge or for a full fledged dinner.  But, if you choose the latter, be prepared to wait!  It's worth it.

The upstairs is more bustling and crowded so it's a very dine-with-a-group kind of feel. Downstairs is dimmer, and more sensual, which is where we sat because I'm a sensual kinda gal. Our waiter, Owen seems out of place, mustache and slight twang of an accent and all, but he's one of the best servers I've ever had the pleasure of meeting. He was kind, informative, gracious, but not overly attentive or trying too hard to make the service seem 5 star or formal. The food: -Glazed Black Cod Miso: very good flavors here, the grilled eggplant on the side and salted cucumbers were slight and balanced out the hint of sweetness in the fish. However, my friend and I weren't huge fans of the fish itself; we like our fish dry and flaky, this was oily and moist. Order it if you like your cod wet. (ooh baby). -Charred Filet Beef: looks are deceiving. My eyes were visually underwhelmed by this boring looking dish with a sad piece of beef on it and  bowl of taro chips in the middle. But, lo and behold, it was cooked PERFECTLY medium-rare and oh, that gravy. I'm not a fan of gravy but I'd slather this buttery, delicious gravy on all my Thanksgiving turkeys if I could.-ShrimpLobster Chow Fun: jumbo shrimp, chunks of lobster meat, veggies, and savory chow fun. This dish is salty, but it adds a much needed carb dish to our dinner, and the portion is generous.-Mapo Tofu: My Szechuan grandma would slap me silly knowing I paid $20+ for mapo tofu but this was some interesting flavored mapo tofu. It was served in a simple bowl with an even simpler bowl of white rice accompanying it. It was a bit spicy, a bit salty, a bit tangy (that was the kicker), and very flavorful. Strangely enough, it was the most authentically Chinese dish of our meal.I would compare this place to Spice Market in ambiance (quite large, impressive decor, has a good balance of fun and sexy), but with better food, and a mixture of Tao for cuisine, only better, and no tourists or kids running around. I went today, so it was mainly an after-work crowd. Buddakan, you almost make me like the MPD again, it's a good thing you face Chelsea.
The food is delicious. Plain and simple. All meats cooked to PERFECTION. The best scallops I've ever had in my life, the steak was one of the best I've ever had, lobster fried rice was not that great but fried rice is pretty boring itself, the edamame dumplings were great and so were the tuna spring rolls and rock shrimp. Drinks were fun but not really worth the price. Generally, BEAUTIFUL restaurant, nice (enough) staff considering they were busy, and fantastic food.

The bar was pretty crowded (Friday night at 8p) but we were seated within 5 minutes and treated very nicely by the waitstaff.Let me start by saying, the portions are described as "family-sized" but the waitress warns you that they are really individual portions. It comes with 3 small fried rolls of tuna tartare which may sound eh~ but they were so yummy I wished I had ordered 2 of those instead of the dumplings.Charred Filet of Beef was okay. We also ordered a side of the cauliflower which was stir-fried with pork. It was a bit spicy and salty, and also just okay. The only thing I'd order again is the Tuna Tartare Spring Rolls. Oh P.S., the cocktails on the menu are super tiny. Like, mimosa-sized tiny. I ordered a Cosmopolitan for my 2nd drink and that was $15. Ridiculous. So my sentiments about Buddakan are basically that it is super-overpriced and I'd never go back. Not that I regret my meal because I wanted to try it some day, but that's that.

I usually dislike going to trendy restaurants trying to do ethnic, but for Buddakan, I caved.  And I was pleasantly surprised!The trick is to do your research ahead of time and know what you want to order.  Buddakan is supposed to serve family-portioned Chinese fare, so the menu was more extensive than I expected.  But I did read up on it beforehand and already had a couple of items in mind.The other trick is that with the prior point, you can actually have a fairly moderately priced experience.  It's easy to drop over $100 for dinner, but mine came out to a very reasonable $40/person (including tip).- Cantonese spring rolls - you only get 3, but they're really good, especially with the mustard.- Charred filet of beef - Oh. My. God.  The buttery, garlicky soy sauce that goes over the meat is absolutely heavenly.  This was the most expensive and least filling plate we ordered but it was the best thing we got.  We came THIS close to ordering another.  I'd go back just for this.- Mao poe tofu - honestly, this was a little disappointing, probably because I'd read just rave reviews about it on NYT and other places.  It's good and it's very filling, but it was a little too tangy sweet for me.- Crying chocolate dessert - I couldn't talk or listen to anyone while eating this.  It was that good.And of course, the ambience!  How much more freakin' trendy and sceney can you get?  Next time, I'm going to try to get a reservation down in the large room.All in all, I had a lot of fun at Buddakan.  Can't wait to go back!
Just as I had promised myself, I dined at Buddakan for my next trip to NYC, and boy was I glad that I followed through with it!I hadn't booked well-in-advance reservations since we were dining on a Sunday evening, but I'd highly recommend it since they ended up being booked until 9:45! Luckily, they have a bunch of tables in their lounge area, even a few community tables, where we could still dine at.Dinner was just as I predicted, a meal that definitely didn't disappoint. We ordered...-Minced Pork Lo Mein w/ pickled cucumbers  thai chili: The minced pork was a nice touch! -Sweet  Sour Chicken: I envisioned the typical mound of deep-fried chicken pieces, swimming in a red glaze, but Buddakan presented a different take on it that I took quite the liking to- slices of chicken breast with a crispy outer layer and a tangy glaze drizzled on top. Yum!-Vegetable Rice w/ coconut curry foam: So good, it was practically the highlight! Not only did I learn something new about Buddakan- that they serve up some tasty dishes, but I also picked up on a few additional details that make this place a true gem. For instance, their definite strength is their friendly service. Staffed w/ a door greeter and a handful of organized hostesses at a sprawling front desk, you couldn't possibly be overlooked. Another little nuance? A hint of BRICK in their bathroom stalls. It may sound like a mundane detail to others, but I love the little signature NYC touch.Overall, coming here was a good/bad idea. Good because it's breathtaking in every way. And bad because it'll hinder me from trying new restaurants in NYC!

Last night I stepped out of my comfort zone and sat in this bar by myself and decided to order a cocktail and some nibblies. I don't really go out alone all that often, but seeing as how the hotel room was turning into one big fat f*#k of a bore, I decided to get out and try somewhere cool as I waited for my friend to finish up her dinner plans.The place I chose was Buddakan and it is gorgeous. I mean really gorgeous. It's dark, it's intimate, it's romantic and it's the kind of joint that even if you are there with yourself, you are probably going to get lucky with yourself later. Know what I'm sayin? ;)So I ordered my usual Belvedere and soda and grabbed a table and perused the menu. I saw a lot of the spiffied up versions of Asian fusion cuisine; the dim sum, the spring rolls, etc. and then I spotted something I have feared for a very long time. Frog Legs.I am not much of a frog person and while I've kissed many and have yet to find my prince, the idea of eating part of one is something I have feared for decades and so I decided to give into the fear and move onto to trying something safe, but dammit if my eyes didn't keep going back to the frog legs. Now I don't know if it was the Food Network weird foods special I watched on the plane or the fact that I was all alone and figured, "What the hell?" but as soon as the waiter came over I said, "Frog Legs please and the beef tartare"What?I couldn't believe what came out of my mouth and with such confidence at that. Who the hell was I on a date with. Clearly the self I know and love never would have ordered that on our date, but the order was in, so I figured I outta start prepping myself for the pending dish.To do this i started texting people. I mean, what else are you gonna do, right? I think I sent this message out to about 12 friends as i sat there downing my drink. "Oh my god, I just ordered frog legs and I am scuuuurrred" Soon people started texting me back things like "Ewwwhhhh" "Girl, you crazy" "Come home!!" "Tastes like...yardbird?" and then I looked up to see the waiter holding my dish. Oh god.So there it sat, staring at me and honestly it wasn't as scuuuurry looking as I had imagined in my warped paranoid brain. The little pieces of leg were mixed in with cabbage and golden chives in a creamy garlicky sauce and compared to the plate of raw meat with tapioca balls next to it, I figured I should just jump in.And so I did. I picked one of the things up with my chopsticks and in my mouth it went. As I chewed I thought, "Steph, you realize you are eating a frog right now. A ribbit. A little guy that used to make noises outside of your bedroom window as a kid. You were chomping down on one of those cute little tadpoles you used to love so much, but damn it, this is actually really tasty."I then found myself grabbing every little piece and enjoying them fully.  I then switched to the beef tartare and after a few nibbles of that I had had enough. It was way too spicy anyway. I then got the text from my friend I was waiting for and wrapped up the check and made my way out to join her.I ate a frog ladies and gentlemen. Wow, who woulda thunk it.

After I ate here Friday night I couldn't sleep because visions of dumplings and lobster were dancing in my head...I'm serious..I woke up..with only 5 hours of sleep because I couldn't stop thinking about the delicious food.  I've read all the detailed reviews on Yelp and I don't really understand why Buddakan has such a low star rating.  In every possible way I would give them five stars (more if I could).  I had an absolutely fabulous time here.  Maybe it was all the beautiful people that I saw, from the Matthew McConaughey look a like to the actual Terri Hatcher.  Maybe I had such a great time because I started my meal off with one of those fabulous cocktails the Charm or maybe it was because I wasn't paying for my meal..but anyhow I had an absolutely fabulous time.  "Spoiler Warning" Before I get into the details of this perfect meal, I just want to say that I believe one of the reasons why I enjoyed the food so much was because I didn't have really high expectations (given the 3 1/2 stars on Yelp) and because the menu only hints to the ingredients used in the dishes...so everything was a delicious surprise.  So if you haven't been to Buddakan and you're reading this list to get ideas on what to order just look at the names of the starred dishes, don't read the descriptions.  It will ruin the surprise. Oh and one of the great things about this place is that its family style..the only way I believe a meal should be eaten.  So first off on the delicious journey of my dinner was: *1. Edamame Dumplings, These little pockets of goodness were the best surprise...They were absolutely delicious.  It was like nothing I ever imagined!  The edamame inside was creamy and sweet, all this blended together with the soft dumpling skins and the salty broth perfectly.  *2. Crispy Calamari Salad, The fried calamari was perfect, not tough or soggy, it went perfectly with the spring greens and soy vinaigrette. 3. Chili Rock Shrimp, the fried shrimp in this dish were cooked perfectly, but they use a spicy mayonnaise sauce and since I'm not the biggest mayonnaise fan, this was my least favorite dish, still really good just not my favorite.  4. Boneless Spare Ribs, They were absolutely delicious, moist and tender, spicy with the accompanying Chinese mustard.  They were so tender you could cut them with your fork. *5. House Special Fried Rice with Scallops was so good!! It almost reminded me of a risotto, creamy with lots of scallops and peas.  This is how you can tell this restaurant is a five star establishment, only a real foody can probably appreciate this but in the fried rice there were peas, not just your easy-ordinary-frozen-from-a-bag peas but fresh-someone-took-the-time-to-depod-real peas...I can't even imagine who's job it is to sit in the kitchen and take peas out of a pod for a fried rice dish...but I thank them because it made it that much more amazing.  *6. Shrimp and Lobster Chow Fun, this was another great dish, with a whole lobster (deshelled), giant shrimp, big chow fun noodles, and baby bok choy.  It was so tasty.7. Whole Peking Duck, This dish was just ok...I really wanted to try it, to compare it to Peking Duck House's version, and can say don't order it here..Its like the most expensive thing on the menu and you can find something tastier here for the money.*8. Charred Filet of Beef, So tender, it was like butter in my mouth.  This piece of beef was cooked to perfection, and then they top it off with this sauce, omg, this sauce was like heaven.  I don't know what was in it but it was def butter.  I tried every dish with a little bit of that sauce..so goodSo last but not least our desserts..Some how we ended up getting two chocolate desserts which I normally don't do but both sounded fabulous so that's what we chose.  From the first few bites I think my body wanted to go into a chocolate/sugar diabetic coma, but I pushed through it, because they were so amazing.*9.  Chocolate Mille Feuille, was this chocolate piece of art filled with bruled bananas, spiced chocolate ice cream, and this decorative avocado anglaise sauce (don't be afraid of the avocado, its sweet and creamy and you don't have to eat it, if you don't want).10. The last thing was this peanut butter chocolate pudding with cinnamon whipped cream, I don't recall what it was called but it doesn't seem to be on the regular menu.  The gooey dark chocolate and peanuts were absolutely amazingly delicious!And so to all my fellow Yelpers, especially the one that ordered fried rice here without egg in it (I won't name names) and all the scenesters without a clue, Buddakan is not only a beautiful restaurant with beautiful people, but they serve up amazingly creative and flavorful dishes that ONLY DESERVE TO BE EATEN by people that truly appreciate food for the art that it can be.

Buddakan is quickly becoming known as Steven Starr's monstrosity of a restaurant/bar.  My friend and I went on a restaurant hopping bonanza last month and Buddakan happened to be the last stop.  Although we were completely stuffed from the restaurant and bar we hit before Buddakan, we ordered 2 appetizers and each had two drinks from the drink specials.  WHAT A TREAT!  The crab rolls were amazing.. that is the dish I would recommend.  The drinks we ordered were all fruit infused and unique, although a bit pricey.  What you really come to this venue for is the ambiance.  Trendy, dark, asian.  Mr. Star must word associate the word "vase" when someone mentions the word "Asian" since they are everywhere!!  In the bathrooms, on the sides of the restaurant, downstairs, near the bar area.. etc.  Downstairs is a real treat, the high celings, motifs on the walls, secret caves and long banquet tables complete the feel to this spectacular restaurant.  Come for the atmosphere, stay for the food and drinks... and oh yes, check out the vases.

While the interior is impressive (decorated kind of like the Viceroy Hotel in Santa Monica, but with dark wood), the service was terrible the first time I went.  We had a reservation, but had to wait for a table for 40 minutes...time does pass quickly there though as it is very scene-y and the techno-house music makes it a good party atmosphere, if not a bit meat-marketish.  Even though we were a huge table (12 people = huge tab especially with drinkers), we did not have enough wait staff and therefore people had to wait to get dishes, etc. and the wait staff was pretty rude when a couple friends tried to join us and pull up extra seats.

The second time I went with a girlfriend- we still had a wait an hour for our 9pm table reservation, but the downstairs library bar is nice and chill...the cocktails are good esp. prosecco with berries drink (think it's called the Charm?) and our waiter could have been a stand-up comedian.  The edamame dumplings while rich, were very good as was the mushroom chow fun (not too salty), steamed Chilean sea bass rolls (heavenly!), deviled egg tuna tartar, and chili rock shrimp were all very good.  We were stuffed after grazing on hot and cold small plates, but inspired by the dessert list and indulged in a peanut butter ice cream, creme fraiche, and chocolate number...yummmmm!

This is a good place to go before you go out...definitely puts you in a "going out" mood!

Housed in a big cavernous building that was once a cookie factory, this restaurant is a dramatic, (though somewhat stark) eatery in Chelsea.  The dark, unassuming grey entrance outside opens into a gigantic bi-level restaurant inside and definitely has a 'design hotel' ambiance.  Two greeters welcome you as you enter a whole team of hostesses stand behind the lobby reception-style desk to check you in for your reservation.  If possible, get your table downstairs where you'll see soaring ceilings, immense chandeliers and big murals of Adam and Eve by the bathroom.The food is Asian Fusion, with a few traditional dishes like the Peking duck.  I loved the Pork Belly appetizer and tuna spring rolls.  My date had the deviled tuna tartare, which was excellent.  It was spiced and dressed tuna with capers on top of egg salad.  Not the usual, but very very good. My entrée was the ginger crusted Mongolian Lamb which was perfectly cooked and highly recommended.  I had the blueberry butter cake for dessert which was substantial, and should definitely be shared.  The cake was warm and went really well with the corn ice cream.  They have some nice cocktails, and I enjoyed the 'Fate' (as in I like to leave my dining future to...) It was the perfect summer cocktail with pineapple juice, elderflower and prosecco.  Service is spot-on, the staff knows what they like and are happy to describe their favorites.
Great food, great atmosphere (except for the fact I was dining with my elderly parents), and a great crowd.  Is it the best food in the city, no.  Was the entire experience worth it, Yes!
The space is really fantastic, and the architecture "wows" (if that can be a verb). The grand, main dining room is 2 or 3 stories high and beautiful. The rest of the restaurant has a nice urban/Asian chic feel to it.  If you want to sit in the main room, make sure you include that requirement in your reservation, though, because the place holds about 200 tables and fewer than half are situated in the great room.The food is just okay. We had the Peking duck, the salmon, a tasty peanut noodle dish, and a bevy of appetizers. Nothing was bad. Nothing was great. I'm tempted to call the place over-rated.One of my dining companions put it well when he alluded to the chef's home turf by saying, "it's like Philadelphia's attempt at Asian fusion in New York."  Another predicted "the place will be packed with customers from New Jersey within a few months."They're both right.
By far the most incompetent management in the city this evening. The wait to pick up one's checked coat was over 20 minutes. The line was probably 70 people deep. And after the wait, having handed them my ticket, they had no record of my coat. They needed a lengthy description and another 5 minutes scouring their closet. And at the end, not even an apology. As a former regular, I won't be returning regardless of the need to check a coat.
HELLOOOO sexy Buddakan!  Walking into this restaurant is overwhelming in a good way. At first you find yourself getting the attention of the busy (but pretty) hostesses and then led into a dark, mysterious, and quite noisy lounge packed with customers. Our party of 3 was seated promptly in the dining area, which was at the bottom of double grand staircases. Every part of this restaurant was pretty and did I mention sexy? Now onto important stuff - the food. - The appetizer platter sampler was pretty good, a slight twist on dim sum. I would have liked something more savory, instead of fried items, but maybe I was just too hungry...- For the main course, shared family style, we had 4 dishes. The Spicy Crab and Shan Tong Noodles - probably my favorite dish of the night. The dish offered a good amount of heat that surprisingly didn't last in your mouth (I secretly wanted it to last). Loved it! The sizzling short rib was cooked to a perfect tenderness. If I were to give a small suggestion, I would have liked a seared crust on the outside for a more bold flavor. It was still good. We had a newer fish menu item I don't remember the name of... It was a stir fry dish with pieces of fish and vegetables on top of a fried exoskeleton part of the fish. (Hard to explain it) I wasn't wow'd by this dish because the tastes were mediocre. I think it needed some black pepper. I would have preferred the whole fish presented to me like how most Asian restaurants cook their fish. It locks in the flavors and most importantly, the moisture of the fish's meat. I guess they chop it up so people don't complain about deboning the fish themselves. We also had the vegetable rice with coconut foam. - For dessert we had the almond tapioca ice cream sandwich and banana fritters. I was not a fan of the cherries that came with the tapioca ice cream - I prefer fresh fruit instead of the ones you get in a cherry pie.  I really liked the banana fritters. It was filling and topped off all of insane amount of food I had just ate. At the end -- I was pleased.Our waiter was awesome too. She was spunky and extremely excited about the food we were about to eat. I would give it 5 stars, but I know I'm paying at least 3 times as much for the experience.
LOVED it. In the busy Meat Packing District so it's super close to a bunch of other restaurants, bars, lounges, clubs... It's a HUGE restaurant with a lounge/restaurant/bar upstairs and an even huge-r room (called the Grand Room) downstairs. Definitely recommend making reservations at the Grand Room, particularly if you have a large party. It's a huge space, but even if you go w/ a small party (it was just me and my date) you will not feel out of place as the service is very good and managed to retain a level of intimacy. The food was surprisingly good, I always worry about the *trendy* places but we enjoyed it. The rock shrimp dish was delicious... I recommend relying on your server as there is a wide selection. Desserts are also very good... especially the peanut butter/chocolate concoction, it was a delicious melted mess and I liked my fingers clean!All the drinks were also outstanding... you have to check it out, worth at least one experience. Prices were fine... I think it was only $200 for 2 of us which included tax/tip and a disgusting amount of cocktails, desserts, appetizers, entrees... oink oink.

Simultaneously old-fashioned  hip, Buddakan blends medieval decor with tropical fauna in a vast space that's very easy to walk right past. Came at 5:30 when they opened up for dinner and were sat downstairs, not in the lounge (which filled up quite quickly before we departed). The Calamari Salad appetizer was surprisingly flavorful, the chilled udon noodles the best I've had, and the Kung Pao monkfish was spectacularly spicy yet not overpowering. Service was solid, portions tremendous (especially for the value--though drinks were a bit steep), and the ambiance was certainly nicer once more folks arrived to drown out the tunes. Happy we hit it up before the Chef departed for Asia.
Really awesome!  Fabulous ambiance - glamour to the hilt.  Gracious service...  and sexy in every way.  Must try from the menu; Edamame Dumplings and Peking duck.
The wait was definitely worth it!  Finally got reservations and had a fabulous meal last night at Buddakan.  I'm still thinking about the meal  the place itself....  After having dined at the Buddakan in Philadelphia a few times, I wouldn't have thought I'd be giving 5 stars to Buddakan NY but I think it totally deserves it! Not only is this place gorgeous inside but they actually serve up some good food!  The interior is sexy, grand, elegant, modern, and hip.  One of those places where you walk in, and you feel either you're just too cool for school or not cool enough.  Yes, it's somewhat obnoxious but I appreciated it for what it's worth... esp when I looked down on the grand banquette table downstairs with the super high ceilings and these lovely chandeliers hanging down.  As for the food... we started with 3 app's, which were all delicious.  The lobster egg rolls were delicious, as were the sea bass rolls.  The taro lollipops were OK but nothing I would get again.  For our main dishes, we had the tea smoked chicken (pretty good but a bit bland compared to the other much more flavorful dishes we had), short ribs (so tender and so good... even the table next to us asked what we were eating and commented, "we should've ordered that... damn... next time."), and my favorite of the night -- the spicy blue chili crab dish with egg noodles.  Nice shreds of crab meat mixed in spices with noodles, scallions, etc.  As for desserts (we somehow made room for a few!), we ordered the crying chocolate (white chocolate ganache in warm chocolate cake w/ espresso ice cream on the side) and the pumpkin souffle.  Didn't care for the latter but the former was tasty.The last pleasant surprise of the Buddakan experience was the price... definitely not a cheap eats spot but for all the great food we had and good service, it was very reasonably priced.  Thus, great food at a good price, awesome ambiance, and throw in a few celeb sightings and interesting people-watching... I'm going to stick to 5 stars!
I was told by a friend who lives in Philly (that's where the original location is) that this is the best restaurant EVER.  And when I heard that I just thought don't get too excited because we all know what happens when you over-hype something - it's a letdown.  But I'll have you know Buddakan was definitely not a let down.  It was probably the best meal I have ever had in NYC.  And I do eat out A LOT!  We started with some cocktails - obviously.  They all have cute names...mine was jealously.  I'd like to say I sampled some others but it was so freakin' good I just stuck with that.  For apps we got scallion pancakes - seems unoriginal I know, but they were fantastic!!  We also got the edamame dumplings b/c everyone raved about them...and they were very good.  But just a little note, they are very subtle in flavor, not bland, but they won't knock you out.  Ok now here's where it gets funny.  My friends and I aren't huge seafood fans and I heard the chicken was not good so we ordered 3 meat dishes.  The lamb chops, the filet of beef and the short rib were all amazing!!!  I honestly can't pick a favorite of the three.  Even though we were all feeling a tad bit full we decided to just go ahead and gain a nice round 10 lbs and order dessert.  We got the peanut thing (can't remember the name) and the Crying Chocolate.  Again, both were AMAZING!!Oh and a final note on service - the hostess who led us to our table was the friendliest woman, as was our waitress.  I did go to dinner at 7pm on a weekday - so maybe that's why they were in good spirits (no annoying, late night, out-of-towners (no offense of course)).  While I hate to give it up to my friend - Buddakan is worth all the hype!!

Checking into Buddakan is like checking into a five start hotel, with over five girls at the counter ready to check you in, take your coats and escort you to the bar while your table is being readied.The ambiance is amazing, you feel like you are walking into a action thriller movie, where you expect actors to jump off the balcony and swing on the massive chandeliers.  WOW is all i have to say about the  massive space which has been very appointed in the trendiest of furnishings.The lobster egg rolls were crispy and steaming hot, the Rock shrimp was creamy and savory, but the tea infused chicken with baby bok choy and crab fried rice were an explosion of flavors that will take to a place you never want to leave.The cauliflower kimchi was fiery, the mushroom chow fun was calm but sassy and the New York Strip with a soy glaze was like Saigon and NYC going at in your mouth!The food, the ambiance, the attitude - worth every Benjamin.
Hi Five!  This is a gem waiting to be found. I must have walked by "Buddakhan" several times not noticing it (it blends in like a cameleon as a part of Chelsea Market). I live right in the neighborhood and it lived up to all expectations. First off, the place in gorgeous inside and the food is even more exquisite. It's not exactly cheap (runs about $50/person), but trust me, the quality and presentation of the food is what you pay for. We ordered the monk fish kung pao and the tuna tatar appetizer. Both were presented beautifully and absolutely delicious. What's even more amazing is how quality is maintained, in spite of the hundreds of people who come here each night, so definitely gets an A for consistency. Definitely the best Asian fusion restaurant I've been to in NYC. Come here with a date, friends, out of town guest, and make sure you dress up as well!

Buddakan's one of my three 5-star restaurants in the city! I love the space (ex-Nabisco factory converted to 2-storey restaurant) AND the menu (food and cocktails). I really like their take on dim sum. My favorites are the edamame dumplings and taro puff lollipops, as well as the shaken chill beef tartare and glazed alaskan black cod from the cold appetizer and fish menus respectively. The desserts are impeccable. I'm hoping there will be new additions to the menu the next time I visit.  Buddakan's is a great place to take someone who has an interest in trendy restaurants and appreciate good food. I've seen couples, groups, families, and after-work crowds and I'm definitely taking my parents here the next time they visit. My point is, trendy places can serve up good food too!  I try not to be suckered by the Buddhist theme but, so far, Tao and Buddakan have impressed me with their food and ambience. Next, Buddha Bar? :)

From SATC to Top Chef, Buddakan could easily fall into that trap of being overhyped. I've been to way too many asian fusion restaurants with poor execution or plain lack of creativity. First of all I warn you that even if you have a reservation time, it appears that you're never seated on time. It's probably because the hostess knows they're so busy, it doesnt really even need your patronage. A 350 seat restaurant according to our waiter, and the layout is absolutely gorgeous, you certainly cant get this ambiance in San Francisco.  Unfortunately we werent placed in the main room, DKNY apparently had booked the 40 seat center table for the night. Tucked away into a corner, it was actually still quite nice, though we were surrounded by several 16 seat tables that just seemed too large.As for the food, some absolute standouts, and some that were just OK.. 1) Edamame dumplings with truffle oil-Absolute standout, the truffle oil is not overwhelming. SO GOOD that I decided to get another order as my dessert 2) Hoisin glazed pork belly with buns-When did pork belly enter the NYC conscience and go on every menu?#1 Momofuku #2 Buddkan #3 Ippudo3) Miso glazed black cod w eggplant relish and black bean foam-No clue what the foam was about. Excellent piece of fish but it would be more of a shame if they messed it up.4) Charred fillet of beef w mustard-well cooked but nothing special and certainly didnt have much asian flare to it5) Broken chili chicken, thai basil, chinese pepper-visually gorgeous, my friends really liked it, but I thought the sauce was more memorable then the actual chicken which was basically breaded and sliced6) Almond bread pudding w whiskey ice cream-actually was an excellent dessert, but Ill admit I only had a taste since I was busy eating another round of edamame dumplingsAll in all a well executed asian fusion menu with some memorable dishes, ambiance of course is amazing, even the bathrooms are fun. I would probably give it 3.5 stars but on yelp a 4 because I love the main dining room!
I decided to take a friend here for his 30th birthday to celebrate, I made reservations surprisingly it had a really good crowd for a Monday evening. We were seated quickly, and given ample time to look over the menu. We ordered the scalion pancakes  for an appetizer which were a tad salty and greasy. The drinks were cute however none of the signature cocktails were strong, more so sweet and danty. When it cametime to order the main course I decided to order chicken as the last time I dined there I ordered from the seafood menu and was disappointed in the portions of the food. I ordered the the Broken Chili chicken $22, lobster fried rice $16, which we shared the rice. The chicken was a bit salty and not spicy at all for something with chili in the name.  Needless to say 1. I was diappointed in the portion of the food for the money they charge one piece of chicken is not sufficient the rice bowl was no where near full. My friend decided to go with something from the meat portion of the menu the sizzling short rib $26 which was tastey and I would say a sufficient portion. Dessert was good and a sweet ending with Happy Birthday written on the plate and a candle. The overall ambiance of the restaurant is very nice. However they need to up the game on their food portions VERY disappointing for such a well known 5 star restaurant.

This place is a good example of why food is all that matters to me when it comes to eating out. For starters, "Asian fusion" is a term I've heard much of, and it seems like one "Asian fusion" joint is opening up every ten minutes on the street corner of the chic area of some American metropolis. This does not mean, however, that the food is bad. Most experiences for me at "Asian fusion" joints have been enjoyable, and Buddakan would be no different. When my mom announced that this is where she had reservations to, I asked how she heard about the place. After telling me a friend recommended it, she also stated that this place had been featured on "Sex and the City." Sorry, fans of that show, but I started to doubt if I would enjoy this place upon hearing that. Upon entering Buddakan, I was taken aback by the atmosphere. Very dark in terms of coloring, and full of beautiful young people, who decided to come eat here after they had finished their shopping sprees at the Banana Republic. As a 22 yr old with his two parents, we looked slightly out of place, but I got over it. Remember, it's about food. And good god, the food. We got things going with the pork belly, the lobster egg rolls, and the spare ribs. My favorite was the pork belly, but the other two were also incredibly delicious in their own right. For dinner, we ordered the rib-eye, the fillet, and the lamb chops to all share. The rib-eye was hands down my favorite of the three, but the other two were delicious, especially the lamb chops. The drinks were good, and I was happy that they served Brooklyn lager, which I became a fan of during my trip. Our server was extremely knowledgeable and friendly, meaning that our whole experience was perfect. I would go back here in a heartbeat, all for the food!
I have been here about 5 times, and never been disappointed. The edamame dumplings are amazing.   Everything I have ordered here is great.  They have a drink called 'fever' - it has jalapeno in it...how much better than that can you get? This is the place I bring friends when they are visiting, because the food is amazing and the place is beautiful.
Adventures with an Expense Account (part II):Last night, Monday, we had a large corporate dinner at Buddakan.  Reservations for 6:30 and got the large communal table on the lower level.  The food was served family style, with a preset menu, and the alcohol was flowing, from a preset menu.  The food (approx 6 types of dim sum / apps, 5 types of entrees, and 6 types of dessert) and booze (sake, red and white wine, cocktails) were mostly great!  I wish I could describe everything we were served, I can't, but I can tell you my favorites!Dim Sum / Apps:- Edamame Dumplings- Tuna Spring RollsEntrees:- Sweet Crispy Jumbo Shrimp- Roasted duck served with cucumber, scallions, hoisin sauceDessert:- Crying Chocolate- White Chocolate Rice PuddingThe Pinot Noir and the Malbec were great and the Silence tea I ordered with the dessert was really nice too!All and all the service was wonderful, however a little heavy on the alcohol pouring, and we all had a great time!Thanks Buddakan
Okay - I understand why people like this place.  It's got really amazing decor and tasty, unusual cocktails.  However, it's really expensive, and I found that the food wasn't really anything to write home about.  As other reviewers have mentioned, you can get something tastier in Chinatown for a quarter of the price.  On the other hand, that wouldn't be as trendy.  That's really the selling point of this establishment - that they're hip and exclusive, and that's why they book you for a 10pm reservation and then make you wait another two hours to be seated.  There are so many places to eat in New York City - if you repeatedly get told that it'll "just be a few minutes," you may want to hightail it elsewhere.
The decor of this place is so impressive! The space is huge and you feel like you are in an Emperor's palace from Asia. Each room is spacious, dark and filled with modern antique like vases. Although we ate upstairs, the downstairs room is amazing! Once you look down, you see a long table with 3 huge chandeliers. This would be a perfect place for a large party.For Valentine's day, I dined here with 3 other lovely ladies. The cuisine is fusion, upscale Chinese. Everything is meant to be shared family style. Everything was presented in a beautiful, unique fashion. For starters we shared four appetizers:Deviled tuna tartare: Delicious, fresh tuna was mixed with avocado and diced eggs. Steamed sea bass wrapped with lettuce: This was really light and fresh.Chili rock shrimp: These tasted like popcorn shrimp flavored with spicy chili oil. VERY good!Scallion pancakes: These were SO good, crispy onion pancakes topped with braised short ribs and julienned apples. This is a must order!For our entrees, we also shared four:Peking duck: juicy, tender meat and crispy skin were served with scallions, cucumbers, and hoisin sauce on the side. You take a mini tortilla and wrap it in all the ingredients. Fun and SO good.Lobster meat and eggplant: Huge lobster meat diced and stir fried with black bean sauce. Lamb chops: mini lamb chops were also very juicy and tenderSweet  Sour scallops: really good and the sauce was served with an unique combination, corn and black beans.Dessert was yummy! We had the white chocolate frozen parfait with kumquat ice cream. The white chocolate just tasted like ice cream.. and the tart flavor from the kumquat ice cream was a really good combinations. We also shared the coconut souffle. It was very airy and light and it was served with a side of sauteed pineapples. Overall, I would highly recommend coming here if you want to go out big. The atmosphere in itself is worth coming here. It's very New York!

I think Buddakan is really good, and for a place that does about a thousand covers a night the food is fantastic.I'm really skeptical about mega-restaurants such as Buddakan, because many times I have been disappointed with TAO which after all started this trend. Buddakan manages to impress with its decor, the huge drop for its main dining hall and most importantly its food, I'm writing this review just after my 5th time dining there, and the food is very impressive for the price. This is my favorite Nobu-esque spot but Chinese cuisine.  Request the cozy Library Room, where you can watch people at the hidden bar, or enjoy the glow from the rooms Golden lighting.As you head down their grand stairwell, and enter the ballroom dining room, complete with chandeliers, and pure luxury decor, the Library room offers a more intimate feel.Food is delicous, the lollipop taro puffs are cleverly presented.  The dishes we shared were all tasty, and the fusion approach was quite sucessful.  This is one of those places where you have to be ready to paint the town red, compete with a sexy dress, clutch, and an eye candy in tow.  The patrons are very city chic, the reservations must be made, the hostesses quite numerous, due to the size of this place.  Even with reservations, expect to wait.  Typical NYC...  Which brings me to the point, that beautiful places have no bearings to how the food is.  Case in point-I've been to Spice Market, when that was the place to go, and despite the beautiful decor, the food was never quite up to par, and I had returned a few times to make sure I wasn't there on an off night...  but Buddakan truly comes up on top as the place to go, for the decor, the people watching, and the food.  So I don't mind if this is the cool trendy place to go, as long as they keep the food tasty, the service good, and the decor well maintained.  I plan on coming back as soon as possible!  This place is yummy chic!!!

Went there last Saturday for a last minute bday dinner. While we couldn't score a table in the actual dining room (thanks for nothing, credit card concierges!!!), we were able to find seating in the bar area right away and, after looking around a bit helplessly for a few minutes or so, even secured our server for the night. We started with a few drinks (Charm, Tranquility, Splash), all of which were tasty. For appetizers, we went with the edamame dumplings as so many folks here had recommended them, the tuna tartare spring rolls and the scallion pancakes. I will agree that the dumpling filling reminded me of baby food as well, they were tasty but not something I'd order again. The pancakes and the short ribs were tasty but the meat was a bit too cold when the dish arrived at the table. The tuna spring rolls were my favorite, although the dough around the fish threw me off...as I always thought egg rolls were friend and spring rolls were not. However, still very, very tasty!We followed up with one Asian sausage fried rice, the sweet and sour chicken and the spiced tofu. I would recommend skipping the tofu dish as the tofu itself was spongy, flavorless and soggy and the veggies a bit too oily. The sweet and sour chicken was good but lacked flavor (think boiled chicken...watery). The fried rice was def. my favorite and the fact that it was a huge dish didn't hurt either. All in all, we spent less than 150 on 3 drinks, 3 appetizers and 3 main courses - and that includes tip already - for a trendier place in the city, this really isn't bad. Although, previous reviewers were spot on about the water: we had to ask to even get any in the first place and had to continuously ask for refills.
I could come here every single day and enjoy a Tranquility (citrus vodka and lemongrass-infused oolong tea) and the tuna tartare spring rolls and be the happiest person alive.  Throw in the edamame dumplings (which are beyond anything the name could conjure up) and the lobster and shrimp chow fun and you could convince heaven exists and I am in it.  The menu is so extensive from drinks to dim sum to main dishes to dessert that you would be remiss to not try everything you could even though you have favorites that you crave the moment you leave your table.  the decor is stunning, from the Moorish cut out doorways and enormous vases that could have been cut from said doorways to the chandelier-draped dining room with the extremely high ceilings.  Our server was knowledgeable, sweet, and attentive as was the rest of the staff.  No sooner do you finish a dish than a suited gentleman who could be the secret service whisks away your plate to make room for the next course.  The sea bass roll was mild to the taste but I love that.  The broken chili chicken is not spicy but still lovely.  The snap peas and candy-crusted Mongolian lamb chops rounded out a fantasy birthday meal.  And the desserts, which I'm shocked we had room for, the Crying Chocolate and Almond Bread Pudding, I'm pretty sure only existed in my dreams until Saturday night.  The only question is, when I return can I break from my pattern of ordering what I already know I love to explore their other offerings...we shall see....

I last ate at Buddakan almost a year back. But the awesome memories of the food that evening still remain with me.It was a Monday evening, and my friend and i had reserved a table beforehand. But when we reached there we found a huge crowd, and were told that we would have to wait for sometime inspite of booking in advance. We bought a couple of drinks and waited in the lounge, and this gave me time to soak in the surroundings.I had been told that it was a Asian and European fusion restaurant. When i entered the restaurant, i immediately looked upon a wall to wall picture, of a Venetian neighbourhood, canals and gondolas and everything. Just that the people were Chinese. The fusion theme was driven home into me as nothing else possibly could :)After some time we were asked to follow someone to our table and we walked behind him, and walked, and walked, and walked. The sheer size of this place is stunning. I can confidently say that this is the biggest restaurant i have ever been to.The food, especially the desserts, were very very tasty. However the service was what was more impressive. My friend is a vegetarian, and when the young lady who was serving us discovered that, she promptly informed her that the veg fried rice that she had ordered had some seasoning which was made of some fish product (which my friend obviously did not know of) and went on to suggest a number of other alternatives. I have rarely seen anyone quite so educated about the intricacies of the menu of the place.It is one of the more expensive places i have been to in New York, but the food and the experience is worth every cent of it.

Fantastic food, fantastic service, fantastic ambiance, fantastic experience!My wife and I went this past Friday night. We showed up right on time for our reservation. The host seemed to know my first name immediately upon me saying my last name, which was a neat trick. We were immediately and politely escorted to the lounge where we waited only a few minutes before a very serious looking man with an ear piece came to escort us to our table. He carried our drinks and walked us all the way to the back of this huge restaurant to what had to be the worst table in the house. We sat there for a few minutes, but then went back to find the man and ask for a better table. He told us to wait 20 minutes and within 10 minutes we were very politely taken to what had to be the best seat in the house. A four top in the main downstairs room where the two of us could sit side by side and both face the room. An extremely friendly waiter then came by and helped us select some of the best food we've ever eaten. Really. The frogs leg appetizer and Kung Pao Monkfish were two of the best thing's I've ever eaten anywhere. We order second helpings of both! Other appetizers and entrees we ordered were also great.The place is clearly a business... meaning they move you in, move you out and turn over the table... no table clothes, food arrives as its ready, sit you long enough in the lounge to by a drink before dinner, etc. But, given what their overhead must be in a place that big its understandable, and its done with such tact and class, you barely notice, let alone mind.That was our one experience. We're heading there again this coming weekend to see if its really that great consistently... and because I'm hooked on the Kung Pao fish!

Philly's original is better... Steven Starr empire expands. Can't help but feel the commercialized chain but it's a trendy scene with a variety of cool dining rooms, food is satisfactory and does great with groups.
The restaurant has an amazing atmosphere; the main dining room is downstairs but open two stories up with huge chandeliers hanging overhead and wax-caked candlesticks on the tabletops. The side area in which we ate has pictures of Buddha heads randomly lit on the walls, and a dark environment that gives a sense of privacy.Our server was very good and well informed about the food on the menu and made some excellent suggestions. The food is served family style, which was a great way to get tastes of several different dishes. Though the serving sizes and presentations seemed generally like a standard one-person entrees.We started with a few appetizers, including the General Tso's Dumpling, which was stuffed with chicken, ginger and garlic, which were served right from the steamer basket. I found the Crispy Calamari Salad with green apples, cashews, and a miso vinaigrette also to be very good. I was tempted to order the frog legs, but we shied away. The steamed sea bass roll with cabbage, ginger, sizzling scallion oil was good, tender and buttery, but a little forgettable.We tried three main courses, and my favorite was the rich and flavorful Sizzling Short Rib with mushroom chow fun (noodles), and Asian pear. The meat was tender and a little fatty, the pear was refreshing, and the mushrooms and noodles were a great compliment. Next on my list was the Glazed Alaskan black cod with chili eggplant, black bean relish. The fish was light and flaky and the black bean relish was a nice flavor to go with it. The last dish served was a seared pork tenderloin with wild mushrooms, lotus scented rice, Chinese bacon. This was good, but I think we were all starting to get full and so it wasn't a favorite. I also felt like the rice, was a bit strong, but the tea-like flavor was good. We also ordered a side of charred asparagus that was amazing (for asparagus), it was not stringy, and had a great flavor with a "black bean foam."Capping off the meal was a great cup of cappuccino and a Tempura Apple Fritter (essentially fried apple rings) with Saigon cinnamon anglaise (a white, creamy sauce) and salt and pepper caramel (a sauce that I found to be a little too peppery, or perhaps too dark of a caramel). Overall it was a great meal, with lots more on the menu I'd like to try. Combine that with top-notch service and it made for an excellent way to celebrate our birthdays!

In short, Buddakan can be summed up in 2 words: edamame dumplings.  I don't even LIKE edamame, but when it's dumplingized and creamy, apparently I love it.  And any trip to Buddakan without them would be akin to visiting Paris without catching a glimpse of the Eiffel Tower.  Actually, most of the appetizers and desserts are great, but the mains are a notch or two below.  Since everything is served family style, I'd recommend a tapas type approach with lots of appetizers instead of a multi-course meal.  And as far as the space, worth a visit in and of itself -- dual height ceilings, dim lighting, terrific vibe for a nice meal with friends, when the parents are in town, or on a date.  A great transplant from Philly -- now if only Tequila's would follow suit...

So New year comes around and one of many restaurants that I decide to hit up to have a celebratory holiday dinner at Buddakan. I've always wanted to come here and there we go.. Getting a reservation is easy if you decide to have an earlier dinner like before 7pm or after 10pm since people tend to eat during peak dinner hours.  I managed to get a reservation at 7:15pm on New years day for a party of 3 which is like suprising since it was a last minute thing. whoopiee..The Place is awesome;  once you enter the place, you feel like you are in a buddhist monastery in the middle of Bhutan with fake books on the side as fixtures. The bright yellow colors along with the jumbo size buddha pictures all over the main dining room along with a huge chandelier makes you want to say to yourself, " what the hell am I doing here for dinner?" . For the starters, My two guests had the Crispy Calamari Salad, spare ribs and the Chili Rock shrimp. I had the Vegan dumplings. The Crispy Calamari Salad was pretty good; a sizeable plate with at least 10 pieces of fried calamari and it was actually crunchy and not heavy as some other places would serve this salad. The Chili Rock Shrimp is to die for. Not to heavy or light the shrimp and the miso dressing just melts into your mouth. soooo good. As for the ribs, my two guests deemed it was beyond good but looking at the ribs for me makes me want to puke since I don't eat pork. ( even if i ate pork i would of not liked it because they only had 3 little ribs on the plate wtfff). As for the dumplings go, they were pretty decent. They were not overly stuffed like chinatown dumplings nor they were greasy which is a plus. As for the entrees I ordered the steamed sole and a side order of the asian veggie stir fry. my other two guest decided to order one entree since one of them has a stomach of a 5 year old and decided to order the beef short ribs. The Steamed sole was outrageously good. It was the breaking point for me in determining if this place was actually good or was it just another overly hyped place. The sole was light and flaky which is what the fish should be. It was not drenched in sodium nor did i taste any MSG. the ginger and the green onion made the fish retain it's natural flavors without overpowering the pungent smells of the green onions.  It was just a work of art. As for the short ribs, I only had a taste of it and it was pretty well made. one big piece of beef rib probably simmered in a pot for hours and served on top of some chow fun noodles. The meat wasn't hard at all and it was just pretty decent. The party of three ate like kings during the meal. The waiters were attentive nor pushy and actually recommended the dishes for me since I was watching my weight. Such a delightful meal. Next time, I hope i can score a seat at the communal table downstairs!

NY location was just as wonderful. I missed the big Buddha of the Philly restaurant though, but ambiance was great. Food was just as outstanding as I remembered.  My food suggestions: My only negative would be the deviled tuna tartar.  Its not bad but it has egg in it that totally takes over the entire tuna taste. If you like egg, go for it. Ok onto the yummy stuff.  Appetizers: Any of the dumplings and the seabass rolls. Entrées: peking duck is incredible  priced accordingly. I also suggest the ginger lobster. It gives you an amazing size portion of the tail and claws so if you're a lobster lover...this is your way to go. Side: lobster fried rice for a side (duh...it had to be done). Veggie: you cant go wrong with a simple asian vegetable stir fry for ur veggie. Service was incredible and we had a great guy who was fun and used to work at the Philly restaurant as well so, he really knew his stuff. They also have wonderful speciality drinks like Longevity that are all named for peace, love and happiness feel. Great place to celebrate special occassions, impress on a first date or for a night on the town.

However, wouldn't order this again.General tso dumplings - Soup dumplings with a twist. this isn't your typical joe shanghai xiao long bao, but it's still good.Boneless spare ribs - meh. It was forgettable.Rock shrimp - Greasy, saucy, but at least it's a decent portion of food. It tasted like sweet and sour shrimp rather than rock shrimp. Chilled udon noodles  vegetable fried rice - do NOT order this. You definitely need to order the crying chocolate dessert. the star of the night was the jasmine ice cream. WIN. also ordered the bread pudding, which was good, but not extraordinary.decor = 5/5. we sat at a very comfortable corner table.service (waitress name was megan I believe) = 5/5. She had the best line of the night when describing the bread pudding. "It's so good that it will answer questions you never knew you had." Um, too bad this wasn't true, but still - it convinced us to order it.overall, $40/pp including tip+tax (excluding drinks) so I thought the prices were VERY reasonable. Also, I would recommend ordering the prosecco at the bar since you inevitably will wait before sitting at your table. Would go again especially with out of town visitors! this place is infinitely better than Tao and priced much more reasonably.PS - the only reason I didn't give this a 5 is because the quality of the food is not extraordinary (3.5/5)....chilled udon noodles...*shudder*

As I embarked on my culinary journey through two major cities in the northeast, I decided to kick-off my adventure in a trendy, ultra-modern restaurant that I had first seen on the big screen. It was featured in the first full-length movie based on the popular television series about four single ladies who spent six seasons giving us insight into the dating scene in New York: Sex and the City. For those of you who are SATC fans, this is the restaurant where Carrie Bradshaw and Mr. Big had their glamorous wedding rehearsal dinner. After looking at the infinite number of items on the menu that looked appealing, we started with one of my all-time must-haves: the Deviled Tuna Tartare, with chili mayonnaise and scallions. While the pieces of tuna were very fresh, they lacked a bit of flavor. The ingredients were layered, not blended, taking away a bit from the potential of the dish. I enjoyed it, but it didn't stand out. We tried the Boneless Spare Ribs, which came with a bit of chinese mustard. Now we're talking. I really wouldn't have guessed this would be my prize winner, but it was. The ribs were tender and moist, and the glaze was delicious. My two favorites were the Sweet  Crispy Jumbo Shrimp and the Kung Pao Monkfish. And the dessert....well it blew my mind! For more information on Buddakan, and other restaurants, visit my page at adventuresofthefoodaholi….

What can get any more authentic than a Chinese person rating a Chinese restaurant?  Perhaps a Chinese born in China...but that's besides the point.  Buddakan has a very unassuming doorway that is simple and not imposing.  However, when you step in, it's a whole separate world that is transformed to take you somewhere between China, Italy, and New York.  With Cherubs dancing on the walls next to murals of the Meekong river, I was expecting italian sausage fried rice.  But I was quite surprised with how traditional some of their dishes are.  For starters, we had the scallion pankakes that were served with braised beef on top.  This was somewhat unfortunate because I love scallion pankakes and the taste of them were overpowered by the braised beef.  However, that said, the braised beef was increadible and very very very nicely done.  Other starters were the edamame dumplings, seasonal salad, and the chicken broth dumplings.  Of the appetizers, the chicken broth dumplings were the most dissappointing.  The reason being that they should've been made out of pork because in Chinese cooking, the fat that comes from steaming the dumplings is what creates the soup inside.  This can be found in typical shanghainese cuisine and is called "Shaio Loong Bao" or Little Dragon Bun.  For an entree, we all shared sweet and sour chicken, filet, veggies, fried rice, noodles, and a couple of other dishes.  We were a party of 5 and I would suggest that you get no more than 2 carb dishes.  Many of these are very traditional and I could hear my mother screaming at me for ordering these dishes at that price.   She would say: "I can make that entire meal for ten dollah...why you need to pay for that?"  Then I would say, but the ambiance and scene are partially what you pay for as well...and they definitely give you your money's worth.  Then she would mutter something under her breadth in Chinese and tell me I'm wasting my money.In total, for 5 ppl, stuffed to the gills with food and drinks, we walked out of there at $50/person which is not bad at all!  Great in fact considering all the time and fun we had there.  Definitely recommend and let me know how it goes for you!
