I dined with my friend on a Thursday night; we had a 6:30 reservation and we were seated immediately. This beautiful  restaurant has two levels, with many rooms. I had the Charm cocktail which was excellent. For the appetizers we ordered the Cantonese Spring Roll and the Tuna Spring Roll. Both items were outstanding. For the entrees we ordered the Charred Fillet of Beef (which was cooked to order) and the Hot and Sour Scallops. Both were excellent. For a side dish we ordered the Wok Noodles with Prawns. My boyfriend and I decided to try Buddakan for our pre-valentines day dinner.  As soon as I walked in, I was impressed by the decor, lighting and atmosphere.  I especially liked the dim lighting, it made it so much more intimate.  They were very prompt with the reservation, I didn't have to wait beyond the time it was made for.  The menu, unlike other places isn't over crowded with options.  For appetizers, we had the jasmine shrimp dumplings and the general tso dumplings.  The jasmine dumplings were by far so much better.  For the entrees, you basically get your protein and if you'd like something to go with it, you should order from the sides, however the portion size is enough to fill you up.  I had the broken chili chicken, which was with the sauce really good.  Finally, their desserts are so decadent.  My bf, who is very hard to pleased, absolutely loved the bread pudding and I had the most luscious melted chocolate ganache.  Overall, this is a really great restaurant with unique and delicious meal options, just expect to dish out a little.

Buddakan is sexy...so very very sexy. Buddakan is located on the upper edge of meatpacking on 9th avenue in a seriously inconspicuous building. Walk inside through the doors of the unimpressive structure and completely get transported to a different world. Stylish, trendy, cool, chic; name it, Buddakan is it. Music is played at a very reasonable level so conversation can still be kept but the tone and mood are still right. what really differentiates Buddakan for me though is the friendly service. Its hard to find a friendly face in meatpacking on the weekend, so the great service and smiling faces are a welcome change. The Asian fusion food is really well presented and never disappoints. Another obvious plus is that the main dining room and table were features in Sex and the City, so its always fun to take a fan of the series and the movies here for the first time. Always a good time, always good food and drinks. Come here on any occasion.

Absolutely beautiful presentation and detail in every aspect of Buddakan.It's like dining inside a glamorous castle. Downstairs is where it's at. I literally gasped the first time I dined here. You walk down banquet stairs (Think Beauty and the Beast: the formal dinner scene) and in the grand room is a long, long table (for your party of 20 or so, just eyeballing it). The space is gorgeous. High ceilings, sparkling chandeliers and the space is flooded with a warm, golden light. There is a "library" with glowing books, flanked by a bar of the premium kind.The drinks are fantastic (Try the "Fate"- Elderflowers, prosecco and pineapple). The food, although overpriced for Chinese fusion fare, is presented flawlessly and made with painstaking attention to detail and flavor. The Tuna Tartare spring roll is light and crispy, the chili rock shrimp is flavorful and sweet, the boneless spare ribs are tasty and the Shanghai soup dumplings (although extremely overpriced compared to Joe's Shanghai/Ginger) is worth the $14. They are light on the soup but heavy on flavor. I got the Charred Filet of Beef, which was delicious. It was well-made and not too heavy. A friend got the Hot  Sour Scallops, which although were very tasty (trusting his judgement since I didn't dare ask to try), but the portion was miniscule. Only two not-very-sizable scallops. The Sweet  Crispy Jumbo Shrimp was wonderful as well. It was a friend's birthday dinner so we ordered a cake and two bottles of wine, that greatly contributed to $80 per person for an eight person table. Normally it'd probably be a little less.if you're looking for an impressive place and are willing to pay for the atmosphere, then this is a perfect place to go. Cheers.

It was fun.  In comparison to Tao, where I've been to quite a few times, I have to say I had more fun here.  The decor isn't so Pacific tacky as Tao is.  In fact, it's quite the opposite.  Pictures on the wall have nothing to do with Eastern culture at times and actually spark interesting conversation instead leaving you thinking you've stepped into a bland pot of coffee like the other place.  It's dark and frankly you can't see much around you past 20 feet, but there's still an expansive sense of warmth all around you.  If you can, get seated downstairs.  If you're stuck upstairs near the bar, you're gonna have only the view of the more open downstairs and the view of buzzed people waiting by the bar for their tables.  We had a large group, and while we had to wait a while despite reservations (about 30-45 minutes,) it was worth it (but not well worth it.)  The dinner was interesting, imaginative, and fun (that's the 2nd time I've said it.)  Our waiter was helpful and funny.   It's very expensive for similar (or even better) tasting food prepared at more authentic Asian food places, given the fact that you can't really change standards like spring rolls, potstickers, general tso's, steamed sole, etc, and they don't even have some of the highly sought after Chinese dishes not popular among casual Chinese food diners.  The one saving grace are the desserts, which aren't necessarily anywhere close to authentic for Chinese food, but are more western in inspiration.

I think my 2nd visit was better due to the following: 1) we were seated in the main dining room (downstairs) in a booth seating and that was just amazing! I think that made all the difference in the world. The first time we went. We were seated upstairs in that one area with the windows looking down into the main dining room and just had the feeling, man.. i want to sit down there! So yeah, downstairs seating is great. 2) Our waiter the 2nd time introduced himself as having been working at the restaurant since it opened. He was extremely knowledgeable, helped us put our menu together, and took our drink orders quickly. He recommended a few different drinks and promised that if we didn't like them.. he would take them back. We had a few rounds of the Charm and Fate. Both were yummy and tasted like sparkling wine with fruit infusions, very light and refreshing :) One of my gf's didn't like her mojito.. it was made too strong the first time around, he quickly took it away and brought her a new one, much better. The first time we went.. i remember having the edamame dumplings, tuna tartare springrolls, chili rock shrimp, wild mushroom chowfun, sugar snap peas, king crab hot pot, etc. The other night we had again the edamame dumplings, tuna tartare spring rolls, the potstickers, the whole peking duck, wok tofu and brocolli, lobster fried rice, sizzling short rib and chili crab and crispy noodles. I would say they did a fabulous job on the duck just because it's really hard to get an entire duck de-fatted, and have the skin crispy. The duck wraps were a little too floury for my taste, but it was authentic still in the sense that they brought out the strips of cucumber and green onion. yum! The short rib was really tender and no fat as well! We also ordered for dessert: the crying chocolate, the 5 spice donuts, asian citron souffle, and the choco peanut butter bomb! the desserts were pretty amazing.. the choco peanut butter bomb was yummy with the peanut powder, it tasted like a glorified reese's that melted in your mouth, so if you like peanut butter... crying choco and souffle wasnt that amazing, but the donuts are yummy and unique esp with the pistachio crumbs on the cinnamon icecream! i do like buddakan :)
I'll start by saying that my one experience here was just at the bar for a couple of drinks.  The drinks were lovely but certainly pricey.  The place is beautiful, the ambiance was lively (it was packed of course)  people watching here was fun; there was plenty of eye candy. *Please Note: I went well before it was featured in Sex in the City so the crowd is likely more touristy. People watching here, I'm betting has a whole new meaning now.* However, getting a drink here can be a mission.  The bar was just as packed and busy as the main dining room.  Considering the price of the drinks  how busy it was I don't think it's worth the battle to get a table to eat here.  I saw many diners enjoying their meals but nothing looked so good (believe me, I was looking) nor were there people making, "Oh" faces so I could easily say, "I'll pass, at least till some of the fame dies down."  However, if someone went through the effort of getting us reservations here, I would indeed give it shot.
The edamame potstickers were amazing, also the lobster rolls, beef pancakes, very good. I would pass on the frog legs as they were tough and over cooked. Nice ambiance and cool decor
you know, the outside of the restaurant is surprisingly obscure. it's a huge door with a small sign that says 'buddakan.'then you walk in and see this service desk with attractive ladies on the other side, asking you if you have a reservation. felt like i was in a hotel.we got wine at the bar which is in this super loungey area. and i immediately felt rich and swanky. haha! we were escorted to our table and pass by this dramatic huge dining room that you needed to go down these steep stairs to get to. and then i thought, "wow. this ambiance is ridiculous!" then were sat on the main floor in the "red vase" room. and now for my food recommendations: the tuna tartare spring roll was AMAZING and delicious and ate it SO fast i didn't know where it went. the jade shrimp dumplings were fresh and yummy. the wild mushroom chow fun was awesome. but the showstopper by a mile was the edamame dumplings. they were SO creamy and interesting, they were the star. you must get them.the waitress was super bubbly and happy, and kept refilling our wine glasses. it was very expensive (my bill alone was $75) but it's worth it. it's a good time, cool ambiance, and it's fun to spend money while you're young!

This place is gorgeous.  It was in the Sex and the City movie as the place where Carrie and Big had their pre-wedding dinner party.  Also, a huge part of the appeal of coming here was that I got to meet Dale Talde who works in the kitchen, and by the way who was absolutely ROBBED on Top Chef by contestants far less talented than him.Okay okay, onto the food :)You have to try the Edamame Dumplings!  They're indescribably good and so innovative.  The Scallion Pancakes were delicious and the apple really makes the dish complete.  The kicker was this crab dish that our waiter recommended to us (I can't seem to find it on the online menu?).  Basically it was 2 crabs cut in half and fried so that you could eat it whole...and there was this amazing, slightly spicy sauce that you could dip it into.  Pure perfection.Other things we got to eat were the Whole Peking Duck and the Lobster Fried Rice.  There were nothing special, but delicious nonetheless.

BEST AND CHEAPEST CHINESE RESTAURANT IN NYC!Yep, i said it.  And i'm not drunk!  Here's an unforgettable meal at Buddakan: mao poe tofu ($14: one of the best preprations of the classic dish, gives hakkasan's michelin rated counterpart in london a run for its money), sauteed water convolvulus ($7: esoteric tubular veggie, no longer on the menu, ask for it, if not get the asian green stir fry) and chinese sausage fried rice with a sunny side egg on the top (yeah, it's the way it's done "out there", none of the greasy soy-sauce soaked crap u get at a typical nyc chinese joint).  Yeah, that's a total of $31 + tip and tax (!!!) for a extraordinarily filling (yes!), balanced (meat, veggies, carbs) and absolutely yummy comfort dinner for 2 (that's right, for 2!), just like ur chinese grandma used to make!  if u get drinks, it jumps to like 300 bucks or something (yeah, they're expensive, don't drink, just wait and get a couple of bud lights for dessert at the cab driver haunt down on 10th ave). all this and u get an wall-streeter-and-cougar-infested, garish, over-the-top, painfully trendy surrounding for free!

I'd like this place more if it weren't so... meatpacking.  You're supposed to feel very lucky and special just to be there at all, even if you are made to wait half an hour despite your reservation, on a weeknight.  The space is inarguably beautiful - especially the stunning downstairs.  The food is good on the whole, but not spectacular.  The yellowtail appetizer was very fresh and good.  The pork belly was reminiscent of, but not as good as, the pork buns at Momofuku.  The jumbo shrimp were coated in an unfortunate, sickly sweet mayonnaise-based sauce.  (Nothing should taste like mayonnaise in an upscale restaurant.  Are we clear on that?)  The fillet of beef was tasty, and came with a buttery bernaise.  I had the chocolate mille feuille for dessert based on yelper recommendations, but it was nothing special.  But the passionfruit mousse dessert was stellar - the consistency of a light fluffy cheesecake, with slices of delicate meringue. The service was odd - our waiter disappeared for such a long stretch that I was sure he'd left the premises for good.  The cute tattooed bartender was nice though, and my second delicious elderflower  gin cocktail was free.  Which would have meant more to me if the firm wasn't paying!

I LOVE Buddakan! My favorite place for Asian food in the city.  First of all everything I have ever had there is delicious so u will not hear one complaint. I always get the edamame dumplings but a friend tried one once and was not a big fan.  My other favorites are the pork buns, general tso dumplings and the short rib entree.  I really want to try others but I can't bring myself to ever order anything else because the tender short ribs with the mushroom chow fun is too amazing.
If Buddakan were a guy, this is what he'd be like:  tall, dark, handsome.  Dressed to the nines, with a smile that makes you melt and with beautiful eyes to draw you in.  I'd take a look and immediately classify him as a pretty face.  And I would never expect that there could be more behind the façade.  So imagine my surprise when I finally dined here this past weekend.  I'd heard some good things but I was reluctant to believe it.It was a girls' weekend and between the three of us girls, we ordered two entrees, two sides, an appetizer and a dessert.  I'd expected the portions to be on the smaller side and we ordered just the right number of dishes for three people.  We started with an order of the pork gyoza and then Heather, Susan and I shared the pork tenderloin and the whole crispy fish with the house special fried rice and the grilled asian vegetables.  We finished with the crying chocolate.Pork gyoza - were good.  There are probably better starters but this one was solid.Pork tenderloin - cooked medium rare, it was perfect.  It came with a side of the best deep fried eggplant I've ever had.  In fact, if I could, I would order the eggplant by itself. This is not to say the pork tenderloin can't stand by itself.  It was as good as what I've had at Blue Hills but the eggplant is divine and worth fighting over.  Crispy whole fish - amazing.  Came with head and tail on.  Crispy on the outside and tender and juicy on the inside, it was enhanced further with a salad of fresh tomatoes, watermelon, and what could have been a daikon cousin.  House special fried rice - I usually steer clear of dishes this easy to make but this wasn't bad actually.  It provided a nice palate from which we could focus on the other complimentary flavors.Asian grilled vegetables - basically, bok-choy and other greens sauteed with garlic.  So simple and yet when you cook good quality vegetable just right, there's nothing that can beat that.When the crying chocolate came, and Heather finally cut into it with her fork, a river of chocolate flowed from it as we all "oooohhh-ed".  The coffee bean ice cream complements the chocolate well and with two bites each, dessert had disappeared.  All in all, service was great.  The dining room is just gorgeous.  Most surprisingly though, the food here was as good as Eleven Madison or Union Square Café.  Reservations can be difficult and prime time slots go about a month in advance.  I had tried booking dinner for large groups here and for groups of 15+, there are prix fixe menus that start at above $100 per person.  Dinner in smalller groups are much more reasonable and while I did not pick up the check, I don't think our dinner was more than $200 total, including tip.

Had a fabulous dinner (after a rocky start in the bar area) over memorial day weekend. We arrived on time for our reservation and were told our table wouldn't be ready for a bit and to grab a drink in the bar. About 30 seconds after puttting in our drink orders, the hostess came to find us and show us to our table. We notified her that we had ordered drinks and asked for them to just be brought to our table. I don't know if this is some weird policy or something but they refused to allow it. We sat there for about 10 minutes with a hostess (awkwardly) standing there on top of us before they brought our drinks. We then had to wait for them to run the credit cards, as they refused to add it to our dinner check. The whole ordeal lasted about 15 minutes and was unnecessarily frustrating. It really started what we hoped to be a nice night out on the wrong foot. Luckily, the food lived up to the hype so the evening was redeemed. We ordered the edamame dumplings, calamari salad, boneless spare ribs, tuna tartar spring rolls, beef lettuce cups and the filet. The edamame dumpling were incredible!! They didn't even taste like edamame to me-  more like truffle mashed potatoes. I wish I had just ordered a bunch of these as my meal! The boneless spare ribs definitely surpassed my expectations, kind of like an upscale pulled pork. The calamari salad was what I was really looking forward to (I LOVE it at other stephen starr restaurants) but unfortunately it was a little diappointing. It was still good, just not as good as the one at continental in Philadelphia. I really wanted to like the tuna tartar spring rolls, but they were the disappointment of the night. They're really the only thing I wouldn't order again.  The lettuce cups and filet were both good too, but nothing you can't get elsewhere. Great for a date night or fun night out with the girls. The restaurant is beautiful and the service (once you're out of the bar area) is top notch!

just came back from dinner and i was pleasantly surprised!  the place was way bigger than i had expected . the decor was chic and lovely. the drinks: strong! the food was way better than i had expecting. if a place is hip and cool that usually means half ass food. I had very low expectations with this being a chic fusiony place BUT everything was cooked with attention to detail and had a very tasty blend of flavors. nothing was oversalted or sugary. everything tasted exceptionally clean .the crispy calamari salad was very light and refreshing. i noticed that instead of making everything sugary  like most fusion places, they integrated some unexpected traditional ingredients into all the dishes. the salad for example had fried calamari with granny smith apples. they complimented eachother perfectly. we also had a claypot duck which had candied walnuts and braised pinenuts.  great .  the steamed red snapper was cooked to perfection, as were the mongolian lamb chops!! There's already 90+ reviews for Buddakan so I'm not gonna really talk about the food or the place other than to say I've really enjoyed both on all my visits.Wheelchair Access: This is something I've been meaning to write for awhile and honestly I apologize to Buddakan for not getting to it sooner. Some months ago The NY Times  did a generally excellent article about accessibility and restaurants. I do however think Buddakan was unfairly portrayed. I've been three times (2 private parties, one business dinner) and have always been treated terrificly by the staff. Upon entrance there's a lift to your left that takes you the 3 or 4 feet to the main level. One time the lift was broken. The manager was waiting at the front to explain and apologize. 2 or 3 large guys (way more than enough) were waiting as well to help me up the stairs. No problem. There's a very accessible bathroom on this level and a lot of different, cool areas to dine. I've never gone 'downstairs' and I'm not sure if there's a way down. Buddakan has always been accessible for me and I've had three great evenings and meals there. Is it perfect, no, but I've always been happy with their effort and care. Call ahead and make sure the manager is aware of your needs and you should be fine. I appreciated the article in the Times, but was disappointed to see these guys take a hit.

This place does not live up to the hype surrounding it. This was a birthday party dinner, our birthday boy was excited about thus restaurant and his birthday. We were a table of 7. And of course 2 of our party were late. The restaurant was somewhat hard to find being that it was all black, and the sign was in black, so you couldn't see it if you were across the street. The people working near the door and desk were all dressed in black, and when I arrived ignored me. I had to speak to another girl at the desk to ask her where the bar was. Once inside at the bar, me and my friends had a drink, one drink to be exact. Our waitress carded us, to which she said she did this to everyone. Maybe because we were graduate students and still had the stench of school with us. But she was delightfully funny. I had the Charm drink, for $12. They finally sat us 20 minutes later, placing our cocktails on a tray and led us downstairs, though they did rush us as we were trying to settle our tab at the bar. We were lead downstairs, we were amazed at the decor and how dim and dark it was. They sat us at the huge table, many people had said it reminded them of harry potter. The bathroom was insanely dark. The ladies room was pitch black, everything was black, they had 3 separate rooms for stalls, but it was dark in there, you couldn't really see what you were doing. The only light was a small beam of light shooting down to the sink. There was no way you could apply lipstick or see if you had food in your teeth, let alone know if you didn't tuck your skirt into your pantyhose....other patrons there complained about the absolute darkness of it.But back to the food. The waitress explained to us that they serve things family style there, and that everyone would take from the dishes, and that no one would have an individual plate. For the birthday boy he was happy because it meant he would be able to try many different dishes. We ended up ordering, the jumbo shrimp, hot and sour scallops, Peking duck, Mongolian lamb chops, side of fried rice, calamari appetizers, and corn and crab balls. We figured that would be enough if we were sharing and also considering how much they were charging us per plate. The calamari came out, and it was tempura like, but fluffy, airy and tasty. It was when the crab corn cakes came out that the trouble started and we could feel we were in trouble. There were not enough appetizers for 7 people. so we split them in half and had a little taste and that was the theme for the rest of the night. As the other dishes came out we could see they were not proportioned for family style. The food was great. The jumbo shrimp, they decided to downscale from the last review of 5 to 4. There were 4 shrimp for 7 people. Then the scallops came. there were 3. Now if you were just one person, and this was your entree I think you'd be somewhat upset at the fact that there are only 3 scallops, clearly not enough for you to be full on or satisfied. The lamb chops were three, with three small pieces of baby bock choi. They were ginger crusted and quite tasty for the small piece i was able to sample. The Peking duck that they claim to be a whole duck, clearly was not a whole duck, they even plated it nicely, but you could tell it was not a whole duck. They seem to think if you make things smaller people will find them cuter. The side of fried rice was somewhat decent, it was something everyone could eat somewhat. It wasn't anything spectacular. Needless to say at the end of this, we were not full, and not amused. When the waitress said family style we thought it implied that it would be somewhat enough for everyone to eat, but apparently the portions showed that it was barely enough for one person to eat. 3 scallops? 4 shrimp? 3 lamb chops? cmon! unless you have a eating disorder or have had your stomach binded or stapled you're not going to get full here unless you order 2 or more entrees. and at that price you might as well go elsewhere.as for the cake? well apparently a cake much like wine gets a fee. the cake slicing fee was $3 a slice, and that would have been a whole other entree!  Their desserts looked very well plated and were at least $10 and up and we were tempted to get some but after we heard the cake cutting fee we decided to leave. When the bill came for our small portions, they had already decided to include a 20% tip! Now we were overcharged for food that barely fed us,  they refused our birthday boy's cake, and they had the audacity to add 20% into our bill! Needless to say, we paid the bill to the exact penny and took our birthday boy's cake elsewhere. Though it was lovely for decor and atmosphere, the portions of the food were appalling. Its filled with wannabe hipsters and trendsters, ugh they don't know what real asian food tastes like, and again the portions are small, the booze is great, and the bathrooms are dark as hell. If you're a party of 2, I'm sure you'll enjoy it more.

I'm usually pretty picky about my Chinese food, but I love Buddakan!!!  It's slightly overpriced for Chinese-fusion food, but it's totally worth it.  The crowd is trendy, the venue is chic, and the food is good.Dishes that I love and always get:  Edamame Dumplings, Taro Puffs, Scallion Pancakes.... and the Sausage Fried Rice with the egg on top!  The main dishes are good too, but I always end up ordering more hot/cold appetizers than main dishes (the cod's good btw).  You also get more variety that way.When making reservations, I like to request the main dining room where you dine under three big chandeliers - to me, it feels like you're dining in a mini version of the Harry Potter's dining hall!  Otherwise, there's always the "red" room in the back and tables in the halls surrounding the main dining room.  The bar area when you first get in can get really crowded during peak dining hours.  As you're waiting for your table, if you don't want to be stuck with the crowds, you can always grab drinks in the Library Room downstairs - that room tends to be less crowded and the headphone-connected hostesses will know to find you down there!
A gorgeous restaurant with awesome decor and pretty hit-or-miss food, Buddakan is a must-see.  Definitely go to check out the space, the ambiance is hard to beat and I doubt you'll find another restaurant like it!  But maybe just grab a drink and some apps here before a night out, there are better places in the city to get a top-notch, full-fledged dinner.  We started with four appetizers--the calamari salad, the pork dim sum lollipops, the rock shrimp and the tuna tartare spring rolls.  The calamari was in the salad was meh, nothing you couldn't get from your around the corner Italian takeout place for half the price. I liked the pork lollipops because they were cutely presented and had an interesting texture.  The spring rolls were awesome, but they could have upped the portion size.   BUT THE ROCK SHRIMP WAS A HOMERUN--great portion size and delicious flavor!The entrees were good but not amazing.  I got the softshell crab, which was tasty but my mom makes it better (I don't know why restaurants insist on frying it, it is so much better sauteed!) My friend got the crab and lobster chow fun, and he liked it.  And the desserts were excellent in both flavor and presentation...try the peanutbutter bomb or the crying chocolate. Have I had better food in the city? Definitely.  But was it in an atmosphere as cool as Buddakan's?  Never.

Awesome service and great atmosphere!! Our waitress was so friendly and was so patient with us. Though I detected a slight urgency, my party and I had a good time overall. It's family style- from what the waitress said. We also were advised to order everything at once.  So the five of us, picked several side dishes, rice, lomein, spinach, etc., appetizers and entrees. The sides weren't small. It was a good portion for the five of us. We started off with drinks. Jealousy and Tranquility is quite good. Stick with Tranquility if you don't want something overly sweet. Charm was alright, it was basically a prosecco garnished with a few berries. Not worth it. We then had tuna spring rolls. They only come with three- but were amazing! Raw tuna tartar (spicy tuna) wrapped in crispy thin wafer like spring rolls, they were a great start and complimented the drinks. Scallion Pancakes were't worth it. They were cold by the time it got to our table. I couldn't even tell it was scallion pancake. Our sides came out rather quickly. We had the seafood fried rice (house special) and shrimp lobster chow fun, wok roasted water spinach, minced pork lo mein ( pickled cucumbers gave the dish an extra zing! very flavorful and not greasy). We were full by sharing all the rice and lomein dishes on top of appetizers! It wasn't greasy but I feel like you could've easily went to a chinatown restaurant and gotten the same food for a fraction of the price. The entrees were a different story. We had the charred filet of beef, medium rare, drizzled with the soy butter sauce. AMAZINGGGGG. We had to fight each other for the last piece. It was so tender and well worth it!!! The wonton potatoes- what the hell was that.. it's just basic potato chips! Sweet and Crispy Jumbo shrimp was delicious!! We also shared the lobster, rather small, I don't recommend it as a "family style" dish. It came with white asparagus and bok choy that were marinated in a delicate sweet and tangy sauce. The lobster was alright.. I think you could get something so much better. Desserts were the crying chocolate and the Chocolate Mille Feuille. I liked the spiced chocolate sorbet that was accompanied with the avocado sauce in the Mille Feuille. Avocados and chocolate?? Who knew? I love them both, and what a great pairing. I wonder when other restaurants will start incorporating this into their menus. The banana brulee w. dark choc. shavings weren't that good in my opinion. I'm not a fan of bananas and chocolate but like I said, the avocado sauce was out of this world!! The crying chocolate was like any other molten chocolate cake, cute decor- but TINY. Well.. there you go. My feast at Buddakan. Excuse me while I run to the bathroom and puke myself silly.. Overall good night, good drinks. Nice crowd. Some dishes were rather ordinary, but the steak made my tummy happy~!

I made reservations for dinner on a Saturday last month, and they could only seat a party of 5 at 5:45pm or 10:05pm by the time I called (it was Friday, so I wasn't that surprised). So we decided to go for 5:45pm. First, we got lost because Buddakan shares an address with the Chelsea Market something or other. When we finally walked up to the doorway, we were greeted by a few people dressed all in black. They seemed to be blocking the door, so we nervously asked for permission to enter...As usual, at least two members of our party were extremely late, so three of us sat in the front room perusing the cocktail and appetizer menu. None of us had come here before, so we were a bit apprehensive of the prices (all three of us are Chinese-American, and it's always painful to pay exorbitant amounts of money for "Asian fusion" cuisine). Luckily, the overstaffed front desk people (seriously, do they need 8 girls behind the counter??) let us keep our reservations despite our late guests.The architecture is quite nice, and the ambiance is also very mellow (read: it's pretty dark). The hostess warned all the women that many others have stumbled down the somewhat hazardous steps leading down to the dining area, which resembled a grand banquet hall. She requested that we all hold on to the banister as we headed down to our table.Once seated, we were pretty puzzled as to why we couldn't make reservations for 7pm like we had wanted to. It wasn't as packed as we expected it to be. By the time we left it was almost 9pm, and business had picked up a little bit, but I'm pretty sure we would have been able to make a 7pm reservation without any problem.Our waitress seemed nice at first, although we were pretty disappointed with her in the end. She explained to us what family style dining was (as if the 4/5 Chinese-Americans at the table didn't know what it meant). Because we were all college/graduate students, we were fine with ordering the noodle and rice side dishes and forgoing the expensive "entree" dishes. Once we had made the order, the waitress had the audacity to tell us that we probably wouldn't have enough food if we didn't order entrees. She told us that she would come back once we decided on some entrees (basically, she was telling us that we weren't spending enough money on our dinner).So, we ordered the tea smoked chicken and the sweet  crispy jumbo shrimp entrees, along with a rice or noodle dish for each person (crab fried rice, vegetable fried rice, Chinese sausage fried rice, roast pork lo mein, mao poe tofu). When our dishes arrived we almost started laughing. The rice and noodle dishes are definitely enough food for one person. The entree dishes had the teeniest portions. The shrimp entree had 5 shrimps, just enough for each person in our party to have one. The food was decent, but not great, and we were truly unhappy that our waitress had bamboozled us into paying an extra $50 for two teeny portions of food. The Mabo Tofu (however they spell it) is not as amazing as we heard it was (I thought it was pretty bland). The veggie fried rice was okay, not great, and I thought the coconut curry foam was weird. Needless to say, the waitress did not get a good tip. As for the five "side dishes" we ordered, we were unable to finish the large amount of food and ended up doggy-bagging the rest of it. So much for not having enough food...Basically, I was disappointed with the flavors of the food. I have had better dishes from hole-in-the-wall Chinese restaurants. It's not worth the money unless you're there for the pretentiousness of a trendy spot. Perhaps I'll find a good Asian Fusion restaurant one day...The bathrooms are pretty neat, though, if you can figure out which side is which.The final verdict? Overrated, but if you've got money to burn, come here to mingle with the "trendy" crowd.

After thinking long about where to eat the call was for Buddakan by my New York friends/co-workers. We ventured from Times Square to the meat packing district. I was impressed with the choice. Is describing it as "Asian tapas" a faux pas? It wasn't really dim sum served on a cart by chinese women who speak little English. Plus it was too refined and tasty with well integrated flavors to be dim sum. So lets call it "Tapas-style Asian fusion cuisine". Well was it really fusion? I though the options were overwhelmingly Chinese in nature - cha su bao-esque beef filled buns, pot stickers (er gyoza, okay that's japanese! haha), hoisin glazed pork belly served on steamed buns, beef/shrimp "cantonese" spring rolls, boneless spareribs, sizzling short ribs, clay pot chicken...oh man am I forgetting anything? $750 later (oh yeah there were 9 of us) I felt like "damn everything was good." The shortribs with chow fun was awesome, the noodles clearly homemade.Far be it for me to complain about the price of food when I don't have to pick up the tab.The space is pretty cool, a tiny bit pretentious with people dressed like they are grabbing a bit of food prior to hitting da club but architecturally it really worked - you enter from the street and check your coat and meet the hostess. Then you walk upstairs to the bar area which has large square tables with bench seats. There was also the traditional bar tables/stools set up. Then seating wise there was the upstairs and the downstairs with their own unique decor yet still familiar. The service was good, I left full and I'd probably go back...but oh yeah I haven't been to New York in 10 years and I think I have many other places to visit first!

totally ridiculous!this is not a truly fair review, since we were treated to a corporate American Express card that could buy us all of our wildest culinary desires... so! what can i say about the food? honestly, i'd never pay for "upscale Chinese", or i wouldn't have, before last night.we started off with a zillion appetizers and dim sum, including Chili Rock Shrimp (an instant favorite, tasted like a riff on general tso's shrimp), Edamame Dumplings in a Shark Fin Broth (insanely delicious, done up soup-dumpling style with a creamy texture), Taro Puff Lollipops (another favorite, like hush puppies from heaven), Scallion Pancakes with braised short ribs and green apples, Steamed Char Sui buns (delicious.. but it was no Momofuku), Tuna Spring Rolls, and General Tso's Soup Dumplings (just like it sounds!).  not a thing was disappointing, and we were all delirious with gustatory delight.we washed the first course down with some of their creative cocktails (not being much a cocktail drinker myself, i stuck with the tamer "Tranquility", which was lemongrass-infused oolong tea and citrus vodka.. basically tasted like a reeeaaallly mild vodka tonic) and happily buzzed about in anticipation of the entrees...we were treated to Glazed Alaskan Black Cod (which was achingly good, so creamy and buttery and wonderful), Shrimp  Lobster Chow Fun (came in a big bowl which we all happily assaulted with our chopsticks), Charred Filet with crispy wonton potatoes (aka chips), a very impressive House Fried Rice, a salad of crisp Snow Peas tossed with soy sauce and roe, and topped it off with a nice order of Peking Duck (not as appreciated as the dishes that preceded it, but perhaps that was because our bellies were maxing out).more drinks, more excited talk about how delicious everything has been, and then we attacked the dessert menu.  the Crying Chocolate was the guaranteed crowd pleaser, with a warm chocolate ganauche and coffee ice cream, the Frozen White Chocolate Parfait was my personal favorite, if only for the unusually tasty candied kumquats and burnt orange ice cream (a couple in our group hated it... but they CLEARLY haven't trained their palate), the Coconut Souffle Cake with pineapple sorbet (i thought the sorbet was better than the souffle), and the Chocolate Mille Feuille, an incredible stacked pastry of dark chocolate, bruleed bananas, a reeeeediculous avocade anglaise, and spice chocolate ice cream.all told, we had a wonderful meal.  i question how fun it would have been if our ordering had been dictated by the fact that we were paying $12 per dim sum plate and $30 per entree... for Chinese food.  if i were to return without the corporate friends, i'd definitely just load up on the appetizers and maybe share an entree. but if you can write it off as a business expense ... do it!

Maybe I was expecting too much or maybe it was the rainy weather but the food was just good and not as amazing as I had hoped. We got the chili rock shrimp because of all of the rave reviews but it is honestly just deep fried shrimp pieces (more breading than shrimp) and lots of mayo. The edamame dumplings  tasted more like some sort of cheese dumpling. It was good but just as good as any cheese ravioli can be and nothing amazing. I would recommend the Alaskan cod  which was perfectly cooked and came with a really good and unique black bean relish. The Black Bean Silken Tofu with kabocha squash, shiitake mushroom, and shishito pepper was good but a bit salty. We also got the Sugar Snap Peas with wild mushrooms and soy tapioca which was also good but overly sauced. Overall, I feel like they use very fresh ingredients but the seasoning and/flavors are lacking. The tofu cheesecake for dessert was really light and delicious. It came slightly deconstructed with an extra graham cracker crust mashed on the side. This place does okay for Asian fusion but I feel like you can go to better places in NYC for good Asian food.

Buddakan is one of those New York institutions that everyone wants to frequent at least once, if only for the chance to be able to casually throw it out in conversation "oh yeah Buddakan, of course I've been there!' with a practiced air of nonchalance, when one wants to show some sophistication and "in-the-know" flair. Its claim to fame is the fact that the engagement party of Carrie and Mr.Big was filmed here (if you are asking me who they are, I'd label you a caveman). The decor is unsurprisingly impressive with the massive long table in the center room and the beautiful chandeliers. There are tables in the outer chambers too but you really don't get the experience you are paying for. Let's face it, the food is beautifully presented like everything else in this place, but the taste is mediocre at best and completely overpriced. Add I the absolutely TERRIBLE service - our waitress was not only slow, she kept trying to make us order more food even though we ordered plenty, and kept pressing one of the girls to order a cocktail even after she made unclear she wouldnt be drinking. A winner for most tourists for sure. And one final tip - if your have friends visiting from out of town and they are staying in a decent hotel, get their hotel to call and make a reservation on your behalf, you are more likely to be seated in the main room to appreciate the decor and ambience that way!

We went here for dinner during our anniversary trip to New York.  Reservations were easy to make on OpenTable.  The restaurant is on the corner of the street.  There is not a big or well lit sign so you have to look for it.  Once you enter, it's almost all black.  You walk to the hostess counter and they check you in.  The hostess invites you to go upstairs to the bar until the table is ready.  There was a lot of people at the bar so I was wondering how the hostess would know who we were, but they did.  Our table was upstairs peering down to the main floor.  It was still pretty dark.  There was a lot of hustle and bustle around us.  Our waitress told us that the plates are meant to be shared and encouraged us to order appetizer, entrees, rice dish, vegetable; basically she wanted us to order at least one thing from every category.  I really don't like it when waitstaff pressure you to order a lot of food.  Makes it seem more like a sales pitch rather than a recommendation.  Here is what we ordered:Dream cocktail = it is pretty sweet.Edamame Dumplings = All the reviews I read prior to making reservations here raved about these dumplings.  Boy, they were not wrong.  The dumplings had good flavor and tasted oh so light.  I wish there was more broth with the dumplings.Sizzling Short Rib = oh so tender.  The first few bites were wonderful.  After a while there was this salty bitter after taste.  Initially I loved it, but after a few bites I just liked it.Sweet  Crispy Jumbo Shrimp = This is their version of walnut shrimp.  I loved everything about this dish but the one thing it lacked was the sweetness.  It was not sweet at all.Chinese Sausage Fried Rice = I'm not a fan of chinese sausage in general so I really didn't have any comment about this.  My husband liked it but he did wish the rice was more fried.  Szechuan long beans = the beans were drenched in oil.  The spicy pork was a bit salty.Sichuan peanut semifreddo = this was probably the best thing we had all night.  The milk chocolate mousse was heaven.  I liked Buddakhan but I didn't love it.  I think this restaurant is super over rated.  It somewhat reminded me of a fancy PF Chang's.  With New York being a restaurant-eccentric city, I think there are probably better options for food with the same price tag.
A girlfriend and I came here on a Friday night at 11pm. The place was still buzzing with people, drinking, eating and conversing. The decor is beautiful, like a very modern Chinese mansion in a club like atmosphere with cut out walls, displays of stuffed birds and neon colors. We're seated and start looking over the menu. I order a cocktail, solid - with bourbon, ginger and orange. It was good. On appetizers we decided on the duck salad and tuna spring roll. The salad could have used a touch more salt on the greens, but the duck itself was great. The tuna tasted really fresh and the spring roll skin was crunchy, it was awesome. For Entrees we shared filet of beef, kung pao monkfish and wild mushroom chow fun. The beef came med, when I ordered it med rare, but it was still tender and juicy nonetheless. This place is completely worth every penny and I cannot wait to come back.I made last minute reservations for a friend and I to eat here on a Saturday night and they were ready for us almost as soon as we walked in. There is a place in the front where there's a bar and some seating if you have to wait to be seated, which is very open. A nice touch since I always hate being at an overcrowded bar in a nice place.We didn't get to sit down in the main area with the large table, but the ambiance of this place was not lost on that. I love places that are a feast for all the senses, not just taste and Buddakan does not fail to deliver.Our waiter was attentive, but not annoying and very extremely helpful especially with making sure I was alright with how the dishes were prepared (veggie here). He made sure to inform the chef of my dietary preferences so that I didn't consume anything I wasn't comfortable with. This is the sign of a place serious about making their guests happy.Not only did the food and our drinks come out in a timely staggered fashion, the whole experience had this flow to it that was very relaxed and natural. I know with places that are very popular you can feel rushed through the dining experience, but not here.All the dishes we had were very fresh and expertly prepared. I know a lot of people on yelp write about the Edamame Dumplings and they are for sure not to be missed! I'm pretty certain that my friend and I could of made an entire meal out of these yummy little pouches of goodness.The dishes we enjoyed were the Carrot Dumplings, Chilled Udon Noodles, Charred Asparagus, Spiced Tofu  Cashews and the Black Bean Silken Tofu. Ending our foodgasm with the Rock Sugar Doughnuts, which come with 3 different sauces for dipping. If I could marry a sauce it would be the spicy strawberry royal jelly. It's last taste on earth amazing and is a flavor I must have again before I die.All and all this dinner has made it into my top 3 on dining experiences in NYC and a place definitely worth saving up for.

I came here with two friends per recommendation of Nancy D. The restaurant was also very gracious in changing our reservations; my cousin and her fiancee were to join us but canceled at the last minute, in addition to my other friend, so the party went from 6 to 3!The entrance is a sleek black door on the corner, and walking in is beautiful. I loved the swanky and classy lounge decor and even spotted the GORGEOUS main dining room downstairs on the way to our table. Everything is lit very well and it feels like I'm on a very sexy date (except I'm here with two girlfriends, damn, if only the BF were here) I love how everything is colorful against a black matte finish. We were seated on the entry level in the back, through some uniquely shaped doorways and into a red-themed room. We got there a little early but the place quickly filled up with both tourists and chic locals. Our server was a little pushy in trying to get us to order everything on the menu, but we stuck with the Chili Rock Shrimp, General Tso's Dumplings, and the Steamed Sea Bass Roll, the latter of which was my favorite - so tender, so sweet, so yummy. The Chili Rock Shrimp also have a crispiness to them that is flavorful and unique. I also ordered the "Fate" cocktail and I loved how frothy it was - it was also pretty strong but complemented my meal very well. I am also a giant sucker for pineapple! My friend got the Charm but it was a little too fruity for me.For entrees we ordered the Szechuan Crusted NY Ribeye, the Sizzling Short Rib, and the Shrimp and Lobster Chow Fun (my order).  Out of all of our orders, my favorite was the Sizzling Short Rib. That was so juicy and it almost melted in my mouth the way Kobe beef does. Don't get me wrong, I LOVED my Shrimp and Lobster Chow Fun; the seafood was cooked very well, the noodles were tender and not soggy, and there were some super-juicy tomatoes thrown in, but that Short Rib hit the spot. I wanted to steal my friend's plate and eat it, even if it was in front of her! (just kidding, but I did fantasize about it)Dessert was my favorite part. I ordered the Chocolate Mille Feuille, and my two friends ordered the Crying Chocolate and the Coconut Creme Brulee. The Chocolate Mille Feuille is creative and executed well. I ordered this simply because it came with an avocado anglaise and I absolutely did NOT expect it to go well with bruleed bananas and chocolate ganache but it DID! It was absolutely delicious. The spiced chocolate ice cream was a little hard on the taste buds but for some reason I kept mixing it with the avocado and it tasted better! The Crying Chocolate is like any other flourless chocolate cake but it was executed beautifully on the plate and was still delicious. I loved the lemongrass ice cream that came with the Coconut Creme Brulee - also well executed because coconut is a flavor that can go so bad so quick.  I was impressed and loved that dish, too.Overall, Buddakan is a great place to have dinner in the West Village; I loved the atmosphere, the food, the service, and everything in between. I hope this place can keep re-inventing itself because I plan on coming back; I hope to see some even more delicious choices on the menu.

They've taken a virtually windowless 16,000 square foot environment and turned it into one of the most extraordinary interiors in the city. From the minute you open the large door you feel as if your going into the abyss of high class. It was about time to see what all the fuss is about. I've always liked the whole discrete entrance idea when it comes to unique establishments so I immediately apprecicated the subtlety of the door tucked away just off the corner of 16th St and 9th Ave. We were greeted at a formal counter seperated from the rest of the space, a slightly different concept than your usual restaurant podium. After checking our coats we were escorted to a beautiful corner table in the grand baroque room overlooking the central dining area which was simply spectacular! Buddakan is like many different worlds in one. There are several rooms and spaces of different colors, design and themes that all surround the main dining room made up of high ceilings and gorgeously ornate wooden walls. This week I decided to take an easier approach to ordering from the menu. We faithfully placed everything in our waiter's hands and asked him to select the best Buddakan's cuisine had to offer. Luckily we didn't have any dietary needs which made for a vast selection of options and here is what we got: Shrimp Dumplings filled with Egg Drop Broth, Scallions and Bamboo Shoots, this appetizer was incredible. This giant, trendy asian-fusion restaurant will wow you when you first walk in. Everything is somewhat sexy with many sections of the restaurant, each with different themes and decor - the lounge is sleek but gets crowded and loud in the evening, the grand room with its high ceiling, gold colors and grandeur commands your attention but also gets loud as the room fills up...but the best is the quieter, more intimate library with tables surrounded by faux gold colored books, softly lit by lights - we have our favorite table here for six that is comfortable yet interesting in decor - which, by the way, is an odd mix of asian and baroque. The food itself is good - particularly the taro puff lollipops which were served hot with a crispy outside and a warm goey pork filling.  The scallion pancakes with short ribs were more like crispy thin flatbread with braised short ribs and scallion on top - but it was delicious. The lobster dumplings were nothing out of the ordinary though. We also tried the NY strip served with tomatos and crispies - it was good, but again, nothing special. The black cod and the snapper, though typical sounding were actually delicious and well accented by the other complementary aspects of the dish susch as the mushrooms and the radish. In terms of dessert - we ordered the chocolate mille feuille with caramelized banana and a kaffir lime tart that came with some sort of a lime souffle and gelato - I highly recommend the lime dessert because the lime souffle and gelato were irresistable. Overall, I would say that the food was delicious, the decor was interesting, the service could have been more consistent - but I'll give them a break since this is only week 2 - and the experience overall was worth trying - but there are definitely better places to eat. Good place to get a drink and small apps though...!

i went last night for dinner. the decor was nice...very sleek inside. again, another take on the "modern" aesthetic. the restaurant is huge...and located conveniently next to chelsea market. from where we sat, it was quite drafty. i assumed most of our food came out hot or warm but by the time we had our first helping, the food had chilled. we sat in the side aisle connecting the bar/lounge area to the back dining area, overlooking the bottom floor dining area. the restaurant was loud as heck. not at all pleasant. perhaps it was due to the cavernous size and the materials used to construct the restaurant (not acting as a sound dampener but rather refracting and amplifying sounds [chatter and music alike]) but it sounded like i was in the middle of lunch rush hour at a high school cafeteria. girls and boys huddle over their tables gossiping all over the place. i could hardly hear what the other person sitting directly across from me was saying.suffice to say, the area where we were sat had quite a lot of foot traffic. not pleasant. and to top it off, our table was so small and there was no sense of timing in which the dishes came out, our small table was brimming with dishes. throughout the majority of our dinner the candle, the sugar holder, our bottles of water, drink glasses, my tea kettle and tea cup were all placed on the ledge next to us to make room for the dishes. you know, small details like that really make or break a restaurant for me. i think two dishes at a time is great for a table our size...instead the servers were piling dish upon dish onto our cramped table even, piling dishes on top of each other. that is ridiculous. i was there for a dining experience not to see how adept the servers were at figuring out how to pile even more dishes onto our table. and each time the servers brought out a new dish, they plopped it down onto our table. and like i'm like, wtf is this? did we order this? none of the usual tirade on what the dish was, what the main ingredient was, etc. just plop and go. was it even that busy last night?and the food. meh. i've had better. the butternut squash dumplings looked good on the menu. it wasn't my favorite. it's way too creamy or gooey. has an odd consistency in your mouth. the dumplings were gooey already but they came served in a gooey sauce. so it was goo drenched in more goo. the char sui pork buns were tasty enough. i had better at momofuku. the scallion pancakes? meh. deviled tuna tartare? meh. our tea smoked chicken was covered in too much of the ginger chutney to be even tasty. is was like, "what am i eating here? ginger?" and the asparagus and black bean dish, we ordered because we were curious as to how it would be presented. when it came out it looked like cut asparagus swimming in velveta and black bean cheese dip. and how much did our lovely meal set us back? $140.not. worth. it.
I enjoyed my dinner here. Obviously a shi-sh-fru-fru experience, but in an era where decadence is no longer seen out and about it was refreshing to dine here and observe a generally well dressed and attractive crowd. The setting is amazing, I love the idea of walking down the steps to your table, treat it as your own personal runway folks! The space is massive and the restaurant check-in area is set up hotel style, so you aren't crowded at the door attempting to let the hosts know that you have arrived! The seating area/bar while you wait is cute, and at first I onwdered how they would locate me amidst such a loud and packed room but they came and seated my party promptly. My waitress was very friendly without beings syrupy or programmed  (you know the kind of service you get at chains). She recommened we do maybe 3 appetizers and 2 entrees, all of which were good, especially the rock shrimp. My water was refilled promptly, my white Russian was good! Are the portions small? Yes, but why do people complain about this? Go to Cheeesecake Factory or Maggianos if you want to gorge and pig out. After the apps and the entree, I didn't even have room for dessert. All in all, this spot seems to be one of the trendy restaurants with substance!
I've been to Buddakan twice now and both experiences have been great!Tried the cocktail "Fate" that was recommended by our waitress. Thought it was quite delicious!On to the food.. Party of 7 ordered - Spring Rolls, Tuna Tartar Rolls, Duck Salad, Spare Ribs, Rock Shrimp, Frog Legs and the Scallion Pancakes to start. I would pass on the pancakes next time but everything else was Yum, Yum and YUM! Then on to the entrees.. we all shared Black Pepper Beef, Black Cod, Scallops, Peking Duck, Lobster Fried Rice, Crab Sticky Rice and Asparagus. You can probably get better pepper steak at a takeout restaurant but all the other dishes were amazing. Wish I had a bigger stomach to try more dishes!! For dessert, I had the Crying Chocolate with Jasmine Ice Cream. It definitely made me cry cause it was so good and I wanted more (corny) LOL
I know this place doesn't need any more reviews... but I rarely get to go to NYC so you better believe I'm going to review what I can!After a full day of corporate training, a group of 12 of us came in here without a reservation - luckily it was early and they were able to accomodate us. We sat in the lounge/bar area, around one of the huge, low tables. At first this was weird... then we realized it was actually awesome. We got to sit back and observe as the crowd poured in; it made for great people watching.With some quick references to the Yelp app on my iPhone, I knew exactly what I wanted to order. Since I had my corporate card in my back pocket, I tried a bunch of different items:Edamame Dumplings - delicate, very unique and tasty but you better be an edamame fan.Chili Rock Shrimp - SPICY and delicious, my favorite item.Sugar Snap Peas - great mix of flavors without being overwhelming, they were a good compliment to the shrimp.I washed it all down with a Lush cocktail (very girly and fun) and then stole a bite of a coworker's dessert - the Crying Chocolate was FANTASTIC. I sincerely regretted not getting one for myself. Next time...Food: 5 starsValue: 4 starsService: 5 starsAmbiance: 5 stars
One of my favorite Asian Fusion restaurants in the city. Terrific food, impeccable service, and an interesting dim decor makes this spot great for a dates or large group of friends.I've been here a couple times, both times with 6+ friends. The food is served family style so you can sample various dishes (which is a good thing). The menu is comprehensive and offers plenty of options. Some of my favorites are the following: - edamame dumplings (has a hint of truffle oil)- pork buns (great asian flavor)- all of their fried rice/noodle dishes (can't pick one, they're all so good) - pepper beef (on the salty side but still a favorite)- miso black cod (comparable to the one at morimotos)- tuna tartar (make sure you don't forget to incorporate the spicy mayo)- lamb chops (not too lamby- great medium rare)
I used to live 2 blocks from here in my glorious 20's and went to this restaurant frequently b/c w/o fail, it was always a fantastic and inspired meal.   Went again recently, maybe 2-3 yrs since my last visit, and was pleasantly surprised nothing has changed (in a good way)- everything was delicious and service was great.  Highly recommend this place.

Yeah, I'm a little slow in knowing that this place is kind of my dream come true.  Dark, sexy, modern, and gorgeous.  You walk in and there's a giant hotel-like front desk where you check in.  Then we were instructed to wait by the bar while our table gets ready.  We had a glass of prosecco (priced decently, $9) while we waited, about 5 minutes.  We were then ushered down the stairs through the grand dining room, to our table in the far side room.  Nicest touch ever was when the hostess carried my champagne for me down the stairs, as high heels + stairs = wobbles.  Super nice touch.At the table, our server came right away and was friendly, attentive, smart, fast, and basically perfect.  Immediately after sitting, an amuse bouche of tuna tartare and spicy yellowtail arrived - both amazing.  Considered ordering full orders of each, but wanted to try more things.  So:We ordered:- edamame dumplings - which were great.  Basically like buttery mashed potato with a delicate wrapper.  All one texture, melts in your mouth.-scallion pancake - a plate of 4 rectangular pancakes, piled high with braised short rib.  More about the beef than the pancake, totally amazing.-Udon noodle with lime sorbet, peanut sauce, cashews, lime, snowpeas, sprouts, and crystalized ginger.  This side dish is magically fresh and delicious.-Ginger-crusted lamb chops - a plate of 3 lamb lollipops, medium rare.  So good I literrally got emotional.-Mapu Tofu - Excellent.  My husband has eaten this dish all over China and said this was up there with the best of them.  A huge serving of white rice accompanies the dish, the only item on the table we didn't finish.We also tried (yes) three of the desserts.  The peanut butter bomb was only ok - it suffered from a heavy shell which I didn't like, but the inside peanut butter mousse was nice.  Much better was the chocolate torte with coffee ice cream, but the best, I thought by far, was the cheesecake with pear sorbet.  Amazing.  Although, the food at this restaurant was SO great, that when dessert came, it almost felt like an afterthought - like - just unnecessary after all the good 'real' food we'd just had.Also had a bottle of cold, unfiltered sake which tasted like candy-goodness.And for all this gloriousness, the check came out to be way less than I expected.  Totally reasonably priced.  I can't wait to go back and try more things on the menu, which is pretty rare for me.Basically my new favorite restaurant.  Wish I had gone sooner.

I had a truly fantastic birthday here last week with my 5 best gals, Sex and the City rehearsal dinner style. Sure it was a splurge, but so fun to dress up and eat amazing food in an amazing space.Naturally we started with some bubbly - Veuve Clicquot - my go-to. Then we perused the enormous menu, and since everything sounded delicious, we went for the tasting. They offer several tiers, and the lowest tier at $65 per person was just perfect.Appetizer highlights: the Edamame Dumplings - edamame puree + truffle oil in a dumpling. Pretty sure this item is on the menu in my heaven. I also loved our first app - the Tuna Spring Roll.Somewhere amid the apps I ordered our next bottle. Wine is generally pricy, as you would expect, but I found a hidden gem among the whites listed as Cape Mentelle Blend. I'll tell you that it's a Sauv Blanc / Semillon, and it's delicious. It's also one of the lowest-priced at $40. Loved it.So by now the rest of our courses are a bit of a blur, but I do recall rave reviews on all of them, from all of us, as we tasted through. We were sufficiently stuffed, but managed to make room for the seemingly-endless desserts - all so different and delicious.I highly recommend Buddakan for a fun / celebratory / special night out... or for any random day/meal if your wallet can support it!

I love this Stephen Starr restaurant, and it is even better than the Philly version.  The steamed sea bass roll is a fantastic app with fragrant scallion oil, and the deviled tuna tartare is the perfect combination of spicy and creamy flavors.  The dungeness crab sticky rice is very solid, although it's not quite as great as Joe's.  The mongolian lamb chops, however, are fantastic, as is the glazed Alaskan cod; the cod flesh is incredibly silky and tender and lamb is tender and flavorful.  Be sure to get the Chinese sausage fried rice with the sunny side-up egg!  There are plenty of options for vegetarians, too, although I personally love the hoisin-glazed pork belly.  It's hard to go wrong with any dish here.  For dessert, I always head straight for the Almond bread oudding with whiskey ice cream and bananas.  It's creamy and has just the perfect hint of alcohol.  Service is always super and you can't beat the hip, upbeat, trendy atmosphere.  Prices are also very reasonable for the ambiance and quality!  LOVE LOVE LOVE!!!

4.5 stars but my group of 12 had no complaints after we left so they get a 5 since they were able to make a large group complaint free. Food: I usually hate paying an extra premium for fusion ethnic foods at trendy restaurants when I can have the real thing at a hole in the wall. But in Buddakan's case, they did not disappoint. Everything was well prepared, had great flavor and the portions were fair for their size. The sake selection is a nice bonus too.Ambiance: Beautiful restaurant, especially the large dining room which was super impressive.Service: Very good and the food came out at a nice pace.Price: Obviously more then a hole in the wall Asian place, but compared to other restaurants with an equivalent ambiance and service, Buddakan is fair if not a good deal.Overall: You aren't coming for the food, you're coming for the atmosphere and environment. Luckily in this case, unlike other similar restaurants, the food is good enough to make you happy when you leave.

DAMAGE CONTROL has to be the stand out factor of Buddakan...but more about that later.I was very excited to come to this swanky spot for my friend's birthday. Drinks were really good, my favorite was the "Lush" with Sake, Gin, Lychee and Rosemary. Drinks were followed by everyone ordering about 2 plates each for the table.  I foolishly did not try the Edamame Dumplings but I hear they were superb.  I loved the Tuna Tartar Spring Rolls and the Deviled Tuna Tartar with Chili Mayo (delicious layer of fresh bright tuna over avocado with a long slide of chili mayo down the plate, so good!)  I was told to order the Calamari Salad which was good but underwhelming (basically fried calamari over greens with apples and cashews and a basic light dressing). Will return more prepared to order outside the appetizer menu and go with the famous recommendations they're known for. As dinner was finishing nicely...the roach came...Yes only the second cockroach I have ever seen in NYC came crawling down the long wood table at the center of the downstairs dining room. Gasps and screams were immediately followed by one of the staff members "taking care" of the critter and all was well.This ordeal was followed by bottles of Veuve for our whole party and then every single dessert on the menu....(I think in hopes of me not mentioning this on Yelp but how the staff handled the situation should be commended).  Supposedly, this has never happened there and I do believe that.  I must say one little roach AFTER dinner was worth the tradeoff of getting to try every dessert on the menu (each also came with a candle for the b-day girl). Best dessert: Almond Bread Pudding...pure heaven.The net-net: will definitely come back, but most likely only for another special occasion.
I have been here 6+ times for dinner and drinks and @ my dear friend Jennifer Y. who says: "the patrons all think they're Paris Hilton socialites when they're all really from the tristate suburbs"- times have changed...This Friday night (I'd usually go on a week day to avoid the BT crowd but I had international guest with me and this restaurant is a showpiece), there was more than one kid there with a mouthful of braces having dinner with his/her family. After 4+ years of being open, it's gone from trendy to touristy to catch-all?I honestly believe that the key to Buddakan is no expectations. You should go once, just to see the space.  No amount was spared making this restaurant look like a million bucks. If you've been more than once, the experience feels different depending on what table you end up with. Upstairs feels different from downstairs and the "great hall" feels like a special occasion dinner even when it's not. My #1 tip is this, ordering well off this extensive menu is the key to your experience here. You can order the wrong thing and write-off the whole restaurant in one trip.  There are so many ways to go wrong..stay away from the traditional fried stuff like rock shimp and all the other BS dim sum, like scallion pancakes which will be the same as the ones in Chinatown just way more expensive, you can get that stuff anywhere. Here are the some great choices:Edamame Dumplings (steamed)- A++Spiced Tofu and Cashews- A+Whole Peking Duck- AYellowtail Yu Sheng- ABy this point, the staff runs like a well oiled machine and they're not only helpful but knowledgeable as well in case you need some recommendations from the menu or help with the wine list!!!If you're looking for a scene go somewhere else...this restaurant managed to make a smooth transition past being trendy with good food and ambiance, I would call it a classic!
This place is in my top 5 restaurants of all time. Flavors are balanced and complex. Must get edamame dumplings, asparagus,  charred filet of beef, and vegetable rice with coconut foam. Roll your eyes back ah-mazing!
I have been to Buddakan probably 15 times now and it has been 100% consistent every time. This is not where you come with your cool friends, they'll think you're nuts to suggest it. But don't be a snob. Bring your own of town guests here. It's perfect for that. It's spacious, pretty, the food is really good, and the service is always amazing. It feels like an event, especially for people from out of town. I took my parents here this weekend and it was just so NICE to take my little old small town folks somewhere that felt hip to them so they felt "New York" and no one there talked down to them or looked down at them or made us feel stupid. And for those who say it's expensive, I really don't know what they're talking about. 3 of us each had a cocktail, we shared 5 plates I think, we had 2 desserts, and it was $150. You don't get better than this for $50 a head.

Came her for my bday a couple of weeks ago. We started with the app sampler which was insane and well worth the money. My girlfriend's fish dish (cod, I believe) was also incredible but my short ribs were bland and had to be dunked in hot mustard just to get them down. I would have been much happier had my waitress not disappeared for a good 20min after we received our entrées because by the time she checked on us I had already finished half of the meal. Yes, I get that we are a 2-top on a saturday night but you can at least come and check in periodically. I had to wait over 15min to get my glass of sake refilled and on top of that, it wasnt the kind I ordered . By the time we finished our meal I was too peeved to order desert so we bounced.Maybe we just had the wrong waitress so I'm open to giving this place another shot. Food and service aside, Buddakan is like a palace - huge and beautifully decorated. Now I get what all the hype is about.
What can I say.  Probably one of the best meals I've had.  From service (by our fantastic server Janette) to the atmosphere - the whole experience was wonderful.  A group of friends and I traveled to NY and made sure to include this in our itinerary.  Originally there just to visit Dale from Top Chef, we were awed by the décor - modern, but cozy and the whole place had certain warmth to it.  We had drinks (from their extensive cocktail list) by the bar as we waited for our table and within fifteen or so minutes we were seated at the downstairs dining room (remember Sex and the City clip of Carrie and Big's engagement party).   A party of 6 food enthusiasts, we opted for the prix fixe menu which consisted of family style dishes.  Luckily, it was pretty easy for all of us to agree on the type of menu - the one with the most food and the best choices.  Every single dish we had was delicious!  From the edamame dumplings (which are a must - thanks to our server for packing us a little box for a late night snack) to the beef with brown butter sauce (if I did not have manners, I would have drank the butter sauce if not asked for a jar to take home with me) - nothing disappointed.  I must add this in though - although I say nothing disappointed - the dessert didn't wow any of us, but it may be because the courses prior to dessert were just so good that nothing would have compared (unless we repeated the whole dinner again).  Once we got the bill, it was as expected - large.  But, unlike most of the places I've been to - I felt that the whole experience and meal, were well worth it and I would not hesitate going back again (even if that means hopping on a plane cross-country).  It's a must for anyone visiting New York. Must trys: edamame dumplings, steak with brown butter, lobster eggrolls, spicy crab
Perhaps we should start w/the story of how I ended up here in the first place.  A good friend of mine who's much deeper in the pockets than I made reservations for a first date here.  Must be nice, right?He hadn't heard from her all day so us being the boys that we are, he hit me up about an hour and a half before the reservation  put me in her spot as a substitute date.  He really wanted to go anyway, so canceling the reservations wasn't an option.  In exchange for my charity, he comped the dinner  told me to order anything I wanted.  w00t!Our table wasn't immediately ready, so we ordered drinks at the lounge.  I drank the Fate all evening.  Very, very nice.  It's elderflower, pineapple,  prosecco.  Yum! :)  He drank the tranquility which is citrus vodka w/lemongrass infused oolong tea.  It must've been good b/c he stuck w/that too. As for the meal---everything tasted good.  I don't even need to go into a thorough description of every dish; I'll just tell you now it's good, and you will like it. Me: Crispy Duck Spring RollsSweet  Sour Chicken Him: Hunan Beef Bao BunsMao Poe TofuDessertOrange Scented BeignetsCouldn't touch that Mao Poe Tofu (Ko don't do pork), but I did eat a Beef Bao Bun  damn those bunz b good. Outside of the dining experience, the staff was excellent, and the decor is top notch.  The music was also very hip and I heard everything from obscure house mixes to Pete Rock  CL Smooth.  Loved it, loved it, loved it. I'd go again...under like circumstances.  Otherwise, I'll always have that day where I +1'd my way into a fine dining experience.
